# NIST SP 800-53 5.2.0 — Access Control Solution Plan — 2026-06-17 10:36

**Standard:** NIST SP 800-53 5.2.0
**Family:** AC — Access Control
**Generated:** 2026-06-17 11:49 UTC
**Model:** N/A

## Executive Summary

- **Total Solutions:** 131
- **Manual (Policy/Process/Documentation):** 6
- **Software (Development/Configuration):** 125
- **Critical:** 124
- **High:** 7
- **Medium:** 0
- **Low:** 0

## Application / System Context

Enterprise business application operating within a security-conscious environment that processes, stores, and transmits confidential organizational information. The application supports critical business functions and is considered important to the organization's operational, regulatory, and security objectives.

Technology Environment:
- Enterprise-managed application hosted within approved infrastructure environments (cloud, on-premises, hybrid, or SaaS)
- Integrated with enterprise identity, access management, monitoring, logging, backup, and security services
- May include web, mobile, API, client-server, microservices, or traditional enterprise application architectures
- Utilizes enterprise-approved databases, storage platforms, and network services

Architecture:
- Multi-tier architecture with logical separation between presentation, application, data, and administrative functions
- Production, test, development, and disaster recovery environments are segregated and managed separately
- Security controls are implemented using defense-in-depth principles across infrastructure, applications, networks, identities, and data
- Administrative functions are isolated from standard user activities where feasible

Users and Access:
- Users include employees, contractors, partners, service accounts, administrators, and privileged operators
- Authentication is integrated with centralized enterprise identity services
- Authorization is governed through role-based and least-privilege access models
- Privileged access is restricted, monitored, approved, and periodically reviewed
- Access to data and functionality is granted based on business need, job responsibilities, and data sensitivity

Data Classification and Sensitivity:
- The application may store, process, or transmit confidential, sensitive, proprietary, regulated, or business-critical information
- Information assets are classified according to enterprise data classification standards
- Data may include business records, customer information, employee information, financial data, operational data, intellectual property, or regulated information
- Data confidentiality, integrity, and availability requirements are considered high

Security Requirements:
- The application must comply with organizational security policies, standards, and governance requirements
- Security is incorporated throughout the system lifecycle, including design, development, testing, deployment, operation, and decommissioning
- Strong authentication, authorization, encryption, logging, monitoring, vulnerability management, and incident response capabilities are required
- Security controls are implemented according to risk assessments and regulatory obligations
- Secure configuration baselines are established and maintained
- Security events and administrative activities are logged, monitored, and retained according to enterprise requirements

Integration Points:
- Enterprise identity and access management services
- Security information and event management (SIEM) platforms
- Monitoring and observability platforms
- Backup and recovery services
- Enterprise databases, APIs, messaging systems, and shared services
- Third-party and vendor-managed systems where business requirements necessitate integration

Operational Environment:
- Managed by designated business, application, infrastructure, and security teams
- Formal change management, configuration management, and release management processes are followed
- Systems are subject to vulnerability scanning, patch management, security assessments, and periodic audits
- Business continuity, disaster recovery, and incident response processes are established and tested
- Security responsibilities are shared among business owners, application owners, administrators, developers, and cybersecurity personnel

Compliance and Governance:
- The application must satisfy applicable regulatory, contractual, legal, privacy, and organizational requirements
- Controls should align with recognized security frameworks and standards, including NIST SP 800-53, NIST Cybersecurity Framework, ISO 27001, CIS Controls, SOC 2, and other applicable requirements
- Control implementations should be scalable, risk-based, auditable, and suitable for enterprise-wide adoption
- Solutions should favor centralized enterprise capabilities, standardization, automation, and repeatable governance processes wherever possible

Assumptions for Compliance Planning:
- Confidentiality, integrity, and availability are all important objectives
- The organization maintains centralized security services and governance functions
- Enterprise security policies and standards take precedence over application-specific implementations
- Controls should be written to accommodate a broad range of technologies and deployment models while maintaining compliance with the selected framework
- Recommendations should emphasize sustainable operational processes, measurable control effectiveness, and audit-ready evidence generation

## Solutions by Control

### ac-1 — Policy and Procedures (Control)

#### CISO-owned Access Control Policy & Procedures with review triggers

- **Category:** Manual
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Days
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Create and maintain an organization-level **Access Control Policy** and supporting **Access Control Procedures** that define how the organization implements access control across systems (including the application context), and ensure they are **owned by the CISO**, **disseminated to defined roles**, and **reviewed/updated on a defined cadence and event triggers**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-1 Policy and Procedures** requires that access control policy and procedures exist and address the AC family controls implemented within the organization. The guidance further requires that the policy/procedures be consistent with the organization’s risk management strategy, that **security and privacy programs collaborate**, and that updates occur based on **scheduled reviews** and **events** (e.g., incidents, audit findings, major changes, legal/regulatory changes). Simply restating controls is not sufficient; the documents must be organizational policy/procedure describing implementation.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Establish document ownership and governance**
   - Assign the **CISO** as the official responsible for managing the access control policy and procedures.
   - Create a lightweight RACI covering: Security (policy lead), Privacy (review/consent where applicable), IAM (procedure input), System Owners/OT/ICS Engineers (procedure input), Legal/Compliance (law/reg change input), and Audit/Internal Compliance (verification).

2. **Develop the Access Control Policy (organization-level)**
   - Publish a single organization-level policy (or a small set of policies if needed) with explicit sections for:
     - **Purpose** and **scope** (covers all personnel, contractors, privileged users; and the application environments: prod/test/DR).
     - **What is included/excluded** (avoid “restating controls” only; describe organizational rules and decision points).
     - **Roles and responsibilities** (including who approves access, who maintains IAM integrations, who owns exceptions).
     - **Management commitment** and coordination between security and privacy programs.
     - **Compliance assurance** approach (how adherence is checked—e.g., access review completion, audit evidence expectations).
     - **Consistency with applicable laws/regulations and organizational standards** (explicitly reference the governing sources used).

3. **Develop Access Control Procedures (how the policy is implemented)**
   - Create procedure documents (or procedure chapters) that provide implementation steps for the roles defined in the organization-defined parameters, at minimum covering:
     - Access request/approval workflow (including privileged access handling).
     - Identity lifecycle handling (joiner/mover/leaver) and contractor access.
     - Periodic access review execution expectations (who performs, frequency, and evidence to retain).
     - Exception handling (how exceptions are requested, approved, time-bounded, and reviewed).
     - Emergency/temporary access process (and required follow-up).
   - Ensure procedures are written for the dissemination audiences:
     - **System owners, network administrators, OT/ICS engineers, and IAM administrators**.

4. **Disseminate with evidenceable distribution**
   - Disseminate the **policy** to **all personnel, contractors, and privileged users**.
   - Disseminate the **procedures** to **system owners, network administrators, OT/ICS engineers, and IAM administrators**.
   - Use a controlled repository (e.g., document management system) and record dissemination/acknowledgement (e.g., LMS attestation or repository read/ack logs).

5. **Set review/update cadence and event triggers**
   - Policy review/update: **annually and after any material change**.
   - Policy update events: **after security incidents or breaches, audit findings, major organizational changes, or changes to applicable laws/regulations**.
   - Procedures review/update: **annually and after any material change**.
   - Procedures update events: **after security incidents or breaches, audit findings, major system changes, or changes to applicable laws/regulations**.
   - Implement a documented change-control workflow that triggers review when any event occurs.

6. **Ensure security + privacy collaboration is documented**
   - Capture privacy review/approval (or documented rationale for when privacy review is not applicable) in the policy/procedure approval workflow.

## WHO
- **CISO**: policy/procedure owner and final approver.
- **Security Program (IAM/Security Engineering)**: drafts policy and procedure content.
- **Privacy Program**: reviews policy/procedures for privacy impacts.
- **IAM Administrators**: provide procedure implementation details and evidence expectations.
- **System Owners / Network Admins / OT-ICS Engineers**: review procedure steps relevant to their responsibilities.
- **Legal/Compliance & Internal Audit**: review for regulatory alignment and auditability.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. An **Access Control Policy** document exists in a controlled repository with:
   - Named **CISO** as official owner/manager.
   - Defined dissemination scope including **all personnel, contractors, and privileged users**.
   - Explicit review cadence: **annual** and **after material change**.
   - Explicit event triggers: **incidents/breaches, audit findings, major organizational changes, legal/reg changes**.
   - Documented collaboration evidence with **privacy** (approval record or documented rationale).
2. An **Access Control Procedures** document set exists with:
   - Defined dissemination audiences: **system owners, network administrators, OT/ICS engineers, IAM administrators**.
   - Explicit review cadence: **annual** and **after material change**.
   - Explicit event triggers: **incidents/breaches, audit findings, major system changes, legal/reg changes**.
   - Procedures describe implementation steps (not only control restatement).
3. Evidence of dissemination exists (e.g., attestation/read-ack logs) for the defined audiences.
4. The repository shows versioning and an approval history for the current policy/procedure set.


### ac-2 — Account Management (Control)

#### Enforce AC-2 account lifecycle via IAM workflow + 24h disable/notify

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Months
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an account management lifecycle for the application that:
- Allows only **individual** and **service** accounts (and prohibits **shared, group, emergency, anonymous, temporary, guest** accounts for group/role membership).
- Defines and enforces **account-specific attributes** (least privilege, access scope/systems-data, MFA requirement, and time-of-day/day-of-week restrictions).
- Requires **approval** for account creation by the **system owner** and the **senior agency information security officer**.
- Performs **create/enable/modify/disable/remove** only through a documented, ticketed, auditable IAM workflow.
- Automatically triggers **disablement within 24 hours** of defined triggers (e.g., no longer required, termination/transfer, need-to-know change).
- Notifies the **account manager** and the **system owner** within **24 hours** when accounts are no longer required, when users are terminated/transferred, and when need-to-know/usage changes.
- Performs **quarterly account reviews** with evidence.

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-2 requires organizations to control the lifecycle of system accounts by defining authorized account types and privileges, enforcing approval/oversight for account creation (with additional scrutiny for privileged/admin access), and ensuring accounts are created/modified/disabled/removed according to policy—specifically including timely disabling and notifications, and periodic review.

This solution directly implements the organization-defined parameters:
- **ac-02_odp.01**: individual and service only; prohibit shared/group/emergency/anonymous/temporary/guest.
- **ac-02_odp.02**: account-specific privileges, access scope, MFA, and time restrictions.
- **ac-02_odp.03**: approvers = system owner + senior agency information security officer.
- **ac-02_odp.04–08**: documented IAM workflow with approval/ticketing/audit logging; disable within **24 hours**; notify within **24 hours** for no-longer-required, termination/transfer, and need-to-know changes.
- **ac-02_odp.10**: quarterly account review.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define allowed/prohibited account types in the IAM integration
- Configure the application’s authorization model to accept identities only from the enterprise IdP/IAM.
- Enforce an IAM policy that **only individual and service accounts** can be used for role/group membership.
- Add guardrails: block provisioning requests that attempt to create/assign prohibited account types (shared/group/emergency/anonymous/temporary/guest) to application roles.

### 2) Create an account attribute/entitlement template per role
For each application role (and for each service account role), define required attributes:
- **Least privilege** mapping to application functions and data scopes.
- **Access scope**: which systems/data the role can access.
- **MFA requirement**: require MFA for interactive user accounts; enforce appropriate auth method for service accounts per enterprise standard.
- **Time-of-day/day-of-week restrictions** where applicable (implement via conditional access rules or application-side enforcement if conditional access is not sufficient).

### 3) Implement an approval-backed, auditable IAM workflow
- Integrate the application’s account lifecycle actions with the organization’s ticketing system (e.g., ServiceNow/Jira) and IAM workflow.
- Require approvals for **account creation** from:
  - **System owner**
  - **Senior agency information security officer**
- Ensure every workflow step writes immutable audit evidence: requester, approvers, role/entitlement requested, justification, timestamps, and resulting account/entitlement changes.

### 4) Enforce 24-hour disablement triggers
- Subscribe to authoritative events (from HR/identity lifecycle sources) for:
  - user termination
  - transfer
  - “no longer required” determinations
  - need-to-know/usage changes
- Configure the IAM workflow to:
  - **disable** the application account/entitlements within **24 hours** of each trigger.
  - record the trigger source and timestamp in the audit log.

### 5) Enforce 24-hour notifications to account manager and system owner
- Configure automated notifications (email/ticket updates) within **24 hours** to:
  - **account manager** and **system owner** when accounts are no longer required (**ac-02_odp.06**)
  - **account manager** and **system owner** when users are terminated or transferred (**ac-02_odp.07**)
  - **account manager** and **system owner** when need-to-know/usage changes (**ac-02_odp.08**)
- Ensure notifications include: affected identity, entitlements to be disabled, trigger type, and due time.

### 6) Implement quarterly account review with evidence
- Generate a quarterly report of all application accounts and their assigned roles/entitlements.
- Route review/attestation to the designated reviewers (at minimum, align with the account manager/system owner responsibilities).
- Store review evidence (attestation results, exceptions, and remediation actions) for audit.

## WHO
- **IAM/Identity Engineer**: implement IAM policies, workflow, conditional access/time restrictions, and event-driven disablement/notifications.
- **Application Owner/System Owner**: define role-to-entitlement mappings and approve account creation requests.
- **Security/Privacy Approver (Senior agency information security officer)**: approve account creation requests requiring additional scrutiny.
- **Account Manager**: performs/attests quarterly reviews and receives notifications.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Account type enforcement**: Attempts to provision prohibited account types (shared/group/emergency/anonymous/temporary/guest) for application role/group membership are rejected and logged.
2. **Per-account attributes**: Every provisioned account has recorded entitlements including least privilege scope, MFA requirement (where applicable), and time-of-day/day-of-week restrictions (where applicable).
3. **Approval evidence**: For account creation, workflow records show approvals from both **system owner** and **senior agency information security officer**.
4. **24-hour disablement**: For each trigger event (termination/transfer/no longer required/need-to-know change), the account/entitlements are disabled within **24 hours**, with audit timestamps matching the trigger.
5. **24-hour notifications**: For each trigger event, notifications are sent within **24 hours** to the **account manager** and **system owner**.
6. **Quarterly review**: Quarterly account review reports exist for the application, including attestation/exception handling and remediation evidence.

## Notes / boundaries
- This solution assumes the organization-defined parameters are adopted for the application’s IAM integration.
- If the application currently uses shared/group authenticators, additional credential-rotation steps must be added; this solution focuses on enforcing the lifecycle and prohibited account types per the provided parameters.

### ac-2.1 — Automated System Account Management (Enhancement)

#### Event-driven system account lifecycle with email alerts & anomaly reporting

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement automated mechanisms to manage **system accounts** across the enterprise application environment, including **create, enable, modify, disable, and remove** actions, and automatically:
- **Notify account managers** when system accounts are created/enabled/modified/disabled/removed.
- **Notify account managers** when users are **terminated or transferred** (for any system-account mappings tied to those users).
- **Monitor system account usage** and **report atypical usage**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-2(1)** enhancement requires support for **automated system account management** using the organization-defined parameter **ac-02.01_odp (automated mechanisms)**, including lifecycle automation, notifications to account managers, monitoring of system account usage, and reporting of atypical usage.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the automation scope and ownership mapping
- Identify which system accounts exist for this application (e.g., service accounts for APIs, batch jobs, integration accounts, admin/ops accounts used by automation).
- Define an **authoritative account registry** (e.g., IdP/directory object, IAM system, or configuration management inventory) that records:
  - system account identifier
  - environment (prod/test/DR)
  - owning account manager(s) (email distribution list or individual)
  - lifecycle state
  - allowed automation actions

**Acceptance evidence:** a maintained mapping document/export showing each system account (or account class) and its account manager(s).

### 2) Implement automated lifecycle actions (create/enable/modify/disable/remove)
- Use **internal system functions** (per ac-02.01_odp default: internal system functions and automated email notifications) to drive lifecycle changes.
- Implement event-driven workflows that call the appropriate automation endpoints for the target systems (examples):
  - directory/IdP provisioning (SCIM/graph/LDAP automation)
  - application account provisioning (admin API / provisioning service)
  - secrets/credentials rotation hooks (where applicable)
- Ensure each lifecycle action is executed via automation with environment segregation (prod vs non-prod).

**Acceptance evidence:** configuration/workflow exports and test logs showing automated execution for all lifecycle actions (create, enable, modify, disable, remove) for at least one representative system account per environment.

### 3) Configure automated notifications to account managers for lifecycle events
- For each lifecycle event (created/enabled/modified/disabled/removed), automatically send an **email notification** to the mapped account manager(s).
- For **user termination or transfer**, ensure any system-account mappings tied to that user (e.g., delegated ownership, break-glass operator mapping, or account manager assignment changes) trigger notifications and corresponding lifecycle updates where applicable.
- Include in each notification at minimum:
  - system account identifier
  - event type
  - timestamp
  - environment
  - correlation ID referencing the automation run/audit record

**Acceptance evidence:** sample notification messages (or message logs) for each event type, with correlation IDs matching automation/audit records.

### 4) Monitor system account usage and report atypical activity
- Enable automated monitoring using enterprise logging/monitoring sources already integrated with the application environment:
  - authentication/sign-in logs for system accounts (where applicable)
  - application audit logs for system-account actions
  - host/network logs for system-account-originated activity (where applicable)
- Implement detection rules for **atypical usage** (examples of signals; tune to your environment):
  - logins from unusual geolocation/device/network segments
  - access outside approved time windows
  - sudden spikes in API calls or privileged operations
  - use of disabled accounts (should be impossible; alert if observed)
- Route alerts to a defined reporting channel and ensure account managers receive actionable notifications (email and/or ticket creation) for investigation.

**Acceptance evidence:** alert rule configuration and at least one test alert demonstrating that atypical usage is detected and reported to the correct account manager(s).

### 5) Ensure auditable records and retention for lifecycle + notifications
- Record an auditable trail that links:
  - lifecycle action (who/what automation, when, what changed)
  - notification event (message sent, recipients, timestamp)
  - usage monitoring alert (if triggered)
- Store evidence in the enterprise logging/audit system with retention aligned to organizational requirements.

**Acceptance evidence:** audit log extracts showing lifecycle event → notification correlation ID → (optional) alert record.

### 6) Document the automation configuration and responsibilities
- Document:
  - the automation workflows and triggers
  - notification templates and recipient mapping logic
  - monitoring/detection rules and escalation/response routing
  - roles/responsibilities (account manager, IAM/app owner, SOC/monitoring owner)
  - how exceptions are handled (e.g., emergency disablement)

**Acceptance evidence:** runbook/procedure and configuration inventory for the implemented automation.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **IAM/Identity Engineer**: implement lifecycle workflows and notification triggers.
- **Application Owner / AppSec**: validate provisioning targets and audit logging coverage.
- **SOC/SecOps Analyst**: tune and validate atypical usage detections and alert routing.
- **Compliance/Control Owner**: verify evidence package completeness for AC-2(1).

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. Automated workflows exist and successfully perform **create, enable, modify, disable, remove** for system accounts in at least one representative production-like environment.
2. For each lifecycle event, an **email notification** is automatically sent to the mapped account manager(s), and the notification includes a correlation ID that matches the automation/audit record.
3. When a user is **terminated or transferred** (for any relevant system-account mapping/ownership), notifications are automatically generated and corresponding lifecycle/ownership updates occur as designed.
4. Automated monitoring detects **atypical system account usage** and reports it to the correct account manager(s) (and/or SOC escalation path) with evidence of alert generation.
5. An auditable record exists linking lifecycle actions, notifications, and (when applicable) atypical usage alerts, with retention in the enterprise logging system.


### ac-2.2 — Automated Temporary and Emergency Account Management (Enhancement)

#### Automate disablement of temp/emergency accounts after 24 hours

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an automated mechanism that **disables (or revokes sign-in for) temporary and emergency accounts exactly after the configured time period** (default: **24 hours**) without requiring administrator action.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-2(2)** enhancement requires: “**Automatically {{ param ac-02.02_odp.01 }} temporary and emergency accounts after {{ param ac-02.02_odp.02 }}**.” Guidance emphasizes removal/disablement **automatically after a predefined time period rather than at the convenience of the system administrator**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the lifecycle inputs and the 24-hour rule
- Treat “temporary” and “emergency” access as **account lifecycle events** (e.g., expiring user, time-bound privileged role/group membership, or time-bound access package) rather than ad-hoc manual enablement.
- Ensure the workflow that creates/enables the account captures:
  - **Enablement timestamp** (source of truth)
  - **Account type** (temporary vs emergency)
  - **Expiry timestamp = enablement timestamp + 24 hours**

### 2) Implement automation in the centralized identity system (IdP/IGA)
- Configure the enterprise identity/access management platform to enforce expiry by:
  - **Disabling the account** (per **ac-02.02_odp.01 = disable**) at expiry time, and/or
  - **Revoking sign-in** at expiry time if the platform supports “block sign-in” as the enforcement mechanism.
- Ensure the automation is driven by the **expiry timestamp** set at creation/enablement time.

### 3) Ensure auditable evidence is generated automatically
- Enable and retain system-generated audit logs/events for:
  - Account creation/enablement for temporary/emergency access
  - The automated disablement (or sign-in revocation) event
- Provide a repeatable report/query that lists, for a given time window:
  - Account identifier
  - Account type (temporary/emergency)
  - Enablement time
  - Disablement time
  - Result/status

### 4) Validate behavior with production-like testing
- In a non-production environment (or a controlled production pilot), create at least:
  - 1 temporary account and 1 emergency account
- Confirm that both are **disabled automatically at ~24 hours** (allowing only for documented clock/logging latency).
- Confirm the audit trail shows the disablement event and timestamps.

### 5) Operationalize and monitor
- Add a monitoring/alert (or scheduled job) that flags any temporary/emergency accounts whose expiry timestamp is passed but are not yet disabled.
- Route exceptions to the appropriate IAM/security operations queue with evidence (account ID, expiry time, current status).

## WHO
- **IAM/Identity Engineer**: implement IdP/IGA lifecycle automation and expiry enforcement.
- **Security Operations / GRC Analyst**: define evidence/reporting requirements and validate auditability.
- **Application Owner (for this enterprise application)**: ensure the application relies on the centralized identity enforcement (no bypass paths) and that emergency access flows are routed through the automated workflow.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For accounts created as temporary or emergency, the system **automatically disables** them after **24 hours** (per ac-02.02_odp.02) with no manual administrator step required.
2. The disablement occurs based on an **expiry timestamp** set at enablement time (not a manual reminder).
3. Audit logs/reporting exist that show, for each tested account:
   - enablement time
   - disablement time
   - account identifier and account type
4. A test/pilot demonstrates at least one temporary and one emergency account are disabled within an acceptable timing tolerance (e.g., within minutes of 24 hours, documented).
5. Monitoring/exception handling exists to detect and remediate any accounts that remain enabled past expiry.


### ac-2.3 — Disable Accounts (Enhancement)

#### Automate account disablement within 24h for expiry/inactivity/orphans

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an automated account disablement workflow for the application that disables user accounts within **{{ param ac-02.03_odp.01 }} (default 24 hours)** when accounts are **expired, inactive for {{ param ac-02.03_odp.02 }} (default 90 days), orphaned/unlinked, or otherwise anomalous/policy-violating**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-2(3) (Enhancement) Disable Accounts** requires disabling accounts within the defined time period when accounts meet the specified conditions. The guidance emphasizes that disabling expired/inactive/anomalous accounts reduces attack surface and supports least privilege/least functionality.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define authoritative triggers and timestamps (authoritative sources)
- **Expiry/termination trigger**: Use the enterprise identity provider (IdP) and/or HR/IGA authoritative feeds that set account expiry or leaver status.
- **Orphan/unlinked trigger**: Use IGA/orphan detection signals (e.g., account not mapped to an active identity/person/entitlement owner).
- **Policy-violating/anomalous trigger**: Use the organization’s policy exception/violation records or security governance flags that identify accounts requiring disablement.
- **Inactivity trigger (90 days)**: Use IdP sign-in logs and/or application authentication telemetry to compute inactivity and identify accounts with **no successful authentication activity for {{ param ac-02.03_odp.02 }}**.

For each trigger, ensure the workflow records:
- **Trigger time** (from authoritative source timestamp)
- **Account identifier** (stable unique ID)
- **Trigger reason code** (expired / orphaned / policy-violating / inactivity)

### 2) Enforce a 24-hour disablement SLA in the workflow
- Configure the identity lifecycle workflow so that once a trigger is confirmed, the system schedules/executes disablement with an SLA of **{{ param ac-02.03_odp.01 }}**.
- If the workflow supports retries/queueing, ensure the queueing mechanism cannot exceed the SLA without generating an auditable exception record.

### 3) Disablement must be effective (close access paths)
When the workflow disables an account, the application must ensure access is actually removed by doing at least the following (based on your auth model):
- **If using federated SSO/OIDC/SAML**: rely on IdP disablement and additionally revoke/stop application sessions where applicable (e.g., invalidate refresh tokens, force re-authentication, terminate active sessions).
- **If the application maintains local sessions**: implement session invalidation keyed to the user/account status change.
- **If the application uses API tokens**: ensure tokens are revoked/blocked on disablement (e.g., token introspection checks account status).

### 4) Implement auditable evidence generation
For every disablement event, write an audit record (and forward to SIEM if available) containing:
- Trigger reason
- Trigger timestamp
- Disablement timestamp
- Workflow run ID / correlation ID
- Account ID and principal type (user/contractor/service account)
- Any exception handling details (only if disablement could not occur within SLA)

### 5) Scope the workflow to the application’s account types
- Include all account types that can authenticate to the application (employees, contractors, partners, service accounts where applicable).
- If service accounts are managed differently, ensure they are either excluded with documented justification or included via the same disablement mechanism (as applicable to the application’s authentication model).

### 6) Operationalization
- Add monitoring/alerting for accounts approaching the inactivity threshold and for any disablement events that exceed **{{ param ac-02.03_odp.01 }}**.
- Provide a monthly report (or dashboard view) listing disabled accounts with trigger reason and SLA compliance.

## WHO
- **IAM/IGA Engineer**: configure IdP/IGA lifecycle rules, inactivity detection, and SLA enforcement.
- **Application Security/Platform Engineer**: implement/verify session/token invalidation behavior on disablement and ensure audit logging.
- **SOC/Monitoring Engineer**: set up alerts and SIEM forwarding for SLA breaches and disablement events.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For test accounts marked **expired**, the application becomes inaccessible for that account within **{{ param ac-02.03_odp.01 }}** of the authoritative expiry trigger timestamp.
2. For test accounts with **no successful authentication for {{ param ac-02.03_odp.02 }}**, disablement occurs within **{{ param ac-02.03_odp.01 }}** of the inactivity trigger timestamp.
3. For test accounts flagged as **orphaned/unlinked** by IGA, disablement occurs within **{{ param ac-02.03_odp.01 }}**.
4. For test accounts flagged as **policy-violating/anomalous**, disablement occurs within **{{ param ac-02.03_odp.01 }}**.
5. For each disablement, audit evidence exists showing **trigger time → disablement time** and the **reason code**, with workflow correlation identifiers.
6. No active sessions/tokens continue to grant access after disablement (validated via an integration test: attempt access after disablement and confirm denial/forced re-authentication).

### ac-2.4 — Automated Audit Actions (Enhancement)

#### Automate audit events for account lifecycle changes to SIEM

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an automated audit pipeline that generates and forwards audit records for **account creation, modification, enabling, disabling, and removal** events, including **who/what performed the action** (actor), **which account was affected** (target), and **when** it occurred, in a **consistent format** aligned to the organization’s AU-02 audit record requirements.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-2(4)** requires the system to **automatically audit** account lifecycle actions: **creation, modification, enabling, disabling, and removal**. Guidance ties audit record definition to **AU-02** and review/analysis/reporting to **AU-06**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Identify the authoritative sources of account lifecycle events
- Enumerate all systems that create/modify/enable/disable/remove accounts that are relevant to this application’s access model (e.g., enterprise IdP/IGA, directory services, HR-driven provisioning connectors, privileged access systems).
- For each source, confirm whether it emits native audit events for the required lifecycle actions.

### 2) Configure automated event capture for all required lifecycle actions
- Enable/verify audit logging for the following event types in each authoritative source:
  - **Account created**
  - **Account modified** (attribute/role/group changes)
  - **Account enabled**
  - **Account disabled**
  - **Account removed/deleted**
- Ensure the event includes:
  - **Actor identity** (admin user, service principal, automation workflow, or system process)
  - **Target account identifier** (username/user ID)
  - **Timestamp** (with consistent time source)
  - **Action type** (created/modified/enabled/disabled/removed)
  - **Source system** (originating platform)
  - **Correlation identifiers** where available (e.g., provisioning job ID / request ID)

### 3) Normalize to the organization’s AU-02 audit record format
- Implement a log normalization/mapping layer (in the SIEM ingestion pipeline or log processing service) that converts each source’s native fields into the **organization-defined AU-02 audit record schema**.
- Enforce consistent field names and data types across sources.

### 4) Forward to centralized, tamper-evident storage
- Configure the SIEM/central logging pipeline to ingest these normalized events automatically.
- Ensure logs are written to **append-only/tamper-evident** storage and are protected from unauthorized modification.
- Validate time synchronization (e.g., NTP) across identity systems and log collectors.

### 5) Prove coverage with automated validation tests
- Create an automated test harness (runbook or CI job) that performs controlled account lifecycle actions through the normal provisioning/admin workflows and then verifies corresponding SIEM events are generated.
- For each action type (create/modify/enable/disable/remove), validate:
  - At least one matching event appears in SIEM within an acceptable time window.
  - The event contains correct **actor**, **target**, **action type**, and **timestamp**.
  - The event is mapped to the AU-02-consistent schema.

### 6) Ensure AU-06-ready review/analysis hooks exist
- Create SIEM saved searches/detections (or ensure existing ones) that support AU-06 review/analysis for account lifecycle activity.
- Route high-risk events (e.g., privileged role assignment, mass enable/disable, deletion followed by re-creation) to the existing SOC/SOAR workflow used for AU-06.

## WHO
- **System Owner / IAM Engineer**: owns configuration of identity/provisioning audit logging and normalization mappings.
- **Security Operations (SOC) / SIEM Engineer**: owns SIEM ingestion, storage integrity settings, and detection/reporting enablement.
- **Application Owner**: ensures the application’s account lifecycle integrations use the authoritative provisioning paths (not ad-hoc/manual account changes).

## Acceptance criteria (evidence to collect)
1. For each lifecycle action (**create, modify, enable, disable, remove**), there is evidence of **automatic** audit records in the SIEM.
2. Each audited event includes **actor identity**, **target account identifier**, **action type**, and **timestamp**.
3. Events are normalized to the **organization’s AU-02 audit record format** (field mapping verified with sample events/screenshots/exports).
4. Coverage is demonstrated by automated tests that perform real lifecycle actions and confirm SIEM event generation.
5. Logs are ingested into centralized storage with **tamper-evident/append-only** protections and are retrievable for the configured retention period (per AU-02).
6. AU-06 review/analysis support exists (e.g., detections/saved searches and/or SOAR routing for account lifecycle events).

### ac-2.5 — Inactivity Logout (Enhancement)

#### Expectation-based manual logout via IdP sign-out + user guidance

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** High
- **Effort:** Days
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an expectation-based **manual logout** requirement for users: when users anticipate being inactive longer than the defined period (**ac-02.05_odp**, default **15 minutes**), they must use the application/IdP **Log out/Sign out** function to end their session.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-2(5)** (Enhancement) requires: **“Require that users log out when {{ insert: param, ac-02.05_odp }}.”** Guidance clarifies this is **behavior- or policy-based** and that **automatic inactivity logout is addressed by AC-11**, so this enhancement must ensure the *user-initiated* logout behavior is clear, reliable, and auditable.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define and publish the expectation (policy + in-product text)
- Update the organization’s access control/acceptable use guidance for this application to include the exact wording:
  - **“After 15 minutes of inactivity, if you expect to be inactive longer than this period, you must log out (sign out) before stepping away.”**
- Add the same expectation to:
  - onboarding materials (security/IT onboarding checklist)
  - application help/about/security page
  - a short in-product reminder near the **Log out/Sign out** control (e.g., tooltip or footer link text)

### 2) Ensure the “Log out/Sign out” button truly terminates access
- Integrate the application’s logout action with the enterprise identity provider (IdP) so that:
  - clicking **Log out/Sign out** triggers **IdP sign-out**
  - application session cookies/tokens are invalidated server-side
  - any client-side session state is cleared
- If the app supports SSO via **OIDC/SAML**, implement the appropriate logout flow supported by the IdP (e.g., OIDC RP-initiated logout / SAML SLO) so that logout is consistent across the app and the IdP session.

### 3) Make logout auditable (evidence for compliance)
- Forward/record logout events to the SIEM/audit store with at least:
  - user identifier
  - application/resource
  - timestamp
  - event type (logout/sign-out)
  - session identifier (or correlation id)
- Ensure audit retention matches enterprise logging requirements.

### 4) Operationalize “expected inactivity” as a user-facing rule (not auto-enforcement)
- Do **not** rely on automatic inactivity timeouts to satisfy AC-2(5).
- Instead, ensure the UI/policy explicitly instructs users to log out based on **expected** inactivity beyond **ac-02.05_odp**.

## WHO
- **Security/Compliance Owner**: approves the user-facing wording and policy update for AC-2(5).
- **Application Owner / Engineering Lead**: implements logout integration and audit event emission.
- **Identity/IAM Team**: configures IdP sign-out behavior and ensures logout propagation works.
- **SOC/SIEM Admin**: validates SIEM ingestion and creates/maintains logout event dashboards for evidence.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. The application’s user-facing guidance explicitly states the **ac-02.05_odp** expectation (default: **15 minutes**) and instructs users to **log out/sign out** when they expect inactivity longer than that period.
2. When a user clicks **Log out/Sign out**, the IdP sign-out is triggered and the application session is terminated (no authenticated access remains after logout).
3. Logout events are recorded in the audit/SIEM with required fields (user, app, timestamp, event type, and session/correlation id).
4. Evidence exists (e.g., screenshots/links to help text + sample SIEM log entries) demonstrating the requirement is communicated and that logout is auditable.


### ac-2.6 — Dynamic Privilege Management (Enhancement)

#### ABAC with real-time privilege revocation and key-epoch enforcement

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Months
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement dynamic privilege management by enforcing ABAC decisions at runtime with continuous re-evaluation so that privilege changes (role/function, time-of-day, emergency/duress) take effect immediately for active sessions. Additionally, propagate encryption key-change state into the authorization context so that access tied to communications encryption keys reflects the new key state without requiring session restart.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-2(6) Dynamic Privilege Management** requires implementing **dynamic privilege management capabilities** (param **ac-02.06_odp**) that support runtime access control decisions (e.g., ABAC), **immediate revocation** without requiring users to terminate and restart sessions, **dynamic rule evaluation** (time/function/emergency), and **effects of privilege changes** including **encryption key-change propagation**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Establish an authoritative attribute model (ABAC inputs)
- Define the authoritative sources and update mechanisms for attributes used in access decisions, including:
  - **Job function/assignment/role** (from HRIS/IAM group/entitlement sources)
  - **Time-based eligibility** (work hours / shift windows)
  - **Emergency/duress flag** (from incident/response workflow or security operations system)
  - **Communications encryption key epoch/version** (from key management/orchestration system)
- Ensure attributes are available to the authorization decision point with minimal staleness.

### 2) Implement ABAC policy-as-code in a centralized authorization decision point
- Create ABAC policies (policy-as-code) that evaluate access based on the above attributes.
- Include explicit rules for:
  - Denying access when outside allowed time windows
  - Denying access when job function/assignment no longer matches
  - Rapidly removing access when emergency/duress is asserted
  - Enforcing that the request/session is authorized for the **current key epoch/version**
- Version policies and require code review/testing before deployment.

### 3) Enforce dynamic decisions during active sessions (no session restart required)
- Route application/API authorization through an authorization gateway or service that performs ABAC evaluation **per request** (preferred) or at a documented maximum decision staleness interval.
- Configure the enforcement layer so that when attributes change, subsequent requests from active sessions are denied/adjusted immediately according to the latest ABAC evaluation.
- If your architecture uses tokens/sessions, implement short-lived authorization decisions (or token introspection/refresh) so that attribute changes propagate without user re-login.

### 4) Key-change propagation into authorization context
- Integrate key-rotation events into the authorization decision context by including a **key epoch/version** claim or lookup result used by ABAC policies.
- When the communications key epoch/version changes:
  - Authorization must reflect the new epoch/version immediately (or within the documented maximum staleness).
  - Requests using the old epoch/version must be denied (or re-authorized) according to the ABAC policy.

### 5) Audit and evidence generation
- Log authorization decision events including:
  - Subject identity
  - Evaluated attributes (or attribute identifiers) relevant to the decision
  - Policy version
  - Decision outcome (permit/deny) and reason codes
  - Trigger source for dynamic changes (e.g., attribute update event, emergency flag assertion, key-epoch change)
- Ensure logs are forwarded to the enterprise SIEM and retained per organizational logging/retention requirements.

## WHO
- **Application Owner / IAM Architect**: defines attribute model and ABAC policy requirements.
- **Security Engineering (Authorization/Gateway team)**: implements the authorization decision point, enforcement configuration, and key-epoch integration.
- **Identity/IAM Operations**: ensures attribute sources publish updates reliably and securely.
- **Security Operations (SOC/IR)**: manages emergency/duress flag assertions and validates propagation.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Immediate revocation**: When a user’s job function/assignment attribute is removed or changed, an active session’s subsequent requests are denied/adjusted without requiring the user to terminate and restart the session.
2. **Time-based enforcement**: When the system time enters/exits an allowed window for the user/function, authorization outcomes change accordingly within the documented maximum decision staleness.
3. **Emergency/duress enforcement**: When the emergency/duress flag is asserted for a user or scope, authorization denies access for active sessions within the documented maximum decision staleness.
4. **Key-epoch propagation**: After a communications encryption key epoch/version change, authorization decisions reflect the new epoch/version without requiring session restart; requests tied to the old epoch/version are denied or re-authorized per policy.
5. **Auditability**: For each dynamic privilege change impact, logs show the policy version, relevant attribute values/identifiers, decision outcome, and the trigger (attribute update vs. emergency vs. key-epoch change), and are available in SIEM.


### ac-2.7 — Privileged User Accounts (Enhancement)

#### RBAC privileged roles via IdP with automated membership monitoring

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement privileged access so that privileged roles are granted only through the organization’s **role-based access scheme** and are continuously monitored for **role/attribute assignment changes**. Privileged role membership must be automatically revalidated and promptly revoked when no longer appropriate, with audit-ready evidence.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-2(7)** enhancement requires privileged access to be managed using the organization-defined privileged access scheme (parameter: **role-based access scheme**), including continuous monitoring of privileged role/attribute assignments and timely revocation when no longer appropriate.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define and implement privileged roles in the IdP (RBAC as source of truth)
- Create an explicit set of **privileged roles** in the enterprise RBAC model (e.g., Key Management Admin, Database Admin, Network Admin, Web Admin).
- Map each privileged role to **IdP groups/roles** and ensure downstream authorization (admin consoles, apps, cloud resources, databases) consumes those IdP groups/roles.
- Configure the IdP so privileged role membership is **not manually assignable** outside the governance workflow (deny direct assignment where supported).

### 2) Establish an automated privileged access lifecycle (request → approval → time-bound assignment)
- Use an identity governance capability (e.g., entitlement management) to require approval for privileged role assignment.
- Make assignments **time-bound** (JIT or expiring entitlements) so membership naturally ends unless renewed.
- Ensure the workflow captures: requester, approver(s), privileged role, justification, start/end time, and ticket/reference.

### 3) Continuously monitor privileged role membership changes
- Stream IdP audit events and group/role membership change events to the SIEM/logging platform.
- Implement detections/alerts for:
  - new privileged role membership
  - privileged role removals
  - privileged role changes (role added/removed)
  - membership changes outside expected workflow windows (e.g., off-hours or without an associated approval/ticket)
- Maintain a **system-generated privileged account list** by querying the IdP authoritative privileged groups/roles and correlating to account identifiers.

### 4) Promptly revoke when no longer appropriate
- Integrate HR lifecycle signals (joiner/mover/leaver) and/or manager role-change events to trigger entitlement review and revocation.
- Enforce automated revocation when the user is no longer eligible (e.g., termination, role transfer, contractor end date), and ensure the revocation action is recorded with timestamp and reason.

### 5) Produce audit-ready evidence for ongoing review
- Generate recurring reports (e.g., weekly automated evidence packs for SOC/IAM; monthly for high-risk roles) showing:
  - current privileged role membership (who has what)
  - membership change history (who changed, when, what changed)
  - evidence of approvals and ticket references
  - revocation events and reasons
- Retain logs/evidence per organizational retention requirements.

## WHO
- **IAM/Identity Engineer**: IdP RBAC design, group/role mapping, workflow configuration.
- **Security Operations (SOC) / SIEM Engineer**: monitoring pipelines, detections, alert routing.
- **Application/Platform Owner**: ensure downstream admin authorization consumes IdP groups/roles.
- **HR/Workforce Systems Integrations Owner**: HR event integration for revocation triggers.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For each privileged role defined in the organization’s RBAC scheme, there exists a corresponding IdP group/role and downstream systems authorize based on that mapping.
2. Privileged role membership changes occur only via the approved governance workflow (no direct manual assignment path for privileged roles, where supported).
3. A system-generated list of privileged accounts exists and is derived from IdP privileged groups/roles.
4. All privileged role membership add/remove events are logged, forwarded to the SIEM, and trigger alerts/detections for unauthorized or out-of-policy changes.
5. When a user becomes ineligible (e.g., leaver/role transfer), privileged role membership is revoked within the defined operational SLA and the revocation event is recorded with timestamp and reason.
6. Audit reports can be produced showing current privileged membership and the full change history (including approvals/ticket references) for the reporting period.

### ac-2.8 — Dynamic Account Management (Enhancement)

#### JIT dynamic service account provisioning with policy checks

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an automated “dynamic account lifecycle” capability for **in-scope system accounts** (service accounts and privileged system accounts for on-prem applications and integrations) that can **create, activate, manage (update), and deactivate** accounts **at runtime** for previously unknown integration entities, while enforcing **authorisation checks** and **least-privilege privilege changes**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-2(8)** requires: “Create, activate, manage, and deactivate {{ param, ac-02.08_odp }} dynamically.” Guidance further requires organizations to plan dynamic management by establishing **trust relationships, business rules, and mechanisms with appropriate authorities** to validate authorizations/privileges.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the in-scope dynamic account model (system design)
- Create a documented account schema for **system accounts** in scope (from **ac-02.08_odp**):
  - Account identifier format (e.g., `svc-{env}-{integrationEntityId}`)
  - Metadata required for lifecycle management (integration entity ID, environment, owner/team, requested privilege template, expiry/deactivation trigger, correlation IDs)
  - Privilege templates mapping (entity type → allowed roles/entitlements/groups)
- Define lifecycle states: `created` → `active` → `managed(updated)` → `deactivated`.

### 2) Establish an authoritative “entity registry” and trust relationship
- Maintain an **approved registry** of integration entities/partners (or entity attributes) that automation can validate against.
- Define which authority can request/approve provisioning (e.g., integration platform service + workflow approval role).
- Ensure the runtime trigger includes: `integrationEntityId`, `requestedOperation` (create/activate/update/deactivate), `requestedPrivilegeTemplate`, and `requester identity/context`.

### 3) Implement policy-as-code for privilege determination and authorization
- Implement a policy engine (or workflow rules) that, before any lifecycle action:
  - Validates the entity exists/attributes match the registry
  - Validates the requested operation is allowed for the current lifecycle state
  - Validates the requested privilege template is permitted for that entity type
  - Enforces least privilege by selecting the **minimum** privilege set from approved templates
  - Enforces approval requirements (either explicit approval reference or pre-authorized rule match)

### 4) Automate runtime provisioning across target systems
- Integrate the workflow with the target on-prem systems that actually host the accounts (e.g., directory/LDAP, application account store, database users, message broker users, etc.).
- For each lifecycle action:
  - **Create**: provision account object but keep it **disabled** until activation checks pass
  - **Activate**: enable account only after policy decision returns “allow”
  - **Manage/Update**: apply privilege changes only via the approved template mapping
  - **Deactivate**: disable account and revoke privileges (remove/strip entitlements) when deactivation triggers occur (expiry, integration disabled, entity removed)

### 5) Maintain a system-generated list of dynamic accounts (source of truth)
- Store lifecycle records in a system-of-record (e.g., IGA/workflow database) that is queryable for audit and operational use.
- Ensure the list is automatically updated on every lifecycle event.

### 6) Produce auditable lifecycle evidence for every action
- For each create/activate/manage/deactivate event, write structured audit logs that include:
  - Account identifier
  - Integration entity ID
  - Requested operation and requested privilege template
  - Policy decision outcome (allow/deny) and reason codes
  - Automation/workflow execution ID
  - Timestamp and initiating requester context
  - Privilege changes applied (before/after or equivalent)
- Forward logs to the enterprise SIEM for retention and correlation.

### 7) Operational controls and responsibilities
- Assign roles:
  - **Security/IGA owner**: maintains entity registry and privilege templates
  - **Integration platform owner**: emits runtime triggers with correct context
  - **Workflow automation**: executes lifecycle actions only after policy allow
  - **App/system owners**: validate target-system provisioning connectors and deactivation behavior

## WHO
- **IGA/Security Architect**: defines account model, privilege templates, and policy-as-code rules
- **Integration Platform Owner**: implements runtime trigger emission and connector wiring
- **Security Operations / SIEM Engineer**: ensures audit log forwarding, retention, and alerting
- **App/System Owners**: validate least-privilege application of changes in each target system

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. When a new integration entity is encountered at runtime, the system **creates and activates** an in-scope system account **only after** policy authorization returns allow.
2. For any denied request (unknown entity, invalid privilege template, missing approval), the system **does not create/activate** the account and records the denial reason in audit logs.
3. On deactivation triggers (expiry/integration disabled/entity removed), the system **disables the account and revokes privileges** within the defined operational SLA.
4. For every lifecycle action (create/activate/manage/deactivate), audit logs exist containing: account ID, entity ID, operation, privilege template, decision outcome, automation execution ID, and privilege change evidence.
5. The system-generated list of dynamic accounts is complete and matches the actual enabled/disabled state in target systems (validated via periodic reconciliation job or report).

### ac-2.9 — Restrictions on Use of Shared and Group Accounts (Enhancement)

#### Custodian-governed shared/group accounts with per-user traceability

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 82%

## WHAT
Implement a governance-and-technical enforcement mechanism so that **shared and group accounts are only permitted when** they:
1) have a **named custodian** assigned (custodian responsibility recorded),
2) are restricted to **approved functions** (least-privilege/allow-listed actions), and
3) provide **individual accountability** via **unique user-to-account mapping** (or compensating controls that provide equivalent traceability).

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-2(9)** (Enhancement) requires: *“Only permit the use of shared and group accounts that meet {{ insert: param, ac-02.09_odp }}.”* The guidance highlights the **increased risk due to lack of accountability** with shared/group accounts. The organization-defined parameter for **ac-02.09_odp (conditions)** specifies that shared/group accounts are permitted only when a **named custodian is assigned**, **access is limited to approved functions**, and **individual accountability is enforced via unique user-to-account mapping or compensating controls**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Create/maintain a Shared/Group Account Registry (source of truth)
- Implement an authoritative registry (e.g., IAM system metadata, PAM/IdP extension, or CMDB/IAM governance database) that stores for each shared/group account:
  - **Account identifier** (username/role/service identity)
  - **Custodian (named person/team)**
  - **Approved functions** (documented allow-list of what the account may do)
  - **Environment scope** (prod/test/DR)
  - **Lifecycle dates** (requested, approved, active, decommission)
- Add a workflow gate so the account cannot be enabled/used unless **custodian + approved functions** are present.

### 2) Enforce unique user-to-account mapping for accountability (technical)
Choose one accountability pattern and implement it consistently for all shared/group account usage:
- **Preferred: PAM/access broker session attribution**
  - Route access to the shared/group account through a PAM or access broker.
  - Configure the broker to record **(requesting user → shared/group account → session ID → executed actions)**.
  - Ensure the broker enforces session controls (time-bound access, command/action logging).
- **Alternative: Just-in-time delegated roles with audit linkage**
  - Keep the shared/group account itself locked down.
  - Grant users time-bound, function-equivalent roles that map to the approved functions.
  - Ensure audit logs include **user identity** and **which approved-function role/entitlement was used**.

### 3) Restrict access to approved functions (technical + configuration)
- Implement least-privilege authorization so the shared/group account (or its delegated equivalent) can only perform the **approved functions** from the registry.
- Use role-based/attribute-based access controls and, where applicable, **command allow-lists** for administrative consoles.

### 4) Ensure audit evidence supports accountability
- Configure centralized logging/SIEM so audit records include at minimum:
  - **Named user identity** (the individual who initiated the access)
  - **Shared/group account identifier**
  - **Session identifier** (or equivalent correlation ID)
  - **Action performed** (what was executed/changed)
  - **Timestamp and environment**
- Retain logs per enterprise retention requirements so investigations can reconstruct “who did what.”

### 5) Governance step: risk acceptance before enabling
- Add a policy/process step that requires the system owner/security reviewer to document the **increased risk due to reduced accountability** before enabling any shared/group account.
- This step is not purely technical; it must be captured as part of the registry approval workflow.

## WHO (roles responsible)
- **IAM/PAM Administrator**: implements registry fields, gating workflow, and technical session attribution.
- **Application Owner / System Owner**: defines and maintains the **approved functions** allow-list for each shared/group account.
- **Security/Compliance Analyst**: validates that audit evidence meets traceability expectations and that risk acceptance is documented.
- **Operations/IT Admin**: ensures operational procedures align with the enforced controls (no out-of-band use).

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1) For every shared/group account in scope, the registry shows:
   - a **named custodian** assigned, and
   - **approved functions** documented.
2) When a user accesses via the shared/group account pathway, audit logs contain a **traceable linkage** from **individual user → shared/group account/session → actions**.
3) Attempts to use a shared/group account outside the approved-function allow-list are denied (or not possible by design).
4) No shared/group account is enabled/active without passing the registry gating workflow (custodian + approved functions + accountability mechanism configured).
5) A sample investigation (e.g., “who performed action X?”) can be completed using audit logs to identify the responsible individual.


### ac-2.11 — Usage Conditions (Enhancement)

#### Enforce service-account usage windows, no interactive logons, ≤8h sessions

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement technical enforcement for the defined **usage conditions** for the defined **system accounts** so they can only be used:
- **During approved maintenance windows**
- **Without interactive logons**
- **With time-bounded sessions that never exceed 8 hours**
Additionally, ensure any violations are **audited and alerted**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-2(11) Usage Conditions (Enhancement)** requires: **“Enforce {{ ac-02.11_odp.01 }} for {{ ac-02.11_odp.02 }}.”**
The organization-defined parameters specify:
- **ac-02.11_odp.01 (circumstances/usage conditions):** “Only during approved maintenance windows; no interactive logons; use time-bounded sessions not exceeding 8 hours”
- **ac-02.11_odp.02 (system accounts):** “service accounts used for on-prem infrastructure administration and automated batch processing”

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Identify and scope the in-scope system accounts
- Build/maintain an authoritative inventory of the **service accounts** used for on-prem infrastructure administration and automated batch processing.
- Store account identifiers (username/service principal) and ownership metadata in a configuration source (e.g., IAM group mapping, CMDB export, or an internal “service-account registry”).

### 2) Define a machine-readable maintenance-window schedule
- Create a single authoritative maintenance-window source (from change management/ticketing or a controlled calendar export).
- Convert it into a machine-readable schedule including:
  - allowed days/times and timezone
  - exception handling (approved emergency windows)
  - default deny behavior when no window is active

### 3) Enforce “no interactive logons”
- Route all administrative and batch execution paths for these service accounts through an enforced access path (e.g., PAM/jump host/bastion/orchestrator) that supports policy enforcement.
- Configure the identity/access layer (or the mediated access gateway) to **deny interactive sign-in/logon** for the service-account identities.
- Ensure that interactive attempts generate auditable events.

### 4) Enforce “maintenance-window-only”
- Implement conditional authorization so that service-account usage is **allowed only when the current time falls within the approved maintenance window**.
- Use policy-as-code or scheduled policy updates so the enforcement logic is updated automatically from the maintenance-window schedule.
- Default to deny when the schedule is missing/expired.

### 5) Enforce “time-bounded sessions not exceeding 8 hours”
- Configure session lifetime controls in the enforced access path so sessions for these service accounts are capped at **8 hours**.
- If the access path issues tokens/sessions, set token/session lifetimes and re-authentication requirements so that the effective session duration cannot exceed 8 hours.
- For long-running jobs, enforce a design pattern that renews/continues work via controlled re-invocation rather than a single interactive session.

### 6) Audit, detect, and alert on violations
- Enable audit logging for:
  - service-account authentication attempts
  - interactive logon attempts (should be denied)
  - authorization decisions (allowed/denied) tied to the maintenance-window condition
  - session start/end and computed duration
- In SIEM/SOAR, create detection rules that alert when:
  - a service account is used outside an approved maintenance window
  - an interactive logon is attempted
  - a session duration exceeds 8 hours (or when the system denies/terminates at the 8-hour boundary)
- Ensure alerts include: service account identifier, timestamp, enforcement rule/condition violated, and source host/gateway.

## WHO
- **IAM/Access Management Engineer**: implement conditional access/session lifetime/no-interactive enforcement and policy-as-code automation.
- **Infrastructure/PAM Engineer**: ensure admin/batch execution is mediated through the enforced access path and that session controls are correctly applied.
- **SOC/SIEM Engineer**: implement SIEM detection rules and alert routing.
- **Change Management Owner**: maintain the authoritative maintenance-window schedule used for enforcement.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Interactive logons blocked:** For any in-scope service account, interactive logon attempts are denied and generate an audit event.
2. **Maintenance-window enforcement:** When outside an approved maintenance window, service-account usage is denied (or terminated) and an alert is generated.
3. **8-hour cap enforced:** For allowed usage, session duration is capped such that no session exceeds 8 hours; events show start/end and computed duration.
4. **Audit evidence:** Audit logs contain enough fields to identify the service account, the enforcement decision, the maintenance-window status, and session duration.
5. **Alerting:** SIEM produces alerts for each violation type (outside window, interactive attempt, >8h) with required identifiers and timestamps.


### ac-2.12 — Account Monitoring for Atypical Usage (Enhancement)

#### SIEM detection + SOAR escalation for atypical system logins

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement automated monitoring of **system accounts** for **atypical usage** defined as:
- **Logins outside normal duty hours**, and/or
- **Logins from unapproved geolocations or network segments**,
then generate an alert/report for each match and **escalate it to both**:
- the **SOC incident response lead**, and
- the **system owner**.

Also complete and maintain a **privacy risk assessment** for this monitoring and ensure the monitoring approach aligns with the organization’s **privacy program plan**.

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-2(12) enhancement requires organizations to **monitor accounts for atypical usage** (including out-of-hours and unapproved geolocation/network patterns), **record sufficient details** to identify the account and login context, and **report atypical usage** to the specified roles. The guidance also requires assessing and documenting **privacy risks** and aligning determinations with the **privacy program plan**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define detection inputs (policy/config)
- Create a configuration dataset that maps each **system account (or system-account group)** to:
  - **Normal duty hours** (time zone + schedule; include exceptions if applicable).
  - **Approved geolocations** (e.g., allowed countries/regions) and/or **approved network segments** (e.g., allowed egress IP ranges, subnets, VPN egress).
- Ensure the configuration is version-controlled and change-managed.

### 2) Ensure logging contains required context
- Configure the enterprise identity/authentication and/or access gateways that authenticate **system accounts** to emit sign-in/authentication events to the SIEM with at least:
  - account identifier (which system account)
  - timestamp
  - source IP
  - derived/available geolocation (if available)
  - network segment/VPN/egress identifier (if available)

### 3) Implement SIEM detections for atypical usage
- In the SIEM, implement two detection conditions for **system accounts**:
  1. **Out-of-hours login**: event timestamp not within the configured normal duty hours for that account/group.
  2. **Unapproved location/segment**: event source geolocation and/or network segment not in the configured approved set for that account/group.
- Record enough event detail in the alert to identify:
  - which system account was used
  - when the login occurred
  - from where (source IP and derived geolocation and/or network segment)

### 4) Alerting and escalation workflow (SOAR)
- Configure SOAR to:
  - create an incident/ticket per atypical event (or per correlated burst, if your privacy/operational model requires correlation—ensure auditability per event)
  - route/escalate to **both**:
    - **SOC incident response lead**
    - **system owner**
  - include the minimum actionable fields from the SIEM alert (account, time, source IP, geolocation/segment, detection reason).

### 5) Privacy risk assessment alignment
- Perform/maintain a **privacy impact assessment (PIA)** specifically covering atypical-usage monitoring.
- Implement privacy mitigations consistent with the organization’s **privacy program plan**, such as:
  - data minimization (store only what is needed for detection/triage)
  - access controls (restrict who can view raw/derived location/network data)
  - retention limits aligned to the PIA

### 6) Evidence and audit readiness
- Maintain evidence artifacts for auditors:
  - the atypical usage definition/config (duty hours + approved geolocations/segments)
  - SIEM detection rule configuration/version history
  - SOAR playbook/routing configuration
  - sample alert payloads showing required fields
  - PIA documentation and current privacy-plan alignment statement

## WHO
- **SOC Incident Response Lead**: receives escalations and confirms triage/response workflow.
- **System Owner**: receives escalations for the affected system account and initiates system-specific investigation.
- **Security Engineering / SIEM-SOAR Engineer**: implements SIEM detections, SOAR escalation, and evidence generation.
- **Privacy Officer / Privacy Program Owner**: owns/approves the PIA and privacy-plan alignment.

## Acceptance criteria
1. For a test system account, a login event occurring **outside configured duty hours** generates an SIEM alert and SOAR escalation to **both** the SOC incident response lead and the system owner, containing account + timestamp + source context.
2. For a test system account, a login event from an **unapproved geolocation or network segment** generates an SIEM alert and SOAR escalation to **both** roles with the required identifying details.
3. Alerts include sufficient information to identify **which account** and **login context** (time + geolocation/segment or equivalent network context).
4. A current **PIA** exists for atypical-usage monitoring and the implemented retention/access/minimization controls match the privacy program plan.
5. Evidence is available: detection rule config, SOAR routing/playbook config, and sample alert records demonstrating the required fields.

### ac-2.13 — Disable Accounts for High-risk Individuals (Enhancement)

#### 24-hour high-risk account disablement workflow with audit evidence

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an account-disablement workflow that, upon discovery of **credible evidence** that an individual poses a significant security/privacy risk, **disables the individual’s system accounts within 24 hours** and produces **audit-ready evidence** (who/when/what) showing the disablement occurred within the required timeframe.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-2(13)** (Enhancement) requires: **“Disable accounts of individuals within {{param ac-02.13_odp.01}} of discovery of {{param ac-02.13_odp.02}}.”**
- The organization must define the **time period** (default: **within 24 hours**) and the **significant risks** (default: **credible evidence of intent to cause harm via authorised access or evidence that an adversary can cause harm through the individual**).
- Guidance emphasizes **close coordination** among **system administrators, legal staff, HR managers, and authorizing officials**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the trigger and evidence criteria (policy + case schema)
- Create a structured “High-Risk Account Disablement” case/ticket type with required fields:
  - **Discovery timestamp** (time evidence was discovered)
  - **Evidence category** mapped to the defined “significant risks” (intent to cause harm via authorized access OR credible adversary can cause harm through the individual)
  - **Identified individual(s)**
  - **Identified account(s)** (IdP user, AD/local accounts, VPN/jump host accounts, PAM identities, SaaS identities)
  - **Approver/authorizing official** and approval timestamp
  - **Legal/HR coordination references** (links/IDs to supporting documentation)
- Configure the workflow so disablement cannot be executed without evidence fields being populated and approved.

### 2) Enforce the 24-hour SLA from discovery
- In the workflow engine (e.g., ServiceNow/Jira + automation/orchestration), compute **T0 = discovery timestamp**.
- Enforce:
  - **Hard deadline**: disablement action must complete by **T0 + 24 hours**.
  - **Escalation**: if not completed by T0 + 18 hours, automatically escalate to the authorizing official and system administrator on-call.

### 3) Execute disablement via identity and downstream account controls
- Implement an automation that, once approved, performs the following in order (as supported by your environment):
  - **IdP disable** (e.g., disable user in Entra ID/Okta/Azure AD) and **revoke active sessions/tokens** where supported.
  - **Conditional access deny** (block sign-in) to prevent new sessions while disablement propagates.
  - **SCIM/deprovision** for SaaS apps where available.
  - **PAM/Pricileged access revocation**: remove from privileged groups/roles and revoke active privileged sessions.
  - **Directory/local accounts**: disable in AD/local directories and any managed account stores.
- Ensure the automation records the **resulting account state** (disabled/blocked) and timestamps from each system’s audit/log source.

### 4) Produce auditable evidence for compliance
- The workflow must automatically attach or reference:
  - Ticket/case record with **discovery timestamp**, **approval timestamp**, and **completion timestamp**.
  - System-generated audit evidence (e.g., IdP audit log event IDs, AD disable event IDs, PAM session revocation IDs).
  - A “Disablement Evidence” section that clearly shows: **accounts disabled** and **within 24 hours**.

### 5) Coordination and roles (operational governance)
