- **Security Engineering / Platform Team**: implements and maintains the boundary enforcement (gateway/proxy/relay) and quarantine controls.
- **SOC/Security Operations**: monitors blocked-transfer events and manages quarantine triage.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For each identified cross-domain transfer path, traffic is routed through the enforcement boundary (no functional bypass path).
2. When a payload fails any configured validation/filtering check, the receiving domain does not receive it in any form (not stored, not queued, not delivered to inbox/share/topic, and not processed).
3. Rejected transfers generate an audit record with a correlated Transfer ID and an explicit outcome of **blocked/rejected/not delivered**, including the validation rule category.
4. If quarantine is enabled, quarantined artefacts are inaccessible from the receiving domain and only accessible to authorized security roles.
5. Automated tests (or integration test runs) demonstrate at least one failure mode per transfer type (e.g., malformed schema for APIs, disallowed file type, malware signature match) results in rejection and no delivery.


### ac-4.32 — Process Requirements for Information Transfer (Enhancement)

#### Immutable payload transfer with validated metadata and success gating

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 72%

## WHAT
Implement a dedicated information-transfer component between security-domain filter pipelines that:
1) treats the information payload as immutable (no content transformation during transfer),
2) validates the filtering metadata (instructions/labels) before it is used to control forwarding,
3) forwards the original payload only after the associated filtering stage reports successful completion for the same correlation context,
4) performs the handoff with minimal, assurance-friendly logic and produces audit evidence.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 AC-4(32) (Enhancement) requires that when transferring information between different security domains, the process that transfers information between filter pipelines has **minimum complexity and functionality to provide assurance that the processes operate correctly**. The guidance emphasizes that the processes transferring information between filter pipelines have **minimum complexity and functionality** to provide assurance they operate correctly.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define a strict transfer contract (payload vs. control-plane metadata)
- Represent the message as:
  - **Payload**: opaque bytes (or immutable object) that must be forwarded byte-for-byte.
  - **Metadata**: a separate structure containing at minimum:
    - correlation identifier (to bind payload to filtering outcome)
    - filter policy identifier/version (or equivalent)
    - destination pipeline identifier (or equivalent)
- Document the contract in a version-controlled spec.

### 2) Implement a small “Transfer Gate” service (minimal logic)
- Create a single-purpose component (microservice/workflow step) responsible only for:
  - metadata validation,
  - waiting for filtering completion,
  - byte-for-byte forwarding,
  - audit logging.
- Avoid embedding business logic, transformations, or additional filtering in this component.

### 3) Validate filtering metadata before any forwarding decision
- Enforce strict schema validation (types, required fields, length limits, allowed values).
- Ensure metadata integrity/trust:
  - accept metadata only from trusted sources (e.g., signed metadata, or metadata derived from a trusted policy reference already established in the system),
  - reject unsigned/untrusted metadata.
- Enforce correlation:
  - correlation ID in metadata must match the payload’s processing context (e.g., request ID / message ID stored in the transfer gate state).

### 4) Success gating: forward only after filtering completes successfully
- Integrate with the filtering stage using an explicit completion signal/event/response that includes the same correlation identifier.
- Transfer Gate behavior:
  - on metadata validation failure: do not forward; record failure.
  - on filtering completion success: forward the original payload unchanged.
  - on filtering completion failure/timeout: do not forward; record failure and trigger defined handling (e.g., quarantine/retry per existing operational procedures).

### 5) Enforce byte-for-byte pass-through
- Ensure the transfer gate does not:
  - normalize/transform encoding,
  - redact,
  - re-serialize JSON/XML,
  - compress/decompress,
  - alter headers/body content.
- If transport framing is required, keep framing outside the payload and forward the payload bytes exactly as received.

### 6) Produce audit evidence for assurance
For each transfer attempt, write an audit record containing at least:
- metadata validation result (pass/fail, reason codes)
- correlation ID
- filtering completion status (success/failure/timeout)
- destination handoff timestamp and destination identifier
- payload immutability evidence (e.g., hash of payload bytes computed at receipt and re-checked at forwarding, without altering payload)

### 7) Keep complexity minimal and testable
- Limit Transfer Gate responsibilities to the four functions above.
- Use configuration-driven allowlists for destination mappings and policy IDs (no ad-hoc logic).
- Add automated tests that verify:
  - forwarding never occurs before success signal,
  - forwarding never occurs on metadata validation failure,
  - payload bytes are unchanged.

## WHO
- **Software engineer / platform engineer**: implement Transfer Gate service, metadata schema validation, correlation binding, and audit logging.
- **Security architect**: define the transfer contract, metadata trust model, and assurance evidence requirements.
- **QA / security testing**: implement automated tests and negative test cases (failure/timeout/correlation mismatch).
- **Operations/SOC**: define alerting/monitoring for “forward without success” and repeated failures.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1) **No content alteration**: For a set of test payloads, the destination receives byte-for-byte identical payloads (verified by hash comparison).
2) **Metadata validation enforced**: If metadata schema/trust/correlation checks fail, the destination pipeline receives no payload.
3) **Success gating enforced**: If the filtering stage reports failure or timeout for a correlation ID, the destination receives no payload.
4) **Correlation correctness**: A filtering success event for correlation ID A cannot cause forwarding for payload/metadata associated with correlation ID B.
5) **Audit evidence present**: Each transfer attempt generates an audit record with metadata validation result, filtering completion status, correlation ID, and destination handoff details.
6) **Minimal transfer logic**: Transfer Gate contains no business transformation/filtering logic beyond validation, gating, pass-through, and audit logging (reviewable in code/design docs).

### ac-5 — Separation of Duties (Control)

#### Enforce separation of duties for privileged admin, policy change, audit approval

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement and enforce separation of duties (SoD) so that **no single individual** can both (1) administer privileged access, (2) perform/approve **security policy or role changes** (where applicable), and (3) **review and approve audit log evidence**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-5 Separation of Duties** requires dividing mission/business and support functions among different individuals/roles, conducting system support functions with different individuals, and ensuring **security personnel who administer access control functions do not also administer audit functions**. The guidance further states SoD is enforced through **AC-2** (account management), **AC-3** (access enforcement), and identity management activities in **IA-2, IA-4, IA-12**. The organization-defined parameter **ac-05_odp** requires that **duties of individuals requiring separation are defined**, including: **privileged access administration, security policy/role changes, and audit log review/approval duties**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Create an SoD duty matrix for the application’s full scope
- Produce a single, authoritative **SoD matrix** covering all in-scope environments for this application (prod/test/DR) and all relevant components (app admin, infrastructure admin, DB admin, IAM admin, logging/SIEM admin).
- Define three duty types per **ac-05_odp**:
  1. **Privileged access administration** (e.g., granting/approving privileged entitlements, managing privileged accounts, PAM vault/admin actions).
  2. **Security policy/role changes** (e.g., changes to authorization roles/groups, security configuration baselines, RBAC mappings, access policy rules).
  3. **Audit log review/approval** (e.g., reviewing audit evidence and formally approving that reviews occurred).
- Define explicit **“no-overlap” rules** (at minimum: privileged access administration ≠ audit log review/approval; and privileged access administration ≠ policy/role change duties where your organization defines that as required).
- Define **exception handling**: who can approve an exception, required compensating controls, time limits, and mandatory ticketing.

### 2) Implement technical enforcement using identity/PAM role design
- Create distinct identity groups/roles (or equivalent entitlements) aligned to the SoD matrix:
  - `APP_PRIV_ADMIN` (privileged access administration)
  - `APP_POLICY_ROLE_CHANGER` and/or `APP_POLICY_ROLE_APPROVER` (policy/role change duties)
  - `APP_AUDIT_REVIEWER` (audit log review)
  - `APP_AUDIT_APPROVER` (audit log approval)
- Configure your identity platform and privileged access tooling so that:
  - Members of `APP_PRIV_ADMIN` **cannot** be members of `APP_AUDIT_REVIEWER` or `APP_AUDIT_APPROVER`.
  - Members of `APP_POLICY_ROLE_CHANGER`/`APP_POLICY_ROLE_APPROVER` are separated from `APP_AUDIT_REVIEWER`/`APP_AUDIT_APPROVER` according to your SoD matrix.
- Enforce separation at the authorization layer (RBAC/ABAC) for:
  - Admin consoles (application admin, DB admin, infrastructure admin)
  - PAM operations (vault/admin actions)
  - SIEM/log management permissions needed to perform review/approval vs those needed to alter logging configuration.

### 3) Route audit log review/approval through a distinct workflow
- Implement an approval workflow (e.g., ticketing/GRC workflow) where:
  - The reviewer identity is captured.
  - The approver identity is captured.
  - Evidence links to the specific audit log queries/dashboards are recorded.
- Ensure the workflow permissions prevent privileged access administrators from approving their own audit evidence.

### 4) Apply the SoD rules across environments and components
- Replicate the same SoD group/role model for prod, test, and DR.
- Ensure service accounts used for admin automation are mapped to the correct duty type and are not granted audit-approval capabilities.

### 5) Produce audit-ready evidence and recurring verification
- Maintain evidence artifacts:
  - SoD matrix (approved version)
  - Identity group/role assignments and enforcement screenshots/config exports
  - Workflow records showing reviewer/approver identities and timestamps
  - Exception tickets (if any) with compensating controls
- Run a recurring SoD check (at least aligned to your access review cadence) that flags any user with overlapping duty memberships.

## WHO
- **Security Governance Lead / GRC Analyst**: owns the SoD matrix and exception process.
- **IAM/PAM Engineer**: implements identity/PAM role separation and enforces no-overlap rules.
- **SIEM/Monitoring Engineer**: configures SIEM permissions and ensures audit review/approval workflow is distinct.
- **Application Owner / System Owner**: validates that the duty mapping covers all relevant admin functions for the application.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. A documented SoD matrix exists that explicitly defines the three duty types from **ac-05_odp** and states the required **no-overlap** rules.
2. Identity/PAM configuration enforces that **no user** is simultaneously authorized for **privileged access administration** and **audit log review/approval** (and policy/role change duties where required by the matrix).
3. Audit log review/approval is performed via a workflow where the **reviewer/approver identities** are recorded and cannot be the same identities that perform privileged access administration.
4. The SoD enforcement is applied consistently across **prod/test/DR** for the application’s in-scope components.
5. Evidence package is available for audit: SoD matrix, current role/group membership exports, workflow approval records, and any exception tickets with compensating controls.


### ac-6 — Least Privilege (Control)

#### Enforce least-privilege via role catalog, JML workflows, and policy-as-code

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement least privilege for both users and system processes by (1) defining an authoritative role/permission catalog with justifications, (2) enforcing joiner/mover/leaver (JML) and privileged access workflows that grant only necessary permissions, (3) ensuring application/service accounts run with no higher privileges than required, and (4) keeping an auditable, current mapping of granted authorizations to roles and tasks.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-6** requires employing least privilege so that users (and processes acting on behalf of users) have only authorized access necessary for assigned organizational tasks, and that system processes operate at privilege levels no higher than necessary. The guidance also expects creation of additional roles/accounts as needed and application of least privilege across development, implementation, and operation.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Build an authoritative least-privilege role/permission catalog (access authorizations list)
- Create a role taxonomy for the application and its administrative functions (e.g., App-User, App-ReadOnly, App-Operator, App-Admin, Data-Admin, Support-Read, etc.).
- For each role/permission, record:
  - **System/component** (e.g., API endpoints, UI modules, database schemas, message topics/queues)
  - **Allowed actions** (CRUD/execute/admin operations)
  - **Business justification** (task/job function)
  - **Environment scope** (prod/test/dev) and **data sensitivity** scope
- Maintain this as the **current assigned access authorizations list** (source of truth for what should be granted).

### 2) Implement JML and privileged access workflows with approval and time-bounding
- Establish procedures for:
  - **Joiner**: HR/onboarding triggers request of the minimum role(s) required.
  - **Mover**: role changes when job function changes.
  - **Leaver**: immediate removal/disablement of access.
- For privileged roles (e.g., App-Admin, Data-Admin):
  - Require **approval** from the application/data owner.
  - Use **time-bound elevation** (JIT) rather than standing admin where feasible.
  - Log all role assignment/elevation events.
- Ensure the workflow updates both:
  - Identity provider groups/roles (for app authorization)
  - Any downstream system permissions (e.g., database roles, message broker permissions) via automated provisioning.

### 3) Enforce least privilege in the application using role-to-capability mapping
- Configure the application to authorize strictly based on the role/permission catalog:
  - Map IdP groups/claims to application roles.
  - Ensure each application endpoint/service checks authorization for the specific capability (not broad “admin” checks).
- Remove/avoid any “catch-all” permissions (e.g., generic admin grants) except where explicitly justified in the catalog.

### 4) Ensure system processes and service accounts run with least privilege
- Identify all application components that act on behalf of users (e.g., background jobs, async workers, scheduled tasks) and all service accounts.
- For each component/service account:
  - Create dedicated identities (no shared superuser credentials).
  - Grant only the minimum required permissions to required resources (e.g., only required DB schemas/tables, only required message topics/queues, only required API scopes).
  - Ensure background processes do not run with higher privileges than necessary.

### 5) Evidence and continuous alignment
- Maintain auditable records showing:
  - Current role/permission catalog and justifications
  - Current role assignments (who has what)
  - Audit logs for role changes and privileged elevations
  - Current configuration evidence that the application authorization model matches the catalog
- Perform periodic access reviews (at least for privileged roles) to confirm ongoing least privilege.

## WHO
- **Application Owner / Data Owner**: approves role definitions, justifications, and privileged access policy.
- **IAM Engineer**: implements IdP role/group mapping and automated provisioning.
- **Application Security Engineer**: ensures application authorization checks enforce least privilege.
- **Platform/DevOps Engineer**: configures service accounts and least-privilege permissions for databases, messaging, and infrastructure.
- **Security/Compliance**: validates evidence package and review cadence.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. A maintained **role/permission catalog** exists for the application, including justifications and environment scope.
2. The application enforces authorization using role-to-capability checks derived from the catalog (no broad admin fallback for standard users).
3. JML workflows are implemented so that:
   - Leavers are disabled/removed promptly
   - Movers update roles to the minimum required
   - Privileged access is approval-based and time-bounded (where feasible)
4. All service accounts/background workers are configured with dedicated identities and minimum required permissions (no shared superuser credentials; no unnecessary database/schema/message-broker privileges).
5. An audit evidence set is available showing current role assignments and logged role/elevation events for the last review period.


### ac-6.1 — Authorize Access to Security Functions (Enhancement)

#### PAM-enforced RBAC for security functions and security-relevant configs

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an authorization mechanism that restricts access to **security functions** and **security-relevant information** to only the organization-authorized roles: **System Security Officer, Security Administrator, System Administrator, System Programmer, and Privileged Access Manager**. Enforce this across the security functions used for access decisions, including **HSMs, firewalls/routers, IDS/IPS, SIEM, endpoint security agents, OS security configuration services**, and related **firmware settings** where supported.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-6(1)** enhancement requires: “Authorize access for {{ param, ac-06.01_odp.01 }} to:” security functions and security-relevant information. Guidance clarifies that security functions include establishing system accounts, configuring access authorizations, configuring audit event settings, and establishing intrusion detection parameters; and that security-relevant information includes firewall/router filtering rules, IDS/IPS parameters, SIEM audit event settings, and cryptographic key management information.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the authorization scope (explicit lists)
- Create and maintain an inventory mapping:
  - **Security functions** (ac-06.01_odp.02–04 and ac-6.1_prm_2): HSMs, firewalls/routers, IDS/IPS, SIEM, endpoint security agents, OS security configuration services, and (where feasible) secure boot/UEFI/TPM firmware management interfaces.
  - **Security-relevant information** (ac-06.01_odp.05): firewall/router ACLs/filtering rules, IDS/IPS detection parameters, SIEM audit event settings, and cryptographic key management metadata.
- For each function, define allowed actions (e.g., view vs change) and the required role(s).

### 2) Enforce role-based privileged access via PAM (broker)
- Integrate the enterprise identity provider (IdP) with a **Privileged Access Management (PAM)** system.
- Configure PAM to broker all administrative sessions to:
  - HSM management consoles/APIs
  - firewall/router management planes
  - IDS/IPS management consoles
  - SIEM administrative interfaces used to change audit-event settings
  - endpoint security agent management consoles
  - OS security configuration services used to change security settings
- Enforce:
  - **Only the five authorized roles** can obtain PAM access to these targets.
  - **Least privilege** per target/action (e.g., System Programmer may deploy certain security configuration artifacts but cannot change SIEM audit-event settings).
  - **Just-in-time elevation** and approval workflow for change actions.

### 3) Target-side enforcement (RBAC on the security functions)
- For each target system, create/enable admin accounts that are restricted to the minimum required permissions.
- Ensure configuration-change operations for the security-relevant items are only permitted for identities that PAM uses (or for PAM-issued/managed identities).
- Where the target supports it, implement RBAC/ACLs so that only the authorized roles can modify:
  - firewall/router ACLs/filtering rules
  - IDS/IPS detection parameters
  - SIEM audit event settings
  - cryptographic key management metadata

### 4) Protect and evidence authorization and changes
- Enable **session recording/command logging** for all PAM-brokered access to security functions.
- Forward logs to the SIEM and ensure SIEM audit-event settings changes are themselves restricted to authorized roles (i.e., changes to what gets audited cannot be performed by non-authorized roles).
- Maintain auditable evidence:
  - current role-to-target/action mapping
  - PAM policy configuration and approvals
  - recorded sessions and resulting configuration-change logs

### 5) Firmware/secure boot/UEFI/TPM (where supported)
- If the environment provides remote management interfaces for secure boot/UEFI/TPM configuration, route those administrative actions through PAM and restrict them to the authorized roles.
- If remote management is not supported, document the compensating process for authorization (but do not claim PAM enforcement where it cannot be technically applied).

## WHO
- **Security Administrator / System Security Officer**: owns the role-to-target/action authorization mapping and approves policy changes.
- **Privileged Access Manager (PAM) administrator**: implements PAM policies, session recording, and broker integrations.
- **System Administrators / System Programmers**: operate within the enforced RBAC boundaries for authorized actions only.
- **IAM/Identity team**: maintains IdP role assignments and conditional access for privileged roles.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For each security function in the inventory (HSM/firewall/IDS/SIEM/endpoint security/OS security configuration services), only the five authorized roles can obtain administrative access to change security-function configuration and security-relevant information.
2. Attempts by non-authorized roles to access or modify any of the following are denied and logged:
   - firewall/router ACLs/filtering rules
   - IDS/IPS detection parameters
   - SIEM audit event settings
   - cryptographic key management metadata
3. All privileged sessions to these targets are brokered through PAM and have session recording/command logging enabled.
4. Evidence exists for:
   - current authorization mapping (role → target → allowed actions)
   - PAM policy configuration
   - approval records for change actions
   - recorded sessions and resulting configuration-change logs.
5. (If technically supported) firmware/secure boot/UEFI/TPM configuration changes are also restricted to the authorized roles and logged with the same evidence standard.

### ac-6.2 — Non-privileged Access for Nonsecurity Functions (Enhancement)

#### Enforce non-privileged role for non-security app access

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement technical enforcement (via the enterprise IdP/RBAC layer and application authorization) so that when a user/role has access to **security functions or security-relevant information** (e.g., audit logs, security monitoring consoles, security configuration management), any access to **non-security functions** occurs only while the user is operating under a **non-privileged account/role** (or an equivalent non-privileged role with the same assurance).

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-6(2)** (Enhancement) requires: “Require that users of system accounts (or roles) with access to {{ ac-06.02_odp }} use non-privileged accounts or roles, when accessing nonsecurity functions.” This limits exposure when operating from within privileged accounts/roles.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define covered security functions/information (AC-6(2) scope)
- Create an authoritative inventory mapping for the application ecosystem:
  - **Covered (security functions or security-relevant information)**: at minimum include audit logs, security monitoring consoles, and security configuration management for security controls (per {{ ac-06.02_odp }} default guidance).
  - **Non-security functions**: all other business functions and general user capabilities.
- Output: a version-controlled “AC-6(2) Scope Matrix” listing each UI/API/admin capability and whether it is **security** or **non-security**.

### 2) Create a role taxonomy with explicit “privileged security” vs “non-privileged non-security”
- In the enterprise IdP/RBAC system, define:
  - **Privileged security roles** (e.g., `SecurityConsoleOperator_Priv`, `SecurityConfigAdmin_Priv`) that grant access to covered security functions/information.
  - **Non-privileged roles** for non-security access (e.g., `AppUser_NonPriv`, `AppOperator_NonPriv`).
- Define “non-privileged” as: roles that do **not** grant access to covered security functions/information.

### 3) Enforce “no privileged session reuse” for non-security access
Implement one of the following enforcement patterns (prefer centralized IdP policy):
- **Pattern A (recommended): IdP conditional authorization / entitlement gating**
  - Configure authorization rules so that when a user is assigned a privileged security role, access to **non-security applications** is denied unless the user switches to the equivalent **non-privileged role**.
  - Ensure the switch is explicit (role selection / token claim change) and auditable.
- **Pattern B: Application-side authorization guardrails**
  - In the application, add an authorization check that blocks non-security endpoints unless the caller’s token/claims indicate a **non-privileged role**.
  - Use the same role taxonomy as the IdP to avoid drift.

### 4) Ensure RBAC role switching provides equivalent assurance
For users who must access both security and non-security functions:
- Require role switching to the non-privileged role using the same identity assurance controls (e.g., same MFA strength, same device/session posture rules) and the same session management approach.
- Ensure sensitive security actions (when in privileged security roles) still require the appropriate step-up controls already used by the organization; the key is that the non-security path is not taken under privileged authorization.

### 5) Generate audit evidence for AC-6(2)
- Ensure audit logs capture:
  - User identity
  - Role/entitlement used (privileged vs non-privileged)
  - Target function/app endpoint category (security vs non-security)
  - Timestamp and session identifiers
- Centralize into SIEM and create an evidence query/report that demonstrates:
  - “Non-security access events occurred only with non-privileged roles” for users who have privileged security roles.

### 6) Operationalize with change control
- Add a requirement to change management that any new endpoint/capability added to the application must be classified in the AC-6(2) Scope Matrix and mapped to the correct role category.

## WHO
- **Application Owner / IAM Engineer**: implement IdP role taxonomy, conditional access/entitlement gating, and application authorization guards.
- **Security Architect**: define AC-6(2) scope matrix and non-privileged definition; validate equivalent assurance for role switching.
- **SOC/SIEM Analyst**: implement SIEM queries/dashboards and validate audit evidence.
- **Change Manager**: ensure endpoint classification updates are included in release/change records.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For every capability classified as **non-security** in the AC-6(2) Scope Matrix, requests are denied unless the caller token/claims indicate a **non-privileged role**.
2. For users assigned privileged security roles, attempts to access non-security functions while still in privileged roles are blocked and logged.
3. Role switching to the non-privileged role is supported and results in successful access to non-security functions without granting access to covered security functions.
4. Audit evidence exists (SIEM report) showing non-security access events include non-privileged role indicators and are attributable to the correct user/session.
5. The implementation is tested in at least one production-like environment (e.g., staging) with both privileged-security-role users and non-privileged-role users.


### ac-6.3 — Network Access to Privileged Commands (Enhancement)

#### Policy-gated remote execution of approved privileged commands

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement a controlled mechanism so that **network-based access to privileged commands** is allowed **only** for **compelling operational needs** (defined as **24x7 on-call incident response and time-critical maintenance when local access is impractical**) and ensure the **rationale is documented in the system security plan**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-6(3)** (Enhancement) requires: **Authorize network access to privileged commands only for compelling operational needs** and **document the rationale for such access in the security plan**. Guidance clarifies that **network access** means access across a network connection in lieu of local access.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the exact “privileged commands” scope (approved tooling only)
- Create an inventory per system/environment that maps:
  - **Privileged command categories** (e.g., OS admin commands, service management, database admin commands, vendor appliance admin CLIs)
  - **Approved execution method/tooling** (e.g., sudo with command allowlists, PowerShell remoting constrained endpoints, vendor CLI via approved jump host)
  - **Target hosts** and **allowed command patterns**
- Enforce that remote execution can only occur through these approved pathways (no ad-hoc remote shells).

### 2) Enforce “compelling operational needs” as a technical policy gate
- Implement a session broker / privileged access workflow (PAM/ZTNA or equivalent) that:
  - Allows privileged command execution **only when the requester is currently authorized for on-call** (e.g., on-call roster membership or time-bound entitlement).
  - Requires the requester to select/submit an **operational need justification** that matches the defined compelling need (24x7 on-call incident response and time-critical maintenance).
  - Captures an explicit **“local access impractical”** indicator (e.g., required checkbox + free-text explanation) before session start.
- Configure the broker so that the session can only run the **approved privileged commands** (command allowlists / constrained endpoints).

### 3) Ensure auditability and evidence for the security plan rationale
- Record, at minimum, the following for each network-based privileged command session:
  - Identity of requester
  - On-call entitlement basis (e.g., roster/timestamp reference)
  - Operational need justification and “local access impractical” rationale
  - Approved tool/workflow used
  - Commands executed (command-level logs where supported)
  - Session start/stop timestamps
- Retain logs per enterprise logging/retention requirements so the security plan rationale can be supported by evidence.

### 4) Update the system security plan with the required rationale
- For each system, update the **security plan** to document:
  - The defined **compelling operational needs** (24x7 on-call incident response and time-critical maintenance)
  - The condition that **local access is impractical**
  - The **approved privileged command execution methods** (what tools/endpoints are allowed)
  - How the technical policy gate enforces the authorization and how rationale is captured
- Reference the privileged access workflow and logging sources as evidence.

## WHO
- **Privileged Access/PAM Administrator**: implements the broker/workflow, command allowlists, constrained endpoints, and session logging.
- **System Owner / ISSO (Information System Security Officer)**: ensures the **system security plan** is updated with the AC-6(3) rationale and that the operational need definition matches organizational policy.
- **On-call Operations Lead**: maintains the on-call roster/entitlement inputs used by the policy gate.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Network access restriction**: Remote privileged command execution is only possible through the approved tooling/workflows; direct admin port/shell access is blocked or not permitted for privileged command execution.
2. **Operational need gate**: A privileged command session cannot start unless the requester is currently authorized for the defined **24x7 on-call** compelling operational need and provides a justification including **local access impractical**.
3. **Command allowlisting**: Only the defined privileged command set/patterns can be executed remotely; attempts outside the allowlist are denied.
4. **Security plan rationale**: The system security plan contains the documented rationale for network access to privileged commands consistent with AC-6(3) (compelling operational needs + local access impracticality) and references the implemented workflow/logging.
5. **Audit evidence**: For a test incident/maintenance scenario, logs show identity, on-call entitlement basis, operational need justification, local access impracticality rationale, approved tool used, and commands executed.

### ac-6.4 — Separate Processing Domains (Enhancement)

#### Isolate app processing domains with VM boundaries and least-privilege

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement separate processing domains for the enterprise application using virtualization-based isolation (e.g., separate VMs or VM clusters) so that user privileges can be granted within a specific domain while being restricted from other domains and from the underlying physical/host management plane.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-6(4) Enhancement: Separate Processing Domains** requires providing separate processing domains to enable finer-grained allocation of user privileges. Guidance explicitly includes using **virtualization techniques** to permit additional privileges within a **virtual machine** while restricting privileges to **other virtual machines** or to the **underlying physical machine**, using **hardware or software domain separation mechanisms**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define domain boundaries (design artifact)
- Create a domain map that assigns application functions to isolated domains, at minimum separating:
  - **Production application runtime** (e.g., web/app tier)
  - **Data tier** (e.g., database/queue services)
  - **Administrative/management functions** (e.g., admin jump host, CI/CD runners, ops tooling)
- Ensure the design states that **privileged roles are scoped per domain** (e.g., “Domain A admin” cannot administer “Domain B”).

### 2) Implement virtualization-based isolation
- Deploy each domain as a separate VM (or VM cluster) with:
  - **Hardened OS baselines** per domain
  - **No shared local admin accounts** across domains
  - **Restricted management-plane access** (hypervisor console/API) to a dedicated privileged identity group.
- Enforce that domain users cannot access the underlying host management plane (e.g., disable/limit host logins for non-host-admin identities; prevent access to hypervisor credentials/sockets).

### 3) Enforce network and protocol boundaries
- Apply virtual network segmentation so only required traffic flows exist between domains.
- Deny lateral administrative protocols by default (e.g., block cross-domain SSH/RDP/WinRM and other admin ports except where explicitly required).
- Use security groups/NSGs/firewall rules to enforce “least connectivity” between domains.

### 4) Implement least-privilege within each domain
- Configure OS/application RBAC so that:
  - Privileged actions (service management, configuration changes, database admin tasks) are granted only to roles scoped to that domain.
  - Cross-domain privilege escalation paths are removed (e.g., no shared admin tooling credentials; no domain-wide secrets usable from other domains).

### 5) Automate and continuously validate domain separation
- Use infrastructure-as-code to provision VMs, network rules, and role assignments.
- Add drift detection/continuous configuration validation to ensure domain boundaries (VM membership, firewall rules, admin role bindings) remain intact after changes.

### 6) Produce audit-ready evidence
- Enable and centralize logs for:
  - Domain access attempts (including denied cross-domain admin attempts)
  - Privilege/role changes within each domain
  - Management-plane actions (hypervisor console/API usage)
- Store evidence in the enterprise SIEM/log repository with retention aligned to organizational requirements.

## WHO
- **System Owner / Application Owner**: approves domain map and privilege scoping requirements.
- **Infrastructure/Cloud Engineer (VM/Network)**: implements VM isolation, network segmentation, and management-plane restrictions.
- **IAM Engineer**: integrates domain-scoped RBAC/privileged groups with centralized identity.
- **Security Engineer**: validates that separation prevents cross-domain/host privilege misuse and reviews evidence.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Domain separation implemented**: The application’s production runtime, data tier, and administrative functions are each deployed in separate VMs (or equivalent isolated processing domains) with documented boundaries.
2. **No cross-domain admin capability**: A user granted admin privileges in Domain A cannot perform administrative actions in Domain B (validated via test attempts and/or access logs showing denials).
3. **Host management plane restricted**: Non-host-admin identities cannot access hypervisor management interfaces; management-plane access is limited to the designated privileged identity group (validated via configuration and logs).
4. **Network boundary enforced**: Firewall/NSG rules prevent cross-domain administrative protocols by default; only explicitly required application traffic is allowed (validated via rule review and connectivity tests).
5. **Evidence available**: Centralized logs show domain access attempts, privilege/role changes, and management-plane actions with sufficient detail for audit review.
6. **Configuration remains stable**: Drift detection/continuous validation is enabled for VM membership, network rules, and admin role bindings; changes are captured in change records.

### ac-6.5 — Privileged Accounts (Enhancement)

#### Enforce privileged account restriction to Admin + ISSO roles

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Restrict **all privileged accounts** on the system (including any built-in/super-user accounts and any OS/app/admin groups that confer privileged capability) so they are usable **only** by the personnel/roles defined in **ac-06.05_odp**: **System Administrator** and **ISSO**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-6(5)** (Enhancement) requires: “Restrict privileged accounts on the system to {{ insert: param, ac-06.05_odp }}.” The intent is to prevent day-to-day users from exercising privileged functions and to ensure the restriction is enforceable.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
Implement technical enforcement and auditable configuration so privileged capability cannot be exercised by unauthorized users.

### 1) Identify every privileged account on the system
- Inventory privileged identities and privilege sources, including:
  - Built-in/super-user accounts (e.g., local “root/admin” equivalents, platform superuser accounts).
  - Any OS/application admin groups or roles that grant privileged functions.
  - Any service accounts that can perform administrative actions (if they are privileged by capability).
- Produce an “AC-6(5) privileged account inventory” that maps each privileged account to its privilege source.

### 2) Enforce role-only usability for privileged accounts
- Configure the system so privileged access is granted **only** when the authenticated user is in one of the authorized roles:
  - **System Administrator** role
  - **ISSO** role
- For each privileged account/privilege source identified in Step 1:
  - Remove/disable any standing membership for non-authorized users.
  - Ensure authentication/authorization checks for privileged actions validate membership in the authorized roles (not local user lists that can drift).

### 3) Remove or lock down built-in/super-user accounts
- If the platform supports it:
  - Disable built-in super-user accounts where feasible.
  - If not disable-able, restrict their usability so they can only be used by identities mapped to the authorized roles (e.g., via centralized identity integration and role checks).
- Ensure no interactive day-to-day use is possible by non-authorized identities.

### 4) Centralize authorization decisions via enterprise identity
- Integrate the application/host admin surfaces with the enterprise identity provider (IdP) already used by the environment.
- Implement authorization rules so privileged endpoints/actions require an authenticated principal whose role claim corresponds to **System Administrator** or **ISSO**.

### 5) Add auditability and evidence generation
- Enable logging for:
  - Privileged account usage attempts (successful and failed).
  - Privileged actions performed (admin operations).
- Forward logs to the SIEM/central logging platform.
- Maintain an auditable record that demonstrates:
  - Current privileged account inventory.
  - Current authorized role membership (System Administrator + ISSO).
  - Privileged activity tied to authenticated identities.

### 6) Operational verification (automated checks)
- Implement a periodic automated verification job (e.g., weekly) that:
  - Exports current privileged role membership.
  - Confirms no privileged accounts/privilege sources are mapped to identities outside the authorized roles.
  - Alerts on drift (new privileged accounts, unexpected group membership, or enabled built-in super-user accounts).

## WHO
- **System Owner / Application Owner**: ensures privileged surfaces are identified and mapped to authorization controls.
- **IAM/Identity Engineer**: implements/maintains role mapping in the IdP and role claims.
- **Platform/Infrastructure Engineer**: configures host/platform privileged account enforcement and disables/locks built-in super-user accounts where supported.
- **Security Analyst (or ISSO)**: reviews privileged access reports and drift alerts; validates audit evidence.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Privileged account restriction enforced:** For every privileged account/privilege source identified in the inventory, attempts by users not in **System Administrator** or **ISSO** roles to use privileged capability are denied.
2. **Built-in/super-user accounts controlled:** Built-in/super-user accounts are either disabled or cannot be used except by identities mapped to the authorized roles.
3. **No standing privileged access for non-authorized users:** There is no persistent privileged membership for users outside the authorized roles.
4. **Evidence available and current:** The system produces/retains:
   - Current privileged account inventory.
   - Current authorized role membership list.
   - Privileged activity logs showing the authenticated identity performing privileged actions.
5. **Drift detection works:** Automated verification detects and alerts on any privileged account/role mapping drift outside the authorized roles.


### ac-6.6 — Privileged Access by Non-organizational Users (Enhancement)

#### Block non-organizational users from privileged roles via IdP+PAM

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement a technical enforcement path that prevents **non-organizational users** (not employee-equivalent) from being granted or obtaining **privileged access** to the application and its administrative functions.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-6(6)** (Enhancement) requires: **“Prohibit privileged access to the system by non-organizational users.”** Guidance clarifies that organizational users include employees and individuals considered equivalent (e.g., contractors/guests) and that non-organizational users are those who are **not** granted equivalent status.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define privileged access and non-organizational status in the application’s authorization model
- In the application access control policy/config, define **privileged access** as the set of roles/permissions that allow administrative or security-relevant actions (e.g., admin console access, role/permission management, security setting changes, access to privileged endpoints, production configuration changes).
- Ensure the application consumes an identity attribute that indicates **employee-equivalent status** (e.g., `isEmployeeEquivalent=true/false`, or `employmentType` mapped to an approved set).

### 2) Enforce a hard deny at the identity layer for privileged roles
- Configure the enterprise IdP authorization/role-mapping so that **privileged groups/roles** used by the application (e.g., `App-Privileged-Admins`) are assigned **only** when the user is employee-equivalent.
- Implement **conditional access/authorization rules** that explicitly deny token issuance or role assignment when `isEmployeeEquivalent=false` (or equivalent attribute).
- Ensure the application trusts only IdP-issued claims for role membership (avoid local/manual role assignment for privileged roles).

### 3) Require privileged elevation via PAM for admin actions
- For any privileged administrative session (admin console, privileged API endpoints, configuration changes), require **PAM-mediated** access or step-up authentication.
- Configure PAM so that elevation requests are only possible for identities that meet the employee-equivalent condition (same IdP attribute), and deny elevation otherwise.

### 4) Maintain auditable evidence of enforcement
- Enable audit logging for:
  - IdP events related to privileged role assignment/denial (or token/claim issuance failures).
  - PAM elevation requests and outcomes (approved/denied).
  - Application authorization failures for privileged endpoints (e.g., “user attempted privileged action without required privileged role”).
- Forward logs to the organization SIEM and retain per enterprise log retention policy.

### 5) Operationalize with periodic reconciliation
- Establish a scheduled reconciliation job/process that compares:
  - Current IdP population for employee-equivalent status.
  - Current privileged role/group membership used by the application.
- Any mismatch triggers an alert and immediate remediation (remove privileged role bindings for non-organizational users).

## WHO
- **IAM/Identity Engineer**: IdP conditional access/role mapping configuration and claim/attribute design.
- **PAM Administrator**: PAM integration, step-up/elevation enforcement, and PAM policy configuration.
- **Application Security/Platform Engineer**: Application authorization mapping to IdP claims; privileged endpoint protection.
- **Security Operations (SOC)**: SIEM log validation, alert tuning, and periodic review of privileged access denials.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. A test user with `isEmployeeEquivalent=false` (non-organizational) cannot obtain privileged access:
   - Cannot receive privileged role claims/tokens from the IdP for the application.
   - Cannot successfully access privileged admin endpoints (authorization denied).
2. Any attempt by a non-organizational user to request privileged elevation is denied by PAM and recorded in logs.
3. Audit evidence exists in SIEM for:
   - Privileged role assignment/denial (IdP).
   - PAM elevation request outcomes.
   - Application privileged authorization failures.
4. Reconciliation detects and reports any privileged role membership that does not match employee-equivalent status, and remediation removes privileged access within the defined operational response time.


### ac-6.7 — Review of User Privileges (Enhancement)

#### Automate 90-day privileged access recertification with evidence

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an automated, recurring review (recertification) of **assigned user privileges** for the in-scope categories: **privileged users, system administrators, and service accounts with elevated access**, at a cadence of **at least every 90 days**. Each review must **revalidate the ongoing need** for each privilege and **record outcomes** (including rationale) and **promptly remove or reassign** privileges when the need cannot be revalidated.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-6(7) Enhancement: Review of User Privileges** requires that the organization periodically review assigned user privileges to determine whether the rationale for assignment remains valid, and if it cannot be revalidated, take appropriate corrective actions. The organization-defined parameters specify:
- **frequency**: review at least **every 90 days** (ac-06.07_odp.01)
- **roles and classes**: include **privileged users, system administrators, and service accounts with elevated access** (ac-06.07_odp.02)

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the in-scope privilege set (authoritative sources)
- In the enterprise Identity & Access Management (IAM) / Identity Governance tool, define scope using authoritative mappings to:
  - privileged user groups/roles
  - system administrator roles
  - service accounts tagged/classified as **elevated**
- Ensure the scope includes **system-generated roles/classes** by mapping them to identity constructs (roles/groups/entitlements) used by the IAM platform.

### 2) Create a 90-day recertification campaign
- Configure an automated campaign that runs **every 90 days** (default user value) and targets the in-scope privilege set.
- For each entitlement/privilege assignment, require the reviewer to:
  - confirm whether the privilege is still required for current mission/business needs
  - provide a **mandatory rationale** (text field) tied to the system/app and operational justification
  - select an outcome: **Keep** vs **Remove/Reduce**

### 3) Enforce corrective action on “Remove/Reduce”
- If reviewer selects **Remove/Reduce** (or rationale is missing/invalid per policy), trigger one of the following based on your enterprise change model:
  - **Automated entitlement revocation** (preferred where safe and already approved by policy), or
  - **Change ticket workflow** with an approval gate and a defined SLA for execution.
- Ensure the audit record captures the entitlement delta (what changed) and the actor/timestamp.

### 4) Evidence generation and retention
- Configure the IAM tool to retain, per campaign cycle:
  - list of reviewed users/service accounts and privileges
  - reviewer identity and review timestamp
  - reviewer decision (Keep vs Remove/Reduce)
  - mandatory rationale text
  - evidence of corrective actions taken (revocation/change ticket outcome)
- Export evidence packs for audit (e.g., campaign report + entitlement change logs) and store them in the organization’s approved evidence repository.

### 5) Assign responsibilities and escalation
- Define reviewer assignment rules (e.g., system/app owner or delegated business owner) and require Information Security involvement for privileged access governance.
- Add escalation for non-responses (e.g., reminder schedule and escalation to security/app governance owner) so the review completes within the 90-day window.

### 6) Integrate with provisioning/deprovisioning
- Ensure the recertification outcomes feed directly into the access provisioning system so that privilege removals/reassignments are applied promptly and consistently.

## WHO
- **Identity Governance/IAM Engineer**: implement campaign configuration, scope mappings, automation, and evidence exports.
- **Application/System Owner (Reviewer)**: attest to ongoing need and provide rationale.
- **Information Security (Approver/Overseer)**: define governance rules, validate reviewer assignment model, and monitor corrective action SLAs.
- **Change Management Owner (if ticket-based)**: ensure corrective actions are executed under approved change processes.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. A recertification campaign runs **at least every 90 days** for all in-scope categories: **privileged users, system administrators, and elevated service accounts**.
2. For each reviewed privilege assignment, the reviewer must provide a **recorded decision** and **mandatory rationale**.
3. For any privilege marked **Remove/Reduce**, the system either:
   - revokes/reduces the entitlement automatically within the defined SLA, or
   - creates an approved change request and completes the corrective action within the defined SLA.
4. Each campaign cycle produces an **audit-ready evidence pack** containing reviewer decisions, rationale, and entitlement change outcomes.
5. Evidence demonstrates that the review revalidates **ongoing need** (not only that a review occurred).


### ac-6.8 — Privilege Levels for Code Execution (Enhancement)

#### Block unsigned/unapproved elevated execution via endpoint app control

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement a technical enforcement mechanism on managed endpoints (and any admin-capable hosts) that prevents execution of the prohibited software category—**all unsigned or unapproved scripts, binaries, and installers (including PowerShell, batch, and MSI)**—from ever running with **higher privilege than the user who launched it**, even when launched from elevated prompts.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-6(8)** (Enhancement) requires: “Prevent the following software from executing at higher privilege levels than users executing the software: {{ insert: param, ac-06.08_odp }}.” The organization-defined parameter **ac-06.08_odp** defines the prohibited software as: “all unsigned or unapproved scripts, binaries, and installers (including PowerShell, batch, and MSI) executed via elevated prompts.”

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Create/maintain an authoritative prohibited/approved execution catalogue**
   - Define “approved” as items that are **signed by an approved publisher** and/or **explicitly allowlisted** (hash/signature/certificate + version) in a central configuration store.
   - Define “prohibited” as anything in the ac-06.08_odp scope that is **unsigned or not approved**.
   - Include at minimum: PowerShell scripts, batch files, executables, and MSI installers.

2. **Configure endpoint application control in deny-by-default mode**
   - Enable application control policies that **block execution** of prohibited items.
   - Ensure enforcement applies regardless of token elevation (i.e., do not allow “elevated prompt” to bypass the policy).
   - Where the platform supports it, enforce rules based on **publisher/signature validation** and/or **hash allowlisting**.

3. **Prevent privilege “escape” patterns for allowed admin workflows**
   - For legitimate administrative tasks, ensure users do not gain higher privileges by launching prohibited content from elevated contexts.
   - Route admin actions through **approved admin tooling/workflows** (e.g., signed management agents/scripts) that are included in the approved catalogue.

4. **Centralize and retain audit evidence**
   - Forward application control events to SIEM/logging with fields sufficient to prove the enforcement outcome (e.g., user, process path/hash/signature status, elevation context, block reason).
   - Retain logs per enterprise retention requirements.

5. **Operationalize change control**
   - Treat updates to the approved/prohibited catalogue and application control policy as controlled changes (versioned, reviewed, and deployed via standard configuration management).

6. **Validate with targeted tests**
   - Test cases must include: launching unsigned/unapproved PowerShell, batch, and MSI from an elevated prompt.
   - Expected result: execution is blocked or fails such that it cannot run with higher privilege than the launching user.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Endpoint Security Engineering / IAM & Endpoint Admin**: implement and maintain application control policies and the approved/prohibited catalogue.
- **Information Security (review/approval)**: approve the catalogue criteria (what counts as “approved”) and review policy changes.
- **SOC/SIEM Operations**: ensure logs/events are ingested and alerts/reporting are available for blocked elevated execution attempts.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For each prohibited category in **ac-06.08_odp** (unsigned/unapproved PowerShell, batch, binaries, MSI), attempts to execute from an elevated prompt are **blocked** (or fail) and do **not** result in higher-privilege execution.
2. Application control policy is **deny-by-default** for the prohibited categories and is enforced consistently across managed endpoints.
3. Audit records exist for blocked attempts showing at least: **timestamp, user, elevated context indicator (if available), executable/script/installer identity (path/hash/signature status), and block reason**.
4. Approved catalogue entries are versioned and changes are deployed through controlled configuration management.
5. Test evidence demonstrates that prohibited items cannot gain higher privileges than the launching user under elevated prompts.

### ac-6.9 — Log Use of Privileged Functions (Enhancement)

#### Audit and centralize privileged-function execution events

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement reliable audit logging for the execution of **defined privileged functions** and ensure those events are **centralized, reviewable, and retained**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-6(9) Enhancement** requires: **"Log the execution of privileged functions."** The guidance emphasizes that misuse of privileged functions (by authorized users, insiders, or compromised accounts) is a serious concern and that logging/analyzing privileged-function use helps detect and mitigate misuse.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the privileged-function scope (per system)
- Create and maintain a **Privileged Functions Register** for this application/system that lists:
  - Each privileged function (e.g., admin console actions, role/permission changes, service start/stop, configuration changes, key/certificate operations, database admin commands, IAM role assignments, policy changes, etc.).
  - The **authoritative event source(s)** that can record execution (OS audit, application audit, database audit, cloud control audit, etc.).
  - The **event type(s)/fields** that will be used to represent “execution” (event name/ID, actor identity, target resource, timestamp, success/failure, session/trace ID).
- Ensure the register is version-controlled and reviewed during change management.

### 2) Enable native auditing for each privileged function
- For each privileged function in the register, enable the corresponding **native audit mechanism** in the relevant layer:
  - **OS/host**: enable OS audit policies (e.g., Windows Security Auditing / Linux auditd) for the specific privileged actions.
  - **Application**: enable application-level audit logging for admin/privileged endpoints and operations.
  - **Database/IAM/Cloud**: enable provider-native audit logs for admin actions and privileged API calls.
- Configure audit settings so that privileged-function events are **actually generated** (not just “available” in logs).

### 3) Normalize and forward to a central SIEM/log platform
- Implement a log pipeline that:
  - Forwards privileged-function audit events to the enterprise SIEM/log platform.
  - Normalizes key fields (actor, privilege function name, target, timestamp, environment, outcome).
  - Preserves original event identifiers and raw payload (for audit evidence).
- Use authenticated transport and restrict access to the log platform to authorized roles.

### 4) Ensure tamper-evident retention and auditability
- Configure retention for privileged-function logs according to organizational incident response/audit requirements (at minimum: ensure logs remain available for later review).
- Ensure audit logs are protected from unauthorized modification/deletion (e.g., append-only storage patterns where supported; least-privilege access; alert on log pipeline failures).

### 5) Create an auditable mapping and validation procedure
- Produce an **Audited-Events Mapping** document that maps:
  - Privileged function → event source → event type(s)/IDs → required fields.
- Perform a validation test for each privileged function:
  - Execute the privileged function in a test environment.
  - Confirm the corresponding event appears in the SIEM with correct actor identity, target, timestamp, and outcome.

### 6) Assign review ownership via operational workflow (evidence-ready)
- Configure SIEM dashboards/queries and alerting for privileged-function execution events.
- Route alerts/events to the appropriate review teams (e.g., SOC for triage; IAM/Platform owners for confirmed misuse) and document the review workflow and SLAs in the system security documentation.

## WHO
- **Application Owner / Security Engineering**: maintain the Privileged Functions Register and Audited-Events Mapping.
- **Platform/Infrastructure Team**: enable OS/cloud/database native auditing and log forwarding.
- **SIEM/Monitoring Team**: implement normalization, retention, access controls, and dashboards/alerts.
- **SOC/IAM/Platform Reviewers**: perform periodic review and retain evidence of review outcomes.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. A **Privileged Functions Register** exists for the application/system and is current (version-controlled).
2. For each privileged function listed, there is at least one **auditable event** generated by native auditing and forwarded to the SIEM.
3. In a test execution of each privileged function, the SIEM contains a corresponding event with:
   - actor identity (user/service account),
   - privileged function name/type,
   - target resource,
   - timestamp,
   - outcome (success/failure).
4. Privileged-function events are **retained** and protected from unauthorized modification/deletion per the organization’s logging/retention policy.
5. Evidence exists that review is enabled (e.g., SIEM queries/dashboards and documented workflow/ownership for review).

### ac-6.10 — Prohibit Non-privileged Users from Executing Privileged Functions (Enhancement)

#### Enforce JIT privileged access for privileged functions with deny logging

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement a technical enforcement mechanism so that **non-privileged users cannot execute privileged functions** (e.g., disabling/bypassing security/privacy controls, creating system accounts, performing system integrity checks, administering cryptographic key management, and bypassing intrusion detection/prevention or malicious-code protections). Privileged actions must require **explicit privileged authorization** and be **blocked** for everyone else, with **audit evidence** of denied attempts.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-6(10)** (Enhancement) requires: **“Prevent non-privileged users from executing privileged functions.”** The guidance clarifies privileged functions include actions such as **disabling/circumventing/altering security/privacy controls**, **establishing system accounts**, **performing system integrity checks**, and **cryptographic key management activities**, including **circumventing intrusion detection/prevention** or **malicious code protection**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define privileged functions and map them to roles (per application/system)
- Create a **Privileged Functions Catalogue** for the application and its supporting infrastructure (admin consoles, CI/CD, cloud admin APIs, host management, key management tooling, security tooling).
- For each privileged function, record:
  - Function name (e.g., “disable IDS/IPS”, “change firewall policy”, “run integrity check”, “manage encryption keys”, “create system/service account”).
  - Target system/component.
  - Required privileged role(s).
  - The enforcement point (IdP/PAM/host control/app authorization layer).

### 2) Enforce privileged execution via step-up/JIT elevation
- Remove standing privileged rights from non-privileged users by default.
- Implement **JIT elevation** (PAM-style) for privileged roles so privileged actions require:
  - Step-up authentication (phishing-resistant where feasible).
  - Explicit approval/workflow for high-risk privileged functions (at minimum for security/privacy control changes and key management).
- Ensure the application and all admin interfaces rely on the same authorization model (IdP roles/groups) and do not allow privileged operations through alternate paths.

### 3) Block non-privileged execution at every privileged entry point
- For each privileged function, configure the system so that **users without the privileged role** cannot:
  - Call privileged admin APIs/endpoints.
  - Access admin consoles.
  - Execute privileged scripts/commands.
  - Perform privileged operations in CI/CD pipelines.
  - Use service accounts/tokens that can perform privileged actions unless they are issued only to approved privileged workflows.
- Where applicable, enforce “deny by default” in:
  - IAM policies (cloud/provider IAM, app authorization, API gateway policies).
  - Host/OS controls (admin group membership, sudoers restrictions, service management permissions).
  - Security tooling consoles (EDR/IDS/IPS/malware protection management endpoints).

### 4) Ensure denied attempts are auditable
- Configure logging so that **every denied attempt** to execute a privileged function records at least:
  - User identity (or service identity), source, timestamp.
  - Privileged function attempted.
  - Target system/component.
  - Outcome (denied) and reason code when available.
- Forward logs to the enterprise SIEM and create alerts for repeated denied attempts and for any attempted bypass patterns.

### 5) Validate with targeted tests and produce audit evidence
- Execute test cases using a **non-privileged test account** attempting each privileged function.
- Confirm:
  - The action is blocked.
  - A corresponding denied event is generated and ingested into SIEM.
- Execute test cases using an **authorized privileged user** (with JIT elevation) to confirm permitted actions succeed.

## WHO
- **Security Architect / IAM Engineer**: owns privileged functions catalogue, role mapping, and enforcement design.
- **Platform/Cloud Engineer**: implements IAM/API/host configuration and logging integrations.
- **Application Owner / DevOps Lead**: ensures admin endpoints and CI/CD workflows enforce the same privileged authorization model.
- **SOC/SIEM Engineer**: ensures denied-attempt logging is normalized and alerting is configured.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For each privileged function in the catalogue, there exists an enforcement mechanism that denies execution by users lacking the privileged role.
2. For each privileged function, a non-privileged test user attempt results in **denial** (no privileged effect).
3. For each denied attempt, an audit record is generated containing user identity, attempted privileged function, target component, and denial outcome, and is visible in SIEM.
4. Authorized privileged users can perform the privileged functions only when JIT/step-up elevation is granted (no standing privileged access).
5. Evidence package exists: privileged functions catalogue, role mappings, configuration screenshots/policy exports, SIEM log samples for denied attempts, and test results.

### ac-7 — Unsuccessful Logon Attempts (Control)

#### Enforce 5 invalid logons/15 min with admin-controlled unlock

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Days
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement enforcement of **unsuccessful logon attempt limits** so that each user (and where applicable, the affected authentication node/component) is allowed **no more than 5 consecutive invalid logon attempts within any rolling 15-minute period**. When the maximum is exceeded, the system must **automatically lock the account or node** and keep it locked **until an administrator explicitly releases it**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-7 Unsuccessful Logon Attempts** requires limiting unsuccessful logon attempts for both **local and network** logons, and taking subsequent action when the maximum is exceeded. The guidance provided also notes that automatic lockouts are typically temporary, but **AC-7 allows exceptions**; in this organization’s parameters, the selected action is to **lock until released by an administrator** (ac-07_odp.03), which must be honored.

Organization-defined parameters to implement:
- **ac-07_odp.01 number:** 5 consecutive invalid attempts
- **ac-07_odp.02 time period:** 15 minutes (rolling window)
- **ac-07_odp.03 action:** lock the account or node until released by an administrator
- **ac-07_odp.06 action:** prompt for secret question before allowing further logon (if selected)

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Centralize enforcement for network and application logons (preferred)
1. **Identify the authentication entry points** used by the application/system: web login, mobile login, API token exchange flows (if they include interactive credential submission), SSO redirects, VPN/remote access portals, and any application gateways.
2. Configure the **enterprise identity provider (IdP)** (or equivalent centralized authentication service) to enforce:
   - **Threshold:** 5 consecutive invalid attempts
   - **Window:** rolling 15 minutes
   - **Response:** lock the account until an administrator explicitly releases it
3. Ensure the lockout policy applies to **all relevant network logon paths** (SSO and direct credential entry) so that attempts are counted consistently.
4. Configure **audit logging** so that events are generated for:
   - invalid attempt threshold progression (if available)
   - lock initiation when the threshold is exceeded
   - administrator release/unlock action
5. Forward authentication/lockout audit events to the organization SIEM/log platform for retention and review.

### 2) Enforce for local logons on endpoints that authenticate users
1. For any **local OS authentication** paths that users can use to access the application environment (e.g., jump hosts, admin consoles, application servers with local accounts), ensure the OS/local authentication mechanism is configured with the **same threshold and window** and uses **admin-controlled unlock**.
2. If full parity is not feasible for certain endpoints, document the gap and ensure compensating controls are in place at the access layer (e.g., require IdP-backed authentication for all interactive access to the application).

### 3) Implement “secret question before further logon” behavior (only if selected/feasible)
1. If the organization’s selected action requires it (**ac-07_odp.06**), implement the flow so that after threshold is approached/exceeded (per your chosen interpretation and IdP/app capabilities), the user is prompted to answer a secret question **before further logon is allowed**.
2. Ensure that this does **not** allow bypass of the **admin-controlled lock** requirement when the maximum is exceeded (ac-07_odp.03). In other words:
   - secret question may be used as an additional friction step per policy
   - but once the maximum is exceeded, the account/node must remain locked until admin release.

### 4) Administrator release workflow and separation of duties
1. Create/align an **administrator unlock procedure** that requires explicit admin action to release the lock.
2. Enforce separation of duties where feasible (e.g., unlock requires privileged role distinct from standard support roles).
3. Ensure unlock actions are auditable and tied to the user/account and timestamp.

## WHO
- **Application Owner / IAM Owner:** owns configuration of authentication/lockout policies and ensures coverage of all login paths.
- **Identity & Access Management (IAM) Engineer:** implements IdP/SSO lockout configuration and audit event forwarding.
- **System Administrator / Privileged Access Administrator:** performs administrator unlock/release actions per procedure.
- **Security Operations (SOC):** monitors SIEM alerts for lockout/unlock events and supports incident response.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For a test user, after **5 consecutive invalid logon attempts within a rolling 15-minute window**, the account is **automatically locked**.
2. After lock initiation, the user **cannot authenticate** again until an **administrator explicitly releases** the account.
3. The enforcement applies to **network logon paths** used by the application (e.g., SSO/web login) and counts attempts across those paths as configured.
4. **Audit evidence exists** for:
   - lock initiation (threshold exceeded)
   - administrator unlock/release event
   - timestamps and affected account identifier
5. If secret-question prompting is enabled per **ac-07_odp.06**, the prompt occurs according to the configured policy, and **does not bypass** the admin-controlled lock requirement after the maximum is exceeded.


### ac-7.2 — Purge or Wipe Mobile Device (Enhancement)

#### MDM device-unlock failure wipe at 10 attempts with audit evidence

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Days
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an MDM-enforced, **device-level** purge/wipe for **in-scope mobile devices** after **10 consecutive unsuccessful device unlock (logon) attempts**, with **cryptographic erase** used when the device has **strong full-disk encryption**, and an **approved NIST SP 800-88 Rev. 1 purge/wipe** method otherwise. Ensure **successful device unlock resets** the failure counter and that **audit records** capture wipe action details.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-7(2)** enhancement requires purging/wiping information from **mobile devices** based on defined **purge/wipe requirements and techniques** after a defined number of **consecutive, unsuccessful device logon attempts**. It also specifies that the logon is to the **mobile device** (not a specific account) and that **successful logons reset the unsuccessful logon count**. The guidance further states cryptographic erase may be unnecessary if sufficiently strong encryption is used, and otherwise NIST SP 800-88 Rev. 1 sanitization should be applied.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Define and enforce in-scope device population (mobile devices)**
   - Create an MDM enrollment/scope group for devices that are allowed to access organizational information (e.g., corporate-managed smartphones/tablets).
   - Ensure only enrolled devices can access org resources (e.g., via conditional access tied to MDM compliance).

2. **Configure device-level unlock failure threshold (10 attempts)**
   - In the MDM, configure the device security policy to trigger **automatic wipe/purge** after **10 consecutive unsuccessful device unlock attempts**.
   - Validate that the trigger is based on **device unlock failures** (screen lock/passcode attempts), not application sign-in failures.

3. **Ensure counter reset on successful device unlock**
   - Confirm via MDM/OS behavior that a **successful device unlock** resets the unsuccessful unlock attempt counter to zero.
   - Document the observed behavior during testing (see acceptance criteria).

4. **Select sanitization method based on encryption strength**
   - Implement a decision rule in the MDM workflow:
     - If the device reports **strong full-disk encryption** enabled (MDM/OS encryption posture signal), perform **cryptographic erase**.
     - Otherwise, perform **NIST SP 800-88 Rev. 1-aligned purge/wipe** (configured as the organization-defined technique).
   - Where encryption posture signals are ambiguous, enforce minimum OS/encryption requirements for enrollment so the method selection remains reliable.

5. **Generate and retain auditable evidence**
   - Configure MDM to emit events for:
     - device identifier (e.g., serial/UDID), user (if applicable), timestamp,
     - wipe action type (cryptographic erase vs purge/wipe), and completion status.
   - Forward events to the SIEM/log platform and retain per organizational logging/retention policy.

6. **Operationalize with change control and configuration management**
   - Manage MDM policy settings via version-controlled configuration templates.
   - Record the organization-defined parameters used:
     - in-scope mobile devices,
     - purge/wipe requirements and techniques,
     - threshold of **10** consecutive unsuccessful device unlock attempts.

## WHO
- **Security/Compliance Engineer**: owns control mapping, parameter definitions, and acceptance testing criteria.
- **MDM Administrator**: implements MDM policies (unlock failure wipe threshold, encryption-based method selection, audit/event forwarding).
- **IAM/Identity Engineer**: ensures conditional access gates access to organizational information for enrolled/compliant devices.
- **SOC/SIEM Engineer**: ensures wipe events are ingested, normalized, and retained for audit.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For an **MDM-enrolled in-scope** device, after **10 consecutive unsuccessful device unlock attempts**, the device initiates the configured **purge/wipe** action automatically.
2. A **successful device unlock** resets the failure counter (verified by test: fail N times, successfully unlock, then fail again and confirm wipe occurs only after reaching 10 consecutive failures post-reset).
