- Send audit events to the enterprise logging/SIEM pipeline.
- Restrict who can change labels (e.g., only authorized roles/workflows), and require elevated authorization for changes that reduce security/privacy protections.

### 5) Support 90-day applicability reviews
- Implement a scheduled governance workflow that:
  - enumerates objects/messages/records with bound labels
  - checks whether the label remains applicable (based on current classification/PII/consent rules)
  - flags exceptions for review and, where policy allows, triggers re-binding.
- Ensure the workflow uses the defined review frequency: **every 90 days** (ac-16_odp.10/11).

## WHO
- **Application Owner / Data Governance Lead**: owns attribute schema, permitted values, and review workflow definitions.
- **Security Engineering (IRM/DLP/API security)**: implements validation, binding propagation, and audit event generation.
- **Platform/OT Engineering**: implements OT-specific binding propagation/sidecar metadata where needed.
- **Compliance/Privacy Officer**: validates privacy attribute handling (PII/HIPAA/consent/role) and approves review criteria.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1) For each covered system, a test message/document/API call can be created with each permitted attribute type/value, and the system **persists** the binding through at least one end-to-end workflow (create → store → process → transmit/export).
2) Attempts to set any attribute value outside the permitted allow-lists are **rejected or normalized** to canonical permitted values; no out-of-range values are stored.
3) Every label binding and label change generates an audit record containing **what changed, when, and by whom**, and these events are visible in the enterprise logging/SIEM.
4) A label change performed by an unauthorized role/workflow is denied.
5) The system produces evidence that the **applicability review runs at least every 90 days** (e.g., scheduled job logs, exception queue, and review artifacts).

### ac-16.1 — Dynamic Attribute Association (Enhancement)

#### Event-driven security/privacy label recalculation and write-back

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Months
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an automated, policy-driven mechanism that **dynamically associates security and privacy attributes** with:
- **Subjects** (information system users and service accounts)
- **Objects** (data objects such as files, database records, and message payloads)
- **Privacy data subjects** (individuals represented in records)
- **Privacy personal data objects** (personal data fields/identifiers and consent artifacts)

The mechanism must **recompute and update attributes as information is created, updated, combined/aggregated, or moved**, and must do so **in accordance with the organization-defined security and privacy policies**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-16(1)** requires: “**Dynamically associate security and privacy attributes** with {{ insert: param, ac-16.1_prm_1 }} in accordance with … **{{ insert: param, ac-16.1_prm_2 }}**” as information is **created and combined**. Guidance notes attributes may change due to **aggregation/combination**, **changes in access authorizations**, **changes in security category**, or **situational changes**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the authoritative attribute model (canonical schema)
- Create a canonical label/attribute schema for:
  - **Security attributes** (e.g., classification Secret/Confidential and access-control authorization tags)
  - **Privacy attributes** (e.g., HIPAA/GDPR categories, data-minimization flags, consent/processing constraints)
- Ensure the schema supports **composition rules** for “created and combined” outcomes (e.g., merged record classification becomes the required resulting category; privacy context becomes the union/most restrictive applicable constraints).

### 2) Encode the organization-defined policies as versioned policy-as-code
- Implement policy-as-code that maps from:
  - **Security policies** (ac-16.01_odp.05) and **privacy policies** (ac-16.01_odp.06)
  - plus current metadata (record fields, data types, classification indicators, consent state, etc.)
  - into computed security/privacy attributes.
- Include explicit rules for the guidance scenarios:
  - aggregation/combination
  - changes in individual access authorizations
  - changes in security category
  - situational privacy changes

### 3) Implement event-driven recalculation triggers
Integrate with authoritative event sources so recalculation occurs when attributes can change:
- **Identity/authorization events**: role/entitlement changes for users and service accounts (subjects)
- **Data lifecycle events**:
  - record/file/message create/update
  - classification/security-category changes
  - merge/aggregate/combine operations (e.g., ETL jobs, report generation, record linkage)
  - move/copy operations across stores/queues
- **Privacy context events**:
  - creation/linking/removal of personal data objects (HIPAA identifiers, GDPR fields)
  - consent artifact changes
  - changes in the set of individuals represented in a record

### 4) Recompute and write back labels/attributes at the right time
- On each event, compute the **current** attributes for affected:
  - **ac-16.1_prm_1 subjects/objects** (security attributes)
  - **ac-16.01_odp.03/04 privacy subjects/personal data objects** (privacy attributes)
- Write back computed attributes to the relevant systems:
  - IAM/IdP or authorization metadata store for subject security attributes
  - data platform metadata (e.g., DB row/document metadata, object storage metadata, message headers) for object security attributes
  - application data model fields for privacy attributes tied to individuals and personal data objects
- Ensure “created and combined” outputs receive **resulting** attributes (not stale source labels).

### 5) Produce audit evidence for every dynamic association change
- For each recalculation/write-back, emit an audit record containing at minimum:
  - what entity (subject/object/privacy subject/personal data object) was updated
  - old vs new attributes
  - triggering event type
  - policy version used (security policy + privacy policy versions)
  - correlation ID for traceability
- Forward audit records to the enterprise logging/SIEM pipeline.

### 6) Guardrails to prevent bypass and ensure consistency
- Enforce that label/attribute updates are performed only by the attribute service (or via a shared library/SDK that calls it) rather than ad-hoc application code.
- Add validation checks so downstream enforcement components reject or quarantine data/requests with missing/invalid attributes.

## WHO
- **Solution owner / Application security architect**: defines label schema and policy-as-code mapping.
- **Platform/data engineering lead**: integrates event sources and write-back into data stores/ETL/message pipelines.
- **IAM engineer**: integrates identity/authorization change events and subject attribute write-back.
- **Security engineering / compliance**: validates policy correctness, composition rules, and audit evidence.
- **Developers**: integrate application components/SDK calls for label enforcement and metadata propagation.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Dynamic security association**: When a user/service account’s role/entitlements change, the system updates the computed security attributes for that subject according to the organization-defined security policy.
2. **Dynamic security association for objects**: When a data object’s classification/security category changes or when data is moved/combined, the system updates the object’s security attributes to the correct resulting values.
3. **Dynamic privacy association**: When personal data objects (HIPAA/GDPR fields/identifiers/consent artifacts) are created/linked/removed or when records are aggregated/combined, the system updates privacy attributes for both:
   - the privacy data subjects represented in records
   - the personal data objects
   according to the organization-defined privacy policy.
4. **Correct handling of “created and combined”**: For at least one implemented aggregation/combination workflow, the resulting output attributes match the defined composition rules (including most-restrictive/union behavior as specified by policy).
5. **Audit evidence**: Every label/attribute change produces an audit event containing old/new values, triggering event, and policy version, and these events are observable in the enterprise logging/SIEM.
6. **No stale labels**: After a combine/move operation, the destination object/record/message contains updated attributes (not references to source labels without recomputation).


### ac-16.2 — Attribute Value Changes by Authorized Individuals (Enhancement)

#### Enforce authorized security/privacy attribute changes with audit trail

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an application capability that allows **only explicitly authorized individuals (or approved automated processes acting on their behalf)** to **define or change** the values of **security and privacy attributes**, and that **records every successful change** with the **actor identity** and **time** (and the changed attribute values).

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-16(2)** (Enhancement) requires: “Provide authorized individuals (or processes acting on behalf of individuals) the capability to define or change the value of associated security and privacy attributes.” The guidance emphasizes limiting attribute creation/modification to authorized individuals because attribute values affect access to organizational information and privacy.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define attribute types and enforce “security vs privacy” scope
- In the application, classify which fields/metadata are **security attributes** and which are **privacy attributes** (e.g., access level, data-sharing consent, privacy handling category).
- Ensure only these classified attributes are eligible for the controlled “attribute change” operation.

### 2) Create an explicit authorization mechanism for attribute writes
- Add a dedicated authorization check for the **attribute-change API/UI** (e.g., `POST /attributes/{type}/{name}` or equivalent).
- Authorization must be based on an **allowlist** of roles/groups/permissions that correspond to “authorized individuals” for each attribute category (security vs privacy).
- Deny all attribute-change attempts by default (fail closed).

### 3) Support “process acting on behalf of individuals” with explicit linkage
- For automated processes, require that the process uses an identity that is **explicitly approved** for attribute changes (e.g., a service account/automation identity).
- Require the request to include an **actor identity claim** (the individual on whose behalf the process acts) and validate it against the workflow/approval system (e.g., ticket/workflow ID mapped to the actor).
- Enforce that the automation identity cannot change attributes without a valid, approved linkage (e.g., workflow state = approved).

### 4) Require step-up authentication for privileged attribute changes
- For interactive users, require step-up authentication (e.g., re-authentication / MFA) when invoking the attribute-change operation.
- For automation, require strong authentication (e.g., mTLS or signed tokens) and restrict the automation identity to the minimum required endpoints.

### 5) Implement tamper-evident audit logging for successful changes
For every **successful** security/privacy attribute change, write an audit event containing at minimum:
- actor identity (user ID / automation identity)
- (if automation acting on behalf) the individual on whose behalf
- timestamp
- target object (e.g., user/account/resource whose attributes changed)
- attribute name/type (security vs privacy)
- before value and after value
- request correlation ID / workflow/ticket ID
- source (admin UI vs API vs automation)

### 6) Ensure audit events are protected and retained
- Send audit events to the enterprise logging/SIEM pipeline.
- Apply integrity protections (e.g., restricted write permissions, append-only storage, and/or WORM/immutable log sink where available).
- Ensure logs are retained per organizational policy.

### 7) Add negative controls and monitoring
- Block unauthorized attempts (return authorization error; do not reveal attribute values).
- Alert on anomalous patterns (e.g., bulk attribute changes, changes outside approved change windows, changes to high-impact attributes).

## WHO
- **Application Owner / Backend Engineer**: implement authorization checks, step-up enforcement, and audit event generation.
- **IAM/Identity Engineer**: provision/maintain the allowlisted roles/groups and automation identities.
- **Security/Privacy Officer (or delegated governance)**: define which attributes are security/privacy and approve which roles/processes may change them.
- **SOC/SIEM Engineer**: configure alerting and ensure audit log forwarding/retention.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Authorization enforcement**: An unprivileged user cannot change any classified security/privacy attribute; the operation is denied.
2. **Allowlist correctness**: Only explicitly authorized roles/groups (and explicitly approved automation identities) can successfully change security/privacy attributes.
3. **Automation linkage**: When an automation identity changes attributes, the request includes a valid approved linkage to the individual on whose behalf; otherwise the change is denied.
4. **Step-up authentication**: Interactive attribute changes require step-up authentication; attempts without step-up are denied.
5. **Audit completeness**: Every successful attribute change produces an audit record containing actor identity, timestamp, target object, attribute name/type, before/after values, and correlation/workflow ID.
6. **Audit integrity**: Audit records are forwarded to the SIEM/log store and are protected against modification by application users.
7. **Test evidence**: Automated tests (unit/integration) and a manual test run demonstrate both authorized success and unauthorized failure, with corresponding audit events present in the log store.

### ac-16.3 — Maintenance of Attribute Associations by System (Enhancement)

#### Signed attribute assertions and integrity-checked bindings for subjects/objects

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an authoritative, tamper-evident mechanism that maintains the association and integrity of **organization-defined security and privacy attributes** (ac-16.3_prm_1) to **organization-defined subjects and objects** (ac-16.3_prm_2) so automated policy decisions (access control, information flow, disclosure, retention expiry) always use the maintained associations.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST AC-16(3) enhancement requires: **“Maintain the association and integrity of {{ac-16.3_prm_1}} to {{ac-16.3_prm_2}}.”** Guidance emphasizes that maintaining integrity of attribute associations with sufficient assurance enables **automated policy actions** and that integrity can be maintained via **integrity monitoring detecting anomalies vs. known-good baselines**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the attribute-to-subject/object binding model (once, then enforce)
- Create a controlled attribute schema for **security attributes** and **privacy attributes** per organization-defined parameters:
  - Security attributes: classification/clearance/need-to-know/ITAR-EAR (ac-16.03_odp.01)
  - Privacy attributes: HIPAA/GDPR tags (ac-16.03_odp.02)
- Define subject types that must carry these attributes:
  - e.g., system administrators, application owners, privileged service identities (ac-16.03_odp.03)
- Define object types that must carry these attributes:
  - e.g., security configuration files, access control policy objects, integrity-monitored known-good baselines (ac-16.03_odp.04)
  - e.g., data stores/datasets/files/config repositories containing Confidential/Secret information (ac-16.03_odp.06)
- Produce an “attribute binding map” that states, for each attribute set, which subject/object identifiers it applies to.

### 2) Implement an Attribute Authority that issues signed assertions
- Deploy/configure an **Attribute Authority** service (can be an existing enterprise policy/attribute service) that:
  - Stores the authoritative attribute bindings for subjects and objects.
  - Issues **short-lived, signed attribute assertions/tokens** (e.g., JWT/JWS or equivalent) containing:
    - subject identifier (and subject attribute claims)
    - object identifier (and object attribute claims)
    - token issuance time and expiry
    - signing key identifier
- Ensure enforcement points validate signatures and token expiry.

### 3) Bind object metadata to immutable identifiers
- For each object type that will be used in automated decisions (datasets/files/config/policy objects), ensure the application uses an **immutable object identifier** (e.g., content hash + canonical metadata ID, or repository object ID) that is referenced in the signed assertions.
- Prevent “free-form” attribute attachment in application code by requiring that attribute claims used for decisions come only from validated signed assertions.

### 4) Enforce maintained associations at automated decision points
- Update authorization and policy decision logic so that automated actions reference the maintained attributes:
  - Access control decisions
  - Information flow control decisions
  - Information disclosure decisions
  - Retention date expiry decisions
- Implementation pattern:
  - At request time, enforcement point obtains/validates the subject’s and target object’s signed attribute assertions.
  - Policy-as-code (ABAC-style rules) evaluates using those claims.
  - If assertions are missing/invalid/expired or object identifier mismatch occurs, default to **deny/restrict** and generate an audit event.

### 5) Maintain integrity via integrity monitoring against known-good baselines
- For security configuration objects and policy objects (ac-16.03_odp.04), implement integrity monitoring that:
  - Computes and stores “known-good” hashes/signatures of the attribute-binding inputs and/or the configuration/policy artifacts that influence attribute associations.
  - Detects anomalies/changes and alerts.
- Integrate integrity monitoring results into enforcement behavior:
  - If a known-good baseline check fails for an object/policy/config that participates in attribute associations, enforcement must treat the association as untrusted (deny/restrict) until remediated.

### 6) Operationalize and document
- Add to system security/privacy documentation:
  - How attributes are defined (ac-16.03_odp.01/02)
  - Which subjects/objects are in scope (ac-16.03_odp.03/04/05/06)
  - How integrity monitoring and known-good baselines are maintained
  - How automated policy actions consume the maintained associations
- Assign responsibilities to application owner/security/privacy engineering for:
  - attribute binding map maintenance
  - baseline updates (with change control)
  - incident response when integrity monitoring flags anomalies

## WHO
- **Application Security Engineer / IAM/Policy Engineer**: implement Attribute Authority integration, signed assertion validation, and policy-as-code enforcement.
- **Security Operations / GRC**: define attribute binding map governance and baseline integrity monitoring procedures.
- **System Administrator / DevOps**: maintain known-good baselines via approved change/release process.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For each in-scope subject/object type defined in ac-16.3_prm_2, the system produces and uses **validated signed attribute assertions** derived from ac-16.3_prm_1.
2. Automated policy decisions (access, flow, disclosure, retention expiry) are evaluated using the maintained attribute claims; ad-hoc/unstamped attribute metadata is not sufficient.
3. If a signed assertion is invalid/expired or the object identifier does not match the assertion, the system **denies/restricts** and logs an auditable event.
4. Integrity monitoring is configured for the defined security configuration/policy objects (ac-16.03_odp.04) and detects deviations from known-good baselines; on detection, enforcement treats the association as untrusted (deny/restrict) until remediated.
5. Evidence exists for: attribute schema, attribute binding map, baseline management procedure, and system documentation describing how maintained associations support automated policy actions.

### ac-16.4 — Association of Attributes by Authorized Individuals (Enhancement)

#### Authorized attribute association with policy validation and audit trail

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an application capability that lets **authorized individuals (or authorized processes acting on their behalf)** associate organization-defined **security attributes** (e.g., PUBLIC/CONFIDENTIAL/SECRET + compartment codes) and **privacy attributes** (e.g., HIPAA/GDPR role tags for subjects; HIPAA PHI/GDPR personal data tags for objects) with **eligible subjects and objects** (users/service accounts; files/directories/network ports; and on-prem document-management items). The system must **enforce valid combinations**, ensure the association is made to the correct **subject/object records**, and **record auditable events** for creation/deletion/modification of attributes.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-16(4)** requires: “Provide the capability to associate {{param ac-16.4_prm_1}} with {{param ac-16.4_prm_2}} by authorized individuals (or processes acting on behalf of individuals).” The guidance further expects support such as prompting/automation, validity checks for attribute combinations, and consideration of auditable events for attribute lifecycle changes.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the attribute model and allowed associations (policy-as-data)
- Create an **Attribute Catalog** in the application (or integrated metadata service) containing:
  - Allowed **security labels**: PUBLIC, CONFIDENTIAL, SECRET, plus **compartment codes**.
  - Allowed **privacy tags**:
    - For **subjects**: HIPAA role (covered entity workforce) and GDPR role (data controller/processor).
    - For **objects**: HIPAA PHI and GDPR personal data.
  - Eligible **subjects**: users and service accounts authorized to assign attributes.
  - Eligible **objects**: files, directories, network ports, and on-prem document-management items.
- Encode **valid combinations** rules (e.g., SECRET requires at least one compartment; HIPAA PHI tag may only be applied to objects that are classified as regulated content types; privacy tags may be restricted by object type).

### 2) Enforce authorization for attribute association
- Implement an **Authorization Check** on every attribute-association request:
  - Only allow actors in an **“Attribute Assigner”** role/group (or ABAC policy) to assign/change attributes.
  - Support “processes acting on behalf of individuals” by requiring that automated workflows carry an **end-user identity context** (e.g., signed/propagated user principal) and are permitted by the same authorization policy.

### 3) Implement the association capability with prompts/automation and validity enforcement
- Provide a UI/API endpoint for attribute association that:
  - Lets authorized users select attributes via controlled inputs (drop-downs/validated pickers) for security labels and privacy tags.
  - Optionally supports **automation** (rule-based categorization) that proposes attributes; the system must still validate combinations before persisting.
  - Enforces **valid combinations** at save time using the Attribute Catalog rules.
  - Ensures associations are applied to the correct **authoritative identifiers** for the target subject/object (e.g., immutable user/service-account IDs; canonical file/directory IDs; network port identifiers; document-management item IDs).

### 4) Persist associations and record auditable events
- Store attribute associations in a dedicated, versioned metadata store (or database tables) with:
  - Actor identity (user/service principal), timestamp, request correlation ID, target subject/object IDs, attribute values before/after.
  - Event type covering **create, delete, modify** of attribute associations.
- Forward audit events to the enterprise logging/SIEM pipeline in a structured format.

### 5) Manage attribute lifecycle and evidence
- Provide administrative controls to update the Attribute Catalog (allowed values and combination rules) with change control.
- Ensure the system can produce audit-ready evidence showing:
  - Who associated which attributes to which subject/object, when, and what changed.

## WHO
- **Application Security Engineer / IAM Engineer**: implement authorization checks and identity context propagation for automated workflows.
- **Application Developer**: implement attribute association endpoints/UI, metadata persistence, and combination validation.
- **Data Governance Lead / Privacy Officer**: define allowed attribute values and valid combinations for HIPAA/GDPR use.
- **Security Operations / SIEM Engineer**: ensure audit event forwarding, retention, and alerting.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Authorization enforcement**: An unauthorized user cannot create/modify/delete attribute associations; attempts are denied and logged.
2. **Correct association targeting**: Attributes are persisted only against the correct authoritative subject/object identifiers; tampering with IDs results in denial or no-op.
3. **Valid combination enforcement**: The system rejects invalid attribute combinations according to the Attribute Catalog rules (e.g., missing required compartment for SECRET).
4. **Automation acting on behalf of individuals**: Automated categorization/workflows succeed only when executed with an authorized end-user context and are logged with that context.
5. **Auditability**: Every attribute association create/delete/modify generates an auditable event containing actor, target IDs, attribute values before/after, and timestamp; events are forwarded to SIEM.
6. **Evidence generation**: A reviewer can query audit logs to reconstruct the full history of attribute associations for a given subject/object.

### ac-16.5 — Attribute Displays on Objects to Be Output (Enhancement)

#### Central output renderer with subscriber-aware full/masked attributes

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement a single, centralized output-rendering component (library/service) that injects required human-readable security and privacy attributes onto every output object (printed pages, screen views, PDFs, exports) at render time.

The renderer must:
- Always display the required attribute labels in human-readable form using the organization’s naming conventions:
  - **Classification**
  - **Handling Caveats**
  - **Data Owner**
  - **System/Network**
  - **Release/Distribution**
  - **Privacy Notice ID**
- Show **full attribute values** only when the **subscriber has unmasked access**.
- Otherwise show **masked/redacted** values.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST AC-16(5) requires that the system “display security and privacy attributes in human-readable form on each object that the system transmits to output devices” using the organization-defined instructions and naming conventions, and that outputs mitigate unauthorized exposure by showing full values only when unmasked by the subscriber.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the attribute display contract (human-readable mapping)
- Create a canonical attribute model for the six required attributes.
- Implement mapping from stored/internal attribute values to **human-readable strings** that match the required labels (per **ac-16.05_odp.02 naming conventions**).

### 2) Implement subscriber-aware unmasked vs masked decision at render time
- Integrate with the enterprise authorization context (e.g., session claims/entitlements from the IdP/authorization service).
- Define a boolean decision such as `unmasked_access` derived from subscriber authorization (role/entitlement + any required context).
- Ensure the decision is evaluated **at output-render time** (not only at data storage time).

### 3) Implement deterministic masking
- Implement a masking function that replaces full values with masked/redacted representations when `unmasked_access=false`.
- Ensure the masking function is applied to the attribute **values** while the **labels** remain visible.

### 4) Enforce “every output object” via a single rendering pipeline
- Route all output generation paths through the renderer:
  - Web UI views
  - Mobile views
  - API-generated PDFs
  - Report/export generators
  - Print templates
- Add a CI/CD guardrail:
  - Template linting or build-time checks that prevent bypassing the renderer or omitting any of the six labels.

### 5) Add audit evidence per output object
- Emit an audit/log event per rendered output object including:
  - output identifier (document/page/screen instance id)
  - subscriber identity
  - attribute set version
  - `display_mode=full|masked`
- Forward to SIEM/logging platform to provide evidence that the correct mode was used.

### 6) Document procedures
- Write a short procedure describing:
  - how `unmasked_access` is granted/verified
  - how masking is applied
  - developer requirement to use the renderer for all outputs
  - how to interpret audit evidence

## WHO
- **Application Security Engineer / Security Architect**: define masking rules, unmasked access decision logic, and audit event schema.
- **Backend/Platform Engineer**: implement the renderer library/service and integrate it into all output pipelines.
- **IAM/Authorization Engineer**: ensure the unmasked entitlement/claims are correctly issued and validated.
- **QA/Test Lead**: validate full vs masked behavior across all output channels.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For each output channel (web screen, PDF export, print), the rendered artifact contains **all six labels** exactly as specified by the organization naming conventions.
2. When `unmasked_access=true`, the artifact shows **full attribute values** for all six attributes.
3. When `unmasked_access=false`, the artifact shows **masked/redacted values** for all six attributes (labels still present).
4. No output template bypasses the renderer (enforced by CI/CD checks).
5. For each output instance, an audit record exists showing `display_mode=full|masked` and the subscriber identity.
6. Automated tests cover at least: (a) unmasked subscriber, (b) masked subscriber, (c) missing/invalid entitlement results in masked mode.

### ac-16.6 — Maintenance of Attribute Association (Enhancement)

#### Attribute association maintenance via authoritative mapping + drift checks

- **Category:** Manual
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Days
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an authoritative, repeatable process (with supporting automation where feasible) that requires personnel to **associate and keep associated** the organization-defined **security and privacy attributes** with the organization-defined **subjects and objects**, **in accordance with** the organization-defined **security and privacy policies/Attribute Management Standard**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-16(6)** enhancement requires: “Require personnel to associate and maintain the association of {{ac-16.6_prm_1}} with {{ac-16.6_prm_2}} in accordance with {{ac-16.6_prm_3}}.”
Guidance clarifies that maintaining attribute association requires **individual users (not the system)** to maintain associations of defined security/privacy attributes with subjects and objects.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the exact attribute-to-subject/object mapping work instructions
- Create/maintain a job aid aligned to **{{ac-16.6_prm_3}} (Attribute Management Standard + privacy policies)** that enumerates:
  - **Security attributes** for **subjects** ({{ac-16.06_odp.01}}): data classification, system role, access authorisation level.
  - **Security attributes** for **objects** ({{ac-16.06_odp.02}}): data classification, handling caveats, encryption requirement.
  - **Privacy attributes** for **subjects** ({{ac-16.06_odp.03}}): personal data type, consent/processing basis.
  - **Privacy attributes** for **objects** ({{ac-16.06_odp.04}}): personal data category, retention/disclosure constraints.
  - **Subjects** and **objects** lists ({{ac-16.06_odp.05}}-{{ac-16.06_odp.08}}).
- Include explicit “when to update” triggers (e.g., role change, new dataset onboarding, system decommission, consent change, retention policy change) referencing the Attribute Management Standard.

### 2) Assign named responsibility and require “maintenance” actions
- Assign roles (e.g., **Attribute Steward / Data Owner / Privacy Officer / OT Data Custodian**) responsible for maintaining associations for their scope of subjects/objects.
- Update the organization’s access/data governance workflow so that attribute association maintenance is a **required step** in:
  - Joiner/mover/leaver (JML) for users/service accounts and OT operator role changes.
  - Data onboarding/offboarding for datasets/records.
  - System/application lifecycle changes that affect data classification or encryption requirements.

### 3) Provide a controlled interface for personnel to maintain associations
- Implement a controlled “Attribute Association Maintenance” workflow (UI or ticket-backed form) that allows personnel to:
  - Select the **subject/object** from the authoritative subject/object registry.
  - Select/confirm the required **security/privacy attribute values** from the allowed taxonomy.
  - Record the **policy basis** (link/reference to the relevant rule in {{ac-16.6_prm_3}}) and the **effective date**.
- Ensure the workflow supports:
  - Versioning of attribute associations.
  - Exception handling (only permitted values; require justification for exceptions).

### 4) Add periodic validation to detect drift and force corrective maintenance
- Run a scheduled validation (e.g., monthly/quarterly based on risk) that compares:
  - Current attribute associations in the association store vs. expected associations derived from authoritative sources (IdP/HR role catalog, data catalog metadata, asset inventory, OT tag registry).
- For any mismatch, generate a remediation work item that requires **personnel action** (not silent auto-correction) to update the association in accordance with {{ac-16.6_prm_3}}.

### 5) Produce audit-ready evidence
- Maintain evidence that personnel maintained associations:
  - Who updated what attribute association, when, and under which policy reference.
  - Change history and approval/exception records.
  - Validation reports showing mismatches found and remediated.

## WHO
- **Attribute Steward / Data Owner**: maintains security attribute associations for relevant subjects/objects.
- **Privacy Officer / Privacy Steward**: maintains privacy attribute associations for relevant subjects/objects.
- **IAM/Identity Governance Lead**: ensures subject registry and role taxonomy are aligned to the Attribute Management Standard.
- **Security/Compliance Analyst**: owns validation cadence, evidence collection, and audit support.
- **System/Application Owner (for this application)**: ensures the application’s data objects are correctly represented in the object registry and that lifecycle events trigger maintenance work.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For each defined subject/object category in {{ac-16.6_prm_2}}, there exists a documented mapping procedure aligned to {{ac-16.6_prm_3}} covering all attribute types in {{ac-16.6_prm_1}}.
2. Personnel can update attribute associations through the controlled maintenance workflow, and updates are recorded with:
   - subject/object identifier,
   - attribute values,
   - effective date,
   - policy reference to {{ac-16.6_prm_3}},
   - user identity of the person who performed the maintenance.
3. A scheduled validation process runs and produces a report of mismatches; for each mismatch, a remediation ticket/work item is created requiring personnel to update associations.
4. Evidence package exists for the last validation cycle showing at least one example of:
   - an attribute association update,
   - a mismatch detection,
   - a personnel remediation action,
   - and the resulting updated association record.


### ac-16.7 — Consistent Attribute Interpretation (Enhancement)

#### Shared attribute semantics guide + contract tests for access/flow

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Create and maintain a single, authoritative interpretation of every **security and privacy attribute** that is transmitted between distributed components, and enforce that interpretation consistently in both **access enforcement** and **information-flow enforcement**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-16(7)** requires organizations to provide a **consistent interpretation** of security and privacy attributes transmitted between distributed system components so that automated **access enforcement** and **flow enforcement** decisions are uniform across components.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
1. **Attribute inventory (scope all distributed enforcement points)**
   - Enumerate every attribute used in automated access decisions and information-flow decisions across the application’s distributed components (e.g., API gateway, service-to-service authorization, IAM integration, policy engines, messaging/stream routing, service mesh policies, application middleware).
   - For each attribute, record: attribute name/key, source component, transport mechanism (headers/tokens/payload fields), data type, allowed values, and where it is consumed.

2. **Define the “single shared interpretation guide” (human-readable + machine-readable)**
   - Produce an authoritative document that defines the **exact meaning** of each security attribute and each privacy attribute.
   - Include: semantics for each allowed value, precedence rules when multiple attributes are present, handling of missing/unknown/empty values, conflict resolution, and explicit mapping to enforcement outcomes for both:
     - **Access enforcement** (allow/deny/step-up/route-to-appropriate resource)
     - **Flow enforcement** (permit/deny/route/quarantine for data movement)
   - Publish the guide as:
     - A versioned human-readable standard (for auditors and developers)
     - A versioned machine-readable contract (e.g., JSON Schema + policy metadata) that can be used by components.

3. **Implement a shared enforcement library or policy contract consumption**
   - Ensure each component that makes access or flow decisions uses the same interpretation artifact:
     - Either import a shared library that implements the semantics, or
     - Consume the same versioned machine-readable contract and evaluate it via a common policy mechanism.
   - Configure components so that enforcement logic is driven by the shared contract (not duplicated ad-hoc logic).

4. **Add build-time and runtime consistency checks (fail closed where feasible)**
   - **Build-time:** add contract tests that validate attribute parsing and semantics (including edge cases like unknown values and precedence).
   - **Runtime:** validate incoming attributes against the contract; if attributes are non-conformant, enforce a defined behavior (preferably **fail closed** for access/flow decisions, or quarantine/deny per the guide).

5. **Audit-ready evidence of consistent interpretation**
   - Ensure enforcement logs include: received attribute values (or hashes/redacted values as appropriate), the **interpretation guide version**, the policy decision, and the enforcement outcome for both access and flow.
   - Ensure logs are retained per enterprise logging/retention requirements.

6. **Governance for updates and drift control**
   - Establish a change process so updates to the interpretation guide/contract are versioned and rolled out consistently across components.
   - Add a periodic verification step (e.g., automated integration tests in CI or scheduled test runs) that confirms components behave consistently for a representative set of attribute combinations.

## WHO
- **Application Security Architect / IAM & Policy Engineer:** owns the attribute semantics guide and machine-readable contract.
- **Application/Platform Engineers:** integrate the shared contract/library into access and flow enforcement points.
- **QA/Test Engineers:** implement contract tests and integration test cases.
- **Security Operations / SIEM Engineer:** ensures audit logging captures interpretation version and enforcement outcomes.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. A versioned **single shared interpretation guide** exists and covers all security and privacy attributes used by distributed enforcement points.
2. A versioned **machine-readable contract** (e.g., JSON Schema/policy metadata) exists and is referenced by all components that perform access or flow enforcement.
3. CI includes **contract tests** that validate attribute semantics, precedence, and edge-case handling.
4. Runtime enforcement validates attributes against the contract and applies the guide’s defined behavior for missing/unknown/non-conformant attributes (fail closed/quarantine/deny as specified).
5. Enforcement audit logs include the **interpretation guide version** and show consistent decisions for the same attribute inputs across components.
6. A documented rollout/change procedure exists for updating the guide/contract and verifying component consistency after changes.

### ac-16.8 — Association Techniques and Technologies (Enhancement)

#### JWS-signed security/privacy labels with HSM verification at decision points

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement the organization-defined technique for **cryptographic binding of security/privacy labels to data** using **signed metadata (JWS)** where **signing keys are protected by an HSM-backed hardware root of trust**, and ensure the system **verifies**:
- the **signed security label** at **access time** (before authorization decisions), and
- the **signed privacy label** at **processing time** (before data-handling/flow decisions).

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST **AC-16(8)** enhancement requires implementing the organization-defined **techniques and technologies** for associating security and privacy attributes to information. The guidance emphasizes that binding can be achieved by **cryptographically binding attributes to information** using **digital signatures** with keys protected by **hardware devices** (hardware roots of trust). This enables automated access/flow enforcement to rely on labels that cannot be silently altered.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the label-binding design (schema + canonicalization)
- Define the **security label** and **privacy label** claim sets to be embedded (e.g., classification/sensitivity, handling constraints, retention, lawful basis/processing constraints—use only what your organization requires).
- Define a **canonical representation** for label claims (e.g., canonical JSON rules) so the same logical label always produces the same signed content.
- Define how the JWS metadata is stored/linked to the object (e.g., embedded in object metadata fields, or stored as a sidecar record keyed by object hash/ID). Ensure the enforcement point can reliably retrieve the JWS for the specific object being accessed/processed.

### 2) Implement HSM-backed JWS signing for labels
- Create/implement a **Label Signing Service** (or library) that:
  - generates **two JWS tokens**: one for the **security label** and one for the **privacy label**;
  - signs using **HSM-protected keys** with **non-exportable private keys**;
  - records key identifiers/aliases used for signing (for audit and verification).
- Ensure signing operations occur via the HSM/KMS interface and that private keys are not exportable.

### 3) Embed signed labels into object metadata
- At label assignment time (e.g., ingestion, classification workflow, or data creation), embed:
  - **security-label JWS** into the object’s security metadata, and
  - **privacy-label JWS** into the object’s privacy metadata.
- Ensure the metadata is immutable or protected against tampering (e.g., write-once semantics where supported, restricted metadata update permissions, and/or integrity checks at retrieval).

### 4) Verify security label at access time (enforcement point)
- Place a verification step in the **access decision path** (e.g., API gateway, data access proxy, PDP/PEP, or application authorization middleware).
- For each access request:
  1. retrieve the object’s **security-label JWS**;
  2. verify the JWS signature using the trusted public key/cert chain;
  3. validate label claim integrity (including any required claim constraints such as issuer, audience, version, and object binding fields if you include them);
  4. if verification fails, **treat the label as untrusted and deny/block** the access (fail closed);
  5. use only the **verified** label values to drive authorization/policy decisions.
- Log verification outcome and the verified label values used for the decision.

### 5) Verify privacy label at processing time (data-flow/processing gateway)
- Place a verification step in the **processing/flow decision path** (e.g., workflow/orchestration gateway, ETL/stream processing gate, data-sharing/export service).
- For each processing/flow action:
  1. retrieve the object’s **privacy-label JWS**;
  2. verify the JWS signature;
  3. validate required privacy claim constraints;
  4. if verification fails, **deny/block** the processing/flow action (fail closed);
  5. use only the **verified** privacy label values to permit/route processing.
- Log verification outcome and the verified label values used for the action.

### 6) Evidence and operationalization
- Produce audit records that show, at minimum:
  - which JWS was verified (object ID, label version, key ID/issuer);
  - verification success/failure;
  - the verified label values used for the decision.
- Include the approach in the organization’s **security and privacy plans** with clear responsibilities for:
  - label assignment/signing operations,
  - enforcement-point verification,
  - key management/HSM administration,
  - incident handling for verification failures.

## WHO
- **Security Architect / Privacy Architect**: defines label schema, canonicalization, and decision-point requirements.
- **Application/Platform Engineers**: implement label signing service, metadata embedding, and enforcement-point verification.
- **HSM/KMS Administrator**: provisions HSM-backed keys, policies, and key rotation procedures.
- **Security/Privacy Operations**: monitors audit logs, investigates verification failures, and manages operational response.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **JWS signing**: Security and privacy labels are signed as **JWS** using **HSM-protected non-exportable keys**.
2. **Access-time enforcement**: For every access request, the system verifies the **security-label JWS** before authorization; if verification fails, access is **denied**.
3. **Processing-time enforcement**: For every processing/flow action, the system verifies the **privacy-label JWS** before allowing the action; if verification fails, processing/flow is **blocked**.
4. **Tamper resistance**: If the embedded JWS metadata is altered, verification fails and enforcement blocks the action.
5. **Audit evidence**: Audit logs exist showing verification outcome (success/failure), object identifier, label version, and key identifier used.
6. **Trusted key management**: Verification uses a trusted public key/certificate chain corresponding to the HSM signing keys (documented and operationally maintained).

### ac-16.9 — Attribute Reassignment — Regrading Mechanisms (Enhancement)

#### Implement validated label regrading service with signed re-tags

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Months
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Create and operate a **single-purpose “Label Regrading Service”** that is the **only** supported mechanism to change **security and privacy attributes** (labels) on information. The service must enforce an **approved policy exception ticket** workflow, perform **pre-release validation** for both security and privacy attributes, perform **cryptographic re-tagging**, and generate **complete audit logs** linking the change to the exception and validation evidence.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-16(9)** requires that security and privacy attribute changes occur **only via regrading mechanisms validated using** the organization-defined technique/procedure in **param: ac-16.9_prm_1**. The guidance emphasizes that regrading mechanisms must be **trusted**, **single purpose/limited function**, and validated because attribute changes can directly affect **policy enforcement**.

This solution directly implements the required regrading mechanism described in **ac-16.9_prm_1**: “approved data-labelling workflow with policy exception ticketing, cryptographic re-tagging, and audit logging,” and adds the required **validation** steps for security and privacy attributes using the organization-defined validation techniques in **ac-16.09_odp.01** and **ac-16.09_odp.02**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Constrain the mechanism to be single-purpose (limited function)
- Implement a dedicated service/API that supports only operations required for **label reassignment** (e.g., `RequestRegrade`, `ValidateAndReTag`, `GetRegradeEvidence`).
- Disallow general data transformation; the service should only accept: (a) target object identifier(s), (b) requested new label set, (c) policy exception ticket reference.

### 2) Enforce policy exception ticketing (authorization gate)
- Require a **policy exception ticket ID** (and fields such as scope, expiry, and allowed label transitions) to be provided with every regrade request.
- Validate ticket status before proceeding (e.g., exists, approved, not expired, matches requested scope/transition).
- Only allow regrade requests from an allowlisted set of service accounts/roles.

### 3) Security attribute validation (validated mechanism)
- Before issuing any re-tag, run **automated rule checks against the approved policy exception and test vectors** per **ac-16.09_odp.01**.
- Implement test-vector execution in the service pipeline (e.g., golden datasets/edge cases) and fail closed if validation does not match expected outcomes.

### 4) Privacy attribute validation (validated mechanism)
- Before issuing any re-tag, run **schema conformance checks** and **differential access-control tests** per **ac-16.09_odp.02**.
- Differential access-control tests must compare access outcomes **before vs after** regrading using the organization’s authorization/policy simulation inputs; fail closed on unexpected access changes.

### 5) Cryptographic re-tagging (integrity-protected labels)
- After successful validations, generate cryptographically protected label tokens for the new label set.
- Include in the token: exception ID, label version, timestamp, and validation evidence hash(s).
- Sign tokens using managed keys (e.g., HSM/KMS-backed signing) and version the signing key material.

### 6) Audit logging (complete, audit-ready evidence)
- Emit append-only audit records for every regrade attempt (success and failure) including:
  - who/which principal initiated the request (service account/user),
  - ticket ID and ticket approval metadata (as permitted),
  - requested old/new label values (or references),
  - validation results (security validation run ID + pass/fail; privacy schema conformance results; differential access test results),
  - cryptographic re-tagging outcome (token ID/version),
  - timestamps and correlation IDs.
- Forward logs to the enterprise SIEM with immutable storage controls (e.g., WORM/object lock) where available.

### 7) Integration so downstream enforcement trusts only regraded labels
- Update downstream label enforcement points (e.g., data platform/DLP/policy enforcement components) to accept **only signed re-tag tokens** (or to verify token signatures before trusting labels).
- Ensure the application path that previously allowed direct label changes is removed/blocked (or restricted so it cannot bypass the service).

## WHO
- **Application/Platform Security Engineer (lead):** designs service boundaries, validation logic, and cryptographic token format.
- **Backend/Platform Engineers:** implement the Label Regrading Service APIs, validation pipelines, and token issuance.
- **IAM/Authorization Engineer:** provides inputs for differential access-control tests and ensures enforcement points verify signed tokens.
- **GRC/Compliance Analyst:** defines/maintains the policy exception ticket requirements and evidence expectations.
- **SIEM/Logging Engineer:** ensures audit logs are routed, retained, and protected for audit.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Single-purpose enforcement:** All label reassignment requests in the environment route through the Label Regrading Service; direct label changes are blocked or cannot bypass the service.
2. **Policy exception gating:** Every successful regrade has a valid, approved, in-scope, non-expired policy exception ticket reference; requests without a valid ticket fail.
3. **Security validation:** For each successful regrade, the service runs automated rule checks against the approved exception and test vectors (**ac-16.09_odp.01**) and records pass/fail evidence; failures prevent token issuance.
4. **Privacy validation:** For each successful regrade, the service runs schema conformance checks and differential access-control tests (**ac-16.09_odp.02**) and records pass/fail evidence; failures prevent token issuance.
5. **Cryptographic re-tagging:** Issued label tokens are signed; downstream components verify signatures before trusting labels.
6. **Audit logging:** For every attempt (success/failure), audit logs include principal, ticket ID, old/new label references, validation results, token identifiers, and timestamps; logs are immutable/retained per enterprise logging policy.
7. **Operational readiness:** The service is deployed with separate environments (dev/test/prod), and validation pipelines run in the release process for production regrades.

### ac-16.10 — Attribute Configuration by Authorized Individuals (Enhancement)

#### RBAC-gated attribute schema admin with auditable change enforcement

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Days
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement a controlled, application-supported capability for **authorized individuals** to define/change the **types and values** of **security and privacy attributes** that can be associated with **subjects and objects**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-16(10)** requires that the system provide authorized individuals the capability to define/change the **type and value** of security and privacy attributes available for association with subjects/objects, and (per guidance) must **limit** creation/modification of attribute type/value to **authorized individuals only**, because attribute content can directly affect access and privacy.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define separate authorization for security vs privacy attribute configuration
- Create two privileged roles (or equivalent) in the enterprise IAM integration:
  - **Attribute Schema Admin (Security)**
  - **Attribute Schema Admin (Privacy)**
- Map these roles to specific individuals/groups in the IdP.

### 2) Enforce authorization at the application/API layer (not only UI)
- Implement RBAC checks on every attribute-schema management endpoint/function:
  - create/update/delete **attribute types**
  - create/update/delete **attribute values**
  - publish/activate schema versions
- Ensure requests are rejected server-side if the caller lacks the correct role.

### 3) Treat attribute schemas as versioned, controlled configuration
- Store attribute schema definitions (types/values, allowed formats, constraints) as **versioned configuration**.
- Require changes to go through an **approval workflow** (e.g., ticket + automated validation) before activation in production.
- Block direct “hot edits” in production by requiring activation via the controlled workflow.

### 4) Validate schema changes before activation
- Add automated validation to prevent unsafe/invalid attribute definitions (examples):
  - disallow duplicate/conflicting type identifiers
  - enforce allowed value formats/ranges
  - ensure referenced attribute types/values exist
- If validation fails, the change is not activated.

### 5) Restrict subject/object association to the deployed schema set
- In the UI/API where subjects/objects are labeled/associated, only allow selecting from the **currently deployed/active** schema types and values.
- Reject associations using unknown/unconfigured types/values.

### 6) Produce audit records for every schema change
- Emit audit events for each change to security/privacy attribute types/values including:
  - initiating identity (who)
  - timestamp (when)
  - action (what: create/update/delete)
  - target (which attribute type/value)
  - old value/new value (what changed)
  - result (allowed/denied)
- Forward audit events to the enterprise SIEM/logging pipeline.

### 7) Add operational guardrails
- Require phishing-resistant MFA and strong session controls for the admin roles (via IdP/conditional access).
- Ensure admin consoles are isolated from standard user functions where feasible.

## WHO (role responsible)
- **Application Security Engineer / Backend Engineer**: implement RBAC enforcement, schema versioning, validation, and audit event generation.
- **IAM Engineer**: configure IdP roles/groups and conditional access/MFA for admin roles.
- **Security/Privacy Governance Owner**: define which individuals are authorized and approve schema changes.
- **SIEM/Monitoring Engineer**: ensure audit events are ingested and retained per enterprise logging requirements.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. A non-authorized user cannot create/update/delete any **security** or **privacy** attribute type/value via UI or API (server-side denial).
2. Only users with **Attribute Schema Admin (Security)** can modify security attribute schemas; only users with **Attribute Schema Admin (Privacy)** can modify privacy attribute schemas.
3. Schema changes are versioned; production activation occurs only through the controlled workflow (no direct production hot edits).
4. Subject/object association screens/APIs only permit selection of types/values from the **active deployed schema**; unknown values are rejected.
5. Every schema change generates an audit record containing initiating identity, action, target, old/new values, and allowed/denied outcome.
6. Audit events are observable in the SIEM/logging system and can be used to reconstruct who changed what and when.

### ac-17 — Remote Access (Control)

#### Remote access types registry with approval gates and enforcement

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement a controlled, auditable **Remote Access Types Registry** for each system/environment, and enforce that only **pre-authorized remote access types** can establish connections. The registry must include (per remote access type) the **allowed users/groups**, **usage restrictions**, **required connection/configuration requirements**, and **implementation guidance**. Enforcement must occur at the remote access entry point (e.g., VPN/remote access gateway/ZTNA/jump host) and at identity (e.g., conditional access), with audit evidence linking each connection to its authorized type.

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-17 requires that remote access methods are **explicitly defined** and that **authorization is obtained prior to allowing remote access** (without specifying formats for authorization). Guidance also notes that encrypted VPNs can provide confidentiality/integrity assurance, but remote access controls must still be managed because VPNs traverse external networks and can affect monitoring/availability.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Create the Remote Access Types Registry (source of truth)
For each system/environment (prod/test/DR), create registry entries for every permitted remote access type, such as:
- Encrypted VPN (with specific crypto/auth profile)
- ZTNA application access (per app)
- Jump host/bastion access (for admin/vendor)
- Vendor remote support (via approved tooling and path)
- Wireless/dial-up (if applicable)

Each entry must document:
- **Who may use it** (named roles/groups; contractors/partners separated)
- **Usage restrictions** (allowed times/locations if applicable; prohibited behaviors)
- **Connection/configuration requirements** (e.g., required authentication method(s), encryption profile, allowed protocols/ports, split-tunneling rules, required client settings)
- **Implementation guidance** (step-by-step setup and verification checklist)

### 2) Implement “authorization before connection” enforcement gates
Enforce that a remote access session can only be established if the requested access path matches an **approved registry entry**.
- **Gateway enforcement**: Configure VPN/ZTNA/jump host so only approved connection profiles/auth methods are enabled per system.
- **Identity enforcement**: Add conditional access rules so the user/device/session is permitted only when it matches the approved remote access type (and required posture/attributes, if used).
- **Policy-as-code templates**: Generate gateway/identity configuration from the registry so drift is detectable and changes require review.

### 3) Create and manage authorization records per remote access type
Before enabling any registry entry for a system/environment:
- Create an **authorization record** (e.g., workflow/ticket) that references the registry entry and includes approvers.
- Only after approval, deploy/enable the corresponding gateway/identity configuration.
- Maintain a mapping: **(system, environment, remote access type) → authorization record ID**.

### 4) Produce audit-ready evidence
Ensure logs/evidence capture:
- User identity
- Remote access type (as determined by the gateway/connection profile)
- Connection start time and source endpoint details
- Authorization record ID (or a deterministic mapping from session attributes to the enabled approved profile)

Integrate with SIEM so evidence can be reviewed per system and remote access type.

### 5) Drift detection and periodic validation
- Nightly/weekly automated checks that enabled gateway/identity profiles match the registry.
- Alert on any enabled profile not present in the registry or not tied to an active authorization record.

## WHO
- **System Owner / Application Owner**: ensures registry entries exist per system/environment and are accurate.
- **IAM Engineer / Security Engineer**: implements conditional access and gateway enforcement.
- **Network/VPN/Platform Engineer**: implements gateway/jump host configuration from policy-as-code.
- **Security Governance/Compliance**: owns approval workflow requirements and periodic evidence review.

## Acceptance criteria
1. For each system/environment, there is a **complete Remote Access Types Registry** listing every permitted remote access type.
2. Each registry entry includes documented **usage restrictions**, **connection/configuration requirements**, and **implementation guidance**.
3. No remote access type can be used unless it has an **approved authorization record** created before enabling the corresponding gateway/identity configuration.
4. Gateway/identity enforcement prevents connections using non-approved remote access types (attempts fail and are logged).
5. Audit evidence exists showing, for each remote access session, the **user identity**, **remote access type**, **start time**, and a traceable link to the **authorization record** or approved profile.
6. Drift detection alerts trigger when enabled profiles diverge from the registry/authorization state.

### ac-17.1 — Monitoring and Control (Enhancement)

#### Automated remote access allow/deny with auditable session monitoring

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement automated mechanisms that (1) **monitor** remote access sessions and (2) **control/enforce** remote access methods by automatically allowing or blocking sessions based on remote access policy, across all supported remote access entry points (e.g., VPN/ZTNA portal, RDP/SSH jump hosts, secure remote web access) and supported user device types (servers, notebooks/workstations, smartphones/tablets).

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-17(1) (Monitoring and Control)** requires: **“Employ automated mechanisms to monitor and control remote access methods.”** The guidance emphasizes auditing connection activities of remote users across system components and that **audit logging for remote access is enforced by AU-2** (with event definitions in **AU-2a**). This solution ensures both automated enforcement and auditable evidence of monitoring and outcomes.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the remote access methods and enforcement points (scope)
- Create an inventory of all remote access methods that can reach the application environment (e.g., VPN, ZTNA app, secure web gateway, jump hosts for RDP/SSH, remote admin portals).
- For each method, identify the **policy enforcement point** (e.g., ZTNA/secure access gateway, VPN concentrator, jump host broker) where the session can be allowed/denied at connection time.

### 2) Centralize remote access authorization in an automated policy engine
- Integrate each remote access method with the enterprise identity/access system (IdP) so that session establishment is contingent on policy evaluation.
- Implement automated rules such as:
  - allowed user groups/roles for remote access to the application environment
  - required authentication strength (e.g., MFA) for remote access
  - device posture/compliance requirements where available (managed vs unmanaged; OS version; endpoint health)
  - optional contextual restrictions (e.g., geo/IP reputation, time-of-day) consistent with organizational remote access policy
- Ensure the enforcement point **blocks session creation** (or terminates the session) when policy fails.

### 3) Enable automated monitoring and structured audit events for both outcomes
- Configure the enforcement points (gateway/VPN/ZTNA/jump host broker and/or IdP) to emit **remote-access audit events** for:
  - **allowed** sessions (successful connection/session establishment)
  - **blocked/denied** sessions (failed authorization, policy denial)
- Ensure the emitted events include the fields required by the organization’s **AU-2/AU-2a remote access audit event definition** (e.g., remote access method, user, target system/service, source device/IP where available, and outcome).
- Forward events to the organization SIEM/logging pipeline and map them to the organization’s defined remote-access audit event schema.

### 4) Validate coverage across supported device types
- For each supported device category (server, notebook/workstation, smartphone/tablet), verify that the enforcement point can capture sufficient device/source context to apply policy and that audit events are generated for both allow and deny outcomes.

### 5) Implement automated alerting for policy-denied remote access
- Create SIEM detections/alerts for patterns such as repeated denied attempts, denied access to sensitive targets, or anomalous source context.
- Route alerts to the SOC/incident workflow (SOAR optional) to ensure monitoring results in timely response.

## WHO
- **Security Architect / IAM Engineer**: designs policy enforcement integration and event schema mapping.
- **Network/Platform Engineer**: configures VPN/ZTNA/gateway/jump host enforcement settings.
- **SIEM Engineer**: ensures audit event ingestion, normalization, and alert rules.
- **Application Owner / System Owner**: confirms remote access methods and targets in scope.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Automated enforcement:** For each in-scope remote access method, when remote access policy conditions fail, the system **denies or prevents session establishment automatically** (no manual intervention).
2. **Automated monitoring:** For each in-scope remote access method, both **allowed and denied** attempts generate remote-access monitoring/audit events.
3. **Auditability:** Audit events for remote access are present in the centralized logging/SIEM system and conform to the organization’s **AU-2/AU-2a remote access audit event details** (including outcome and required connection/session attributes).
4. **Device-type coverage:** Testing from at least one representative device per category (server, notebook/workstation, smartphone/tablet) demonstrates policy evaluation and correct allow/deny behavior with corresponding audit events.
5. **Operational readiness:** SIEM dashboards/detections show remote access allow/deny activity and denied-attempt alerts trigger as expected for defined test cases.

### ac-17.2 — Protection of Confidentiality and Integrity Using Encryption (Enhancement)

#### Enforce VPN-only remote access with approved crypto and audit evidence

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Days
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement a remote-access architecture where **all remote access sessions to the application’s administrative and internal resources are established only through an approved VPN (or equivalent secure remote cryptographic tunnel)**, using **configured cryptographic mechanisms that protect confidentiality and integrity** for every session.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-17(2)** (Enhancement) requires: **“Implement cryptographic mechanisms to protect the confidentiality and integrity of remote access sessions.”** Guidance notes that **VPNs** and **TLS** are examples of cryptographic protocols used for end-to-end communications security.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define and enforce “remote access must be encrypted” as a technical invariant
- Update the organization/application access policy to state: **remote access to application admin functions and internal resources must occur only via the approved VPN (tunnel-first)**.
- At the network edge, enforce **“no VPN, no access”**:
  - Block direct inbound access to internal subnets/services from the internet.
  - Allow inbound only to the VPN endpoints; route/permit internal access only from VPN address pools.

### 2) Standardize VPN cryptographic configuration (approved suites)
- Configure VPN endpoints using a **single approved baseline** (per enterprise crypto standards), including:
  - Minimum protocol version (e.g., IKEv2/IPsec or TLS-based VPN as approved by the organization)
  - Strong cipher suites and key exchange parameters
  - Certificate validation rules (if applicable)
  - Disable legacy/insecure algorithms and weak configurations
- Apply the baseline consistently across production, test, and DR environments.

### 3) Ensure encryption applies to every remote session
- Ensure the VPN is the only supported path for remote access to:
  - Administrative interfaces (e.g., admin consoles, management ports)
  - Internal APIs/services that must not be reachable directly from the internet
- If any alternate remote access paths exist (e.g., vendor tooling, web-based admin portals), either:
  - route them through the same VPN/tunnel-first design, or
  - implement equivalent cryptographic protection and enforce it with the same “encrypted-only” invariant.

### 4) Integrate identity and session controls (to support secure remote access)
- Require enterprise identity integration for VPN authentication (IdP integration) and enforce MFA per enterprise policy.
- Apply session controls such as re-authentication on risk (where supported) and session termination on policy changes.

### 5) Produce audit-ready evidence that encryption was used
- Enable VPN logging sufficient to demonstrate per-session protection, including at minimum:
  - user identity, source IP
  - session start/stop
  - negotiated cryptographic parameters (where the VPN platform provides them)
  - tunnel establishment events
- Centralize logs to SIEM and retain per the system security plan/retention requirements.

### 6) Document the cryptographic mechanisms and configuration
- Maintain an auditable record (e.g., security design/configuration document) that includes:
  - which cryptographic protocol(s) are used for remote access (VPN and/or TLS)
  - the approved configuration baseline (protocol versions, cipher suites, certificate/validation approach)
  - diagrams showing remote-access entry points and trust boundaries
- Keep configuration exports and change records demonstrating that the approved baseline is deployed.

## WHO
- **Network/Security Engineering Lead**: implements and standardizes VPN configuration baseline and edge enforcement.
- **IAM/Identity Engineer**: integrates IdP/MFA requirements for VPN authentication.
- **Application Owner / System Owner**: ensures remote access policy is aligned to “VPN-only” and that admin interfaces are not exposed outside the VPN.
- **Security Operations (SOC)**: validates logging, SIEM ingestion, and retention; supports audit evidence packaging.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Technical enforcement**: From the internet, direct access to internal application/admin endpoints is blocked; access is possible only via the approved VPN tunnel.
2. **Cryptographic configuration**: VPN endpoints are configured to use the organization-approved cryptographic protocol(s) and approved cipher/key exchange settings; insecure/legacy options are disabled.
3. **Coverage**: All remote administrative and internal-resource access paths are routed through the encrypted VPN tunnel (or equivalent cryptographic tunnel if an alternate method exists).
4. **Audit evidence**: VPN logs in SIEM show per-session tunnel establishment with user identity and session timestamps; logs retain negotiated cryptographic details where supported.
5. **Documentation**: Security design/configuration documentation exists and matches the deployed VPN configuration (validated via configuration exports/change records).

### ac-17.3 — Managed Access Control Points (Enhancement)

#### Enforce remote access via managed gateways only (allowlist + logs)

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Days
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement a small, organization-approved set of **managed network access control points** (e.g., VPN concentrators and/or ZTNA/secure web/remote access gateways) as the **only** routable entry path for remote administrative and other in-scope remote access to the application’s administrative interfaces and management ports.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-17(3)** requires that remote accesses are **routed through authorized and managed network access control points**. The enhancement guidance notes that limiting the number of access control points reduces attack surface.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define and inventory the managed access control points
- Create/maintain a **managed access control points register** containing: identifier (hostname/IP/FQDN), purpose (e.g., admin VPN, ZTNA connector), ownership, and monitoring/log sources.
- Ensure the register is **complete** for all remote access paths to the in-scope application environments (prod/test/DR as applicable).

### 2) Enforce routing so target systems accept remote access only from the gateways
- For each target system that can be reached remotely (e.g., app admin endpoints, SSH/RDP, database admin interfaces, internal management services):
  - **Remove/disable** direct inbound internet access to management/admin ports.
  - Configure network controls (firewall/security groups/NACLs) to **allow inbound only from the managed gateway IP ranges/security groups** (or, where supported, from gateway identities/connector networks).
  - Ensure any “break-glass” or vendor access is either:
    - routed through the same managed gateways, or
    - explicitly documented and controlled via the same managed entry-point model.

### 3) Centralize authentication and session establishment at the access control points
- Integrate gateways with the enterprise IdP and enforce **phishing-resistant MFA** (where available) and conditional access policies.
- Ensure authorization to the application/admin functions is enforced at/through the gateway (or immediately after session establishment) using existing RBAC/least privilege.

### 4) Centralize and retain evidence (audit-ready)
- Forward gateway logs and network enforcement logs (allow/deny, session start/stop, source IP, user identity, target system/port) to the SIEM.
- Configure detections/alerts for attempts to reach target admin ports **from non-gateway sources**.
- Retain logs per enterprise logging/retention requirements.

### 5) Document the design/configuration in the system security plan
- Update system design documentation and the **system security plan** to show:
  - the managed gateways as the remote access entry points,
  - the network enforcement mechanism (e.g., firewall rules/security groups) that restricts inbound access to gateway sources,
  - the log sources used to prove routing.

### 6) Continuous verification (operational control)
- Implement a periodic reconciliation process (e.g., monthly/quarterly):
  - compare the managed access control points register against current firewall/VPN/connector configuration exports,
  - verify no direct inbound rules exist for management/admin ports from the internet.

## WHO
- **Network Security Engineer / Cloud Network Engineer**: implement firewall/security group allowlisting and gateway routing.
- **IAM Engineer**: integrate gateways with IdP, enforce MFA/conditional access.
- **Application Owner / System Owner**: confirm which admin interfaces/ports are in-scope and validate access behavior.
- **Security Operations (SOC)**: ensure SIEM ingestion, alerting, and log retention.
- **Compliance/Assurance**: validate evidence package and system security plan updates for audit readiness.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. A current **managed access control points register** exists and includes all gateways used for remote access to in-scope application/admin functions.
2. For each in-scope target system/admin interface, network controls are configured such that **inbound access is permitted only from managed gateway IP ranges/security groups** (no direct internet access to management/admin ports).
3. Remote sessions to in-scope admin interfaces originate from the managed gateways (validated via SIEM/gateway logs).
