4. For systems using the **Approved Agreement** path, an approved, in-scope written agreement is retained and linked to the ESR entry.
5. Audit evidence can be produced showing, for a sampled set of external systems, the assurance method used, the approval/review dates, and the linkage to the specific external-system activities and data types.


### ac-20.2 — Portable Storage Devices — Restricted Use (Enhancement)

#### Workflow-controlled encrypted USB use with pre/post scanning

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Months
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement a managed process and supporting technical enforcement so that organization-controlled portable storage devices (e.g., encrypted USB drives) may be used by authorized individuals **only** for **approved mission tasks** on **external systems with written authorization**, with the device **encrypted**, **malware-scanned immediately before and after** each use, **auto-run disabled**, and **copying prevented to unmanaged/removable media**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-20(2)** (Enhancement) requires: “Restrict the use of organization-controlled portable storage devices by authorized individuals on external systems using {{ insert: param, ac-20.02_odp }}.” The organization-defined parameter **ac-20.02_odp (restrictions)** specifies: use only for approved mission tasks; only on systems with written authorization; no copying to unmanaged media; encrypt devices; scan before/after use; disable auto-run.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Standardize and harden the portable devices (technical baseline)
- Select approved device models and ensure **encryption is enabled** (e.g., hardware-encrypted USB or OS-managed encryption with device-level protection).
- Ensure **auto-run/auto-play is disabled** on the device (set at device build time and verify via configuration evidence).
- Maintain a device inventory with serial numbers, encryption status, and build/config evidence.

### 2) Enforce “written authorization for external systems” and “approved mission tasks” via a single workflow
- Create an ITSM/secure portal workflow that captures, at minimum:
  - user identity
  - approved **mission task** reference
  - external system identifier (hostname/system ID)
  - **written authorization reference** (ticket/approval ID, document link, or signed authorization)
  - date/time window and expected duration
- The workflow should only release a device when all required fields are present and approvals are valid.

### 3) Require pre-use malware scanning before the device touches the external system
- Provide a hardened “checkout/scanning station” (or managed endpoint) that:
  - verifies the device is encrypted
  - performs a malware scan **before** the device is connected to the external system
  - records scan results (timestamp, scanner version, result status) to an auditable log
- Only after a clean scan should the workflow allow the user to proceed.

### 4) Require post-use malware scanning immediately after the external-system session
- Require the device to return to the scanning station immediately after use.
- Perform a malware scan **after** use and record results.
- If malware is detected, quarantine the device (block further workflow checkouts) and trigger incident/response per organizational procedure.

### 5) Prevent copying to unmanaged media (enforcement at the external-system boundary)
- Configure the **external systems** (or the session environment the device connects to) to prevent copying from the organization-controlled device to unmanaged/removable media.
  - Practical implementation options (choose what matches your environment):
    - restrict removable media classes and disable “write” to other removable devices during the session
    - enforce endpoint controls that block data transfer to unmanaged USB devices
    - if the external system is a managed jump host/session, ensure only the approved device is permitted and other removable media are blocked
- Document the external-system configuration standard and require it as part of the “written authorization” package.

### 6) Disable auto-run verification and evidence
- During device build and periodically (or at checkout), verify auto-run/auto-play is disabled and store evidence.

## WHO
- **IT Security / Compliance Owner**: defines the portable storage restrictions policy and acceptance criteria; approves external-system configuration standard.
- **IT Operations / Endpoint Engineering**: implements device hardening (encryption + auto-run disabled) and scanning station tooling.
- **Service Desk / ITSM Admin**: implements the checkout workflow and ensures required authorization/task fields are captured.
- **External System Owners**: implement the removable-media/data-transfer restrictions required for the session.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Workflow enforcement**: No device checkout is possible without (a) approved mission task reference and (b) written external-system authorization reference.
2. **Encryption**: Every checked-out device has recorded evidence of encryption enabled.
3. **Auto-run disabled**: Devices are configured with auto-run/auto-play disabled; evidence is retained.
4. **Pre-use scanning**: For each checkout/use event, a malware scan result exists with timestamp and scanner identity, recorded **before** connection to the external system.
5. **Post-use scanning**: For each return event, a malware scan result exists with timestamp and scanner identity, recorded **after** the external-system session.
6. **Quarantine on detection**: If a scan detects malware, the device is quarantined and cannot be checked out again until cleared by the security team.
7. **No unmanaged copying**: External systems used with the device are configured to prevent copying to unmanaged/removable media; configuration evidence is available for audit.
8. **Auditability**: Logs include user, device serial, external system identifier, authorization reference, mission task reference, scan results, and timestamps.

### ac-20.3 — Non-organizationally Owned Systems — Restricted Use (Enhancement)

#### Approval-gated external/non-owned system use with data-class limits

- **Category:** Manual
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Days
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an approval-gated process and technical enforcement that restricts use of **non-organizationally owned systems/components** (other organizations’ systems and personally owned devices) to **processing, storing, or transmitting organizational information** only under the organization-defined restrictions: **prior approval**, **approved security controls**, and **access limited to Confidential/Secret**; additionally, **personally owned devices are prohibited for Classified processing**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-20(3)** (Enhancement) requires: “Restrict the use of non-organizationally owned systems or system components to process, store, or transmit organizational information using {{ insert: param, ac-20.03_odp }}.” The organization-defined parameter **ac-20.03_odp (restrictions)** states: “Allowed only with prior approval, approved security controls, and access limited to Confidential/Secret data; personally owned devices prohibited for Classified processing.”

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define restricted categories and enforceable rules (policy + system mapping)
- Update the organization’s AC-20(3) procedure to explicitly define “non-organizationally owned systems/components” to include:
  - Other organizations’ systems/components (e.g., vendor/partner SaaS, contractor-managed platforms, third-party cloud accounts not under your tenant)
  - Personally owned devices (BYOD)
- Create an enforceable mapping from each category to required authorization artifacts:
  - **Prior approval required** before any connection/use is authorized
  - **Approved security controls required** (record which controls were approved)
  - **Data classification ceiling**: Confidential/Secret only
  - **BYOD rule**: personally owned devices cannot process Classified

### 2) Build an approval workflow that produces audit-ready authorization evidence
- Implement an ITSM/Service Request workflow (or extend an existing one) that must be completed **before** any user/system can connect to or use a non-owned system/component.
- Workflow fields must capture at minimum:
  - Requester, business owner, and system/component owner
  - Identity of the external/non-owned system/component (vendor, URL/account, device identifier if BYOD)
  - Purpose (what organizational information is processed/stored/transmitted)
  - Requested data classification (Confidential/Secret/Classified)
  - Connection method (API, browser, file transfer, remote access, etc.)
  - Evidence checklist for “approved security controls” (see step 3)
  - Explicit approval decision and approval authority
- Enforce hard rejects:
  - If requested data classification is **Classified**, deny unless the request is not BYOD and is explicitly approved under a separate, documented exception process (AC-20(3) enhancement specifically prohibits BYOD for Classified processing).
  - If the request involves **personally owned devices** and the requested classification includes **Classified**, deny.

### 3) Require “approved security controls” as a gate (not just a checkbox)
- In the workflow, require security review sign-off and attach/record evidence that the external/non-owned system/component meets organization-approved controls relevant to the connection and data handling.
- At minimum, require the reviewer to record:
  - Encryption in transit and at rest (where applicable)
  - Authentication strength (e.g., MFA) and account lifecycle controls
  - Least-privilege access model for organizational data
  - Logging/audit capability for access to organizational information
  - Vulnerability/patch posture expectations (where the organization can assess or contractually require)
  - Data handling constraints (retention/deletion/transfer controls)
- Store the approval record as the authorization evidence for audits.

### 4) Implement technical enforcement using identity/data access controls (policy-as-code)
- Configure the enterprise identity/data access layer so that access to external/non-owned systems is only granted when the workflow approval exists and the data classification ceiling is respected.
- Practical enforcement patterns (choose those that match your stack):
  - **Conditional access**: allow access to the external app/system only for approved users/groups tied to the approval record.
  - **Device restriction for BYOD**: deny access from personally owned devices for any application/workflow that is authorized for Confidential/Secret only if your organization requires managed devices; at minimum, ensure BYOD cannot be used for Classified processing by denying access to any Classified-labeled data flows.
  - **Data classification enforcement**: implement labeling/controls so that Confidential/Secret data can be accessed, but Classified-labeled data cannot be exported/transmitted to the non-owned system.
- Ensure the enforcement is revocable: when approval expires or is withdrawn, access is automatically removed.

### 5) Bind agreements/terms to the authorization record
- For each approved external/non-owned system/component, ensure the authorization record references the executed agreement/terms (e.g., vendor contract clauses) that support the approved security controls and data handling restrictions.
- For personally owned devices, require explicit user acknowledgment of restrictions and incident/forensic cooperation expectations (coordinate with legal as needed).

## WHO
- **Information Security (or Security Governance)**: owns the approval criteria, security control approval, and audit evidence requirements.
- **ITSM/Service Desk (Process Owner)**: implements and maintains the request workflow and required fields.
- **Application/System Owner**: provides technical details of the connection and confirms data classification usage.
- **Identity & Access Management (IAM) team**: implements conditional access and data/classification enforcement.
- **Legal/OGC (as needed)**: reviews legal terms for personally owned devices and external system usage.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For at least one pilot external/non-owned system/component and one BYOD scenario, no connection/use occurs unless an approval record exists (workflow submission + security sign-off).
2. The approval record includes:
   - Prior approval decision
   - Recorded “approved security controls” evidence
   - Data classification ceiling (Confidential/Secret)
   - Explicit BYOD prohibition for Classified processing
3. Technical enforcement is demonstrated:
   - Access to the external system is denied when approval is missing/expired.
   - BYOD cannot be used for Classified processing (attempts are blocked and logged).
4. Audit evidence is retrievable:
   - SIEM/IdP logs show who accessed the external/non-owned system and when, and can be correlated to the approval record.
5. Documented procedure exists and is communicated to relevant teams (ITSM, system owners, IAM, security reviewers).

### ac-20.4 — Network Accessible Storage Devices — Prohibited Use (Enhancement)

#### Block prohibited external network storage endpoints via registry+config

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Prohibit use of **all network-accessible storage devices** in **external systems** (including **public, hybrid, or community cloud online storage**) by enforcing a hard technical ban on storage endpoints/shares and maintaining auditable evidence that the prohibited targets were not used.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-20(4)** (Enhancement) requires: **“Prohibit the use of {{ insert: param, ac-20.04_odp }} in external systems.”** The guidance clarifies that network-accessible storage devices in external systems include **online storage devices in public, hybrid, or community cloud-based systems**. Your organization-defined parameter **ac-20.04_odp** is: **“all network-accessible storage devices (NAS, SAN, SMB/NFS shares, object storage endpoints) in external systems.”**

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Create/maintain a Prohibited Storage Endpoint Registry (policy artifact)
- Maintain an authoritative list of prohibited storage targets relevant to the application environment:
  - NAS/SAN: hostnames/IPs, storage array identifiers, export names
  - SMB/NFS: server FQDNs, share paths, export paths
  - Object storage: bucket/container names and endpoint URLs
- Include: owner, approval status, last-updated date, and change ticket reference.
- Ensure the registry explicitly covers **public/hybrid/community cloud online storage endpoints**.

### 2) Enforce the ban in the application’s and platform’s configuration (technical guardrails)
Implement deny-by-default controls so prohibited storage endpoints/shares cannot be used:
- **Egress/network controls**: configure firewall/security group/egress filtering for the application tiers and admin tooling so connections to prohibited storage endpoints are denied.
- **Protocol controls** (where applicable): block or restrict mounting/usage of **SMB/NFS** from application/workload networks unless the destination is explicitly approved (exceptions must be rare and time-bound).
- **Object storage controls**: restrict IAM/service-account permissions so workloads cannot call object storage APIs for non-approved buckets/containers; deny access to prohibited endpoints.
- **Mount/connector controls**: if the application supports user-driven connectors (e.g., “connect to external storage”), disable or remove those features for external systems, or enforce allow-listing that excludes prohibited endpoints.

### 3) Integrate enforcement with the registry (automation)
- Use automation (e.g., policy-as-code, configuration management, or infrastructure-as-code pipelines) to translate the prohibited registry into:
  - firewall/egress rules
  - IAM policy constraints
  - application connector allow/deny lists
- Ensure updates to the registry propagate to enforcement within a defined SLA (e.g., same release window).

### 4) Produce audit evidence (demonstrate non-use)
- Configure logging for:
  - denied/blocked network attempts to prohibited storage endpoints
  - successful storage connection attempts (should be zero for prohibited targets)
  - object storage API calls and authorization denials
  - mount attempts (SMB/NFS) and failures
- In SIEM, generate periodic evidence reports that:
  - cross-reference logs against the prohibited registry
  - show no successful access to prohibited targets (and/or show only denied attempts)

## WHO
- **Application Owner / System Owner**: accountable for the prohibition scope and ensuring the application/platform is configured accordingly.
- **Cloud/Infrastructure Engineer**: implements egress/network and IAM enforcement.
- **Security/Compliance Analyst**: maintains the prohibited storage registry governance and validates audit evidence.
- **SIEM/Monitoring Engineer**: ensures logs and correlation rules produce audit-ready reports.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. A current **Prohibited Storage Endpoint Registry** exists and includes **NAS, SAN, SMB/NFS shares, and object storage endpoints** for **external systems**, explicitly covering **public/hybrid/community cloud online storage**.
2. For the application’s production (and other in-scope) environments, enforcement is in place such that:
   - connections to prohibited storage endpoints are **denied** at the network and/or IAM layer
   - SMB/NFS mounts to prohibited shares are blocked (or not possible)
   - object storage access to prohibited buckets/containers is blocked (authorization denied)
3. Audit evidence is generated:
   - SIEM reports show **no successful access** to prohibited targets during the reporting period
   - denied attempts (if any) are logged and attributable to the prohibited registry entries
4. Registry changes propagate to enforcement within the defined SLA and are traceable to change tickets.


### ac-20.5 — Portable Storage Devices — Prohibited Use (Enhancement)

#### Deny org-controlled USB use on external systems via endpoint policy

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Days
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement a **complete technical prohibition** on using **organization-controlled portable storage devices** (e.g., managed USB drives) by authorized individuals on **external systems**, and back it with **process-based enforcement** for any approved exceptions.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-20(5)** (Enhancement) requires: **“Prohibit the use of organization-controlled portable storage devices by authorized individuals on external systems.”** Guidance states this prohibition must be **complete** and **enforced using technical methods and/or nontechnical methods**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define scope: what counts as an “external system”
- Create/maintain an access-control definition used by endpoint and network enforcement, e.g.:
  - Any system not owned/managed by the organization (partner/customer/contractor/vendor environments)
  - Any system reached via partner networks, customer sites, or unmanaged VPN/remote access contexts
  - Any non-corporate managed endpoint group (including contractor-owned devices)
- Publish this definition in the organization’s portable media policy and reference it from the application’s security procedures.

### 2) Technical enforcement on endpoints used to access external systems
- For all organization-managed endpoints that can reach external systems (employee laptops, contractor laptops under org management, admin jump hosts used for external access):
  - **Disable/deny USB mass storage and removable media** by default using centralized endpoint management.
  - Where feasible, implement **conditional enforcement** so the deny applies when the endpoint is in an “external access” posture (e.g., connected to external networks, using external-access VPN profiles, or targeting external system categories).
- Implement device-control rules that specifically prevent **USB mass storage** (and other removable storage categories) from being used.
- Ensure the rule is applied consistently across **production/test/admin** endpoint groups where external access could occur.

### 3) Enforce “organization-controlled portable storage” prohibition
- If the organization issues managed USB devices:
  - Configure endpoint policy so those devices are **not usable for external-system access**.
  - If the endpoint platform supports it, use allow/deny logic tied to device identifiers/ownership status (managed device vs. unmanaged) to ensure the prohibition targets the organization-controlled devices.
- Provide an approved alternative for any required data movement (e.g., secure enterprise transfer tooling, encrypted cloud transfer, or approved secure file transfer service) and ensure those alternatives are permitted.

### 4) Logging and audit evidence
- Enable endpoint logs for:
  - USB/removable media connection attempts
  - Deny/block outcomes
  - User identity and endpoint identity
  - Timestamp and target context (where available)
- Forward events to SIEM and retain per enterprise log retention requirements.
- Produce periodic audit extracts showing the deny rule is active and that blocks are occurring (or that exceptions are handled via the approved process).

### 5) Process-based enforcement for exceptions (when technical blocking is incomplete)
- Create a documented exception workflow:
  - Require pre-approval by Information Security (and data owner for sensitive data)
  - Require justification and approved transfer method
  - Require compensating controls (e.g., malware scanning, encryption, time-bounded approval)
- Train authorized users that **USB insertion into external systems is prohibited** and that approved transfer methods must be used instead.

## WHO
- **Information Security Officer / GRC**: owns the “external system” definition, portable media policy, and exception workflow.
- **Endpoint Management Administrator (IT)**: implements and maintains the device-control/deny policies and compliance reporting.
- **Application/System Owner**: ensures the application’s operational procedures reference the portable media prohibition for external access workflows.
- **SIEM/Monitoring Administrator**: ensures logs are collected, normalized, and retained for audit.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. A published definition of **“external system”** exists and is referenced in the portable media policy/procedures.
2. Endpoint management shows a **deny configuration** for USB mass storage/removable media that prevents use on endpoints used for external access.
3. For organization-controlled managed USB devices, the configuration prevents their use on endpoints when accessing external systems (or provides an auditable exception path).
4. SIEM contains events for USB connection attempts and deny/block outcomes including **user identity** and **endpoint identity**.
5. An audit report can be generated demonstrating the deny policy is enabled and that blocked attempts (or approved exceptions) are recorded.


### ac-21 — Information Sharing (Control)

#### AC-21 Sharing workflow with access-match, NDA/SAP prompts, audit trail

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an application-integrated “information sharing request” workflow that (1) binds each shared item to machine-readable data classification tags and required access/use restrictions, (2) performs an automated access-match check between the item’s required restrictions and the selected sharing partner’s authorizations/eligibility, and (3) enforces mandatory user prompts/validation when NDA-governed and/or SAP/compartment-governed sharing is required. The workflow must record outcomes, automated-check results, prompt completion, and (when user discretion is allowed) the user’s rationale.

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-21 requires that information sharing applies to restricted information and that sharing decisions are supported by defined circumstances requiring user discretion and by automated mechanisms/manual processes that assist users in making information-sharing and collaboration decisions. The guidance further specifies that sharing decisions must consider whether access authorizations assigned to a sharing partner match the information’s access and use restrictions, and that automated assistance may use information flow techniques/security attributes to support correct decisions.

This solution directly implements the organization-defined parameters:
- **ac-21_odp.01**: define circumstances where user discretion is required to determine whether partner authorizations match the information’s access/use restrictions (including classified/contract-sensitive, SAP/compartment, NDA).
- **ac-21_odp.02**: define automated mechanisms/manual processes that assist users in making information-sharing/collaboration decisions (policy-based guidance using classification tags, automated access checks, and required NDA/SAP/compartment validation prompts).

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the information-to-restriction mapping (policy-as-data)
- Create a configuration artifact in the application (or connected policy service) that maps **data classification tags** to:
  - required allowed actions (e.g., view/edit/download)
  - required partner eligibility attributes (e.g., NDA required = true/false)
  - required SAP/compartment identifiers (e.g., compartment IDs, special access program IDs)
  - any additional access/use restrictions (e.g., purpose limitation)
- Ensure the mapping is versioned and change-controlled.

### 2) Bind each shareable item to tags and required restrictions
- Enforce that information items (documents/records/objects) have machine-readable classification tags and restriction attributes at creation/ingestion.
- If the application already uses metadata/DLP/classification services, integrate by consuming those tags; otherwise, implement tagging at the point where the item enters the application.

### 3) Integrate partner eligibility and authorizations
- Implement (or integrate with) a **partner directory** that represents sharing partners at the required granularity (individual/group/organization).
- For each partner, store/derive:
  - NDA eligibility/coverage status (e.g., NDA agreement ID(s) and validity)
  - SAP/compartment authorization status (e.g., allowed compartment IDs)
  - general authorization entitlements (e.g., IAM roles/entitlements) used for the access-match check.
- Source authorizations from enterprise IAM/entitlement systems and contract/NDA repositories where available.

### 4) Build the sharing request workflow in the application
- Add a “Share” action that creates a **sharing request** record containing:
  - item identifier
  - item classification tags and derived required restrictions (snapshotted at request time)
  - selected sharing partner
  - requested access type(s)
  - purpose/use case
- The workflow must run an automated **access-match check** before allowing approval/dispatch.

### 5) Implement automated access-match logic (policy-as-code)
- Automated check must verify that:
  - the partner is eligible for the item’s required restrictions (not merely that the partner has some generic access)
  - requested access type is within the item’s allowed actions for that classification
  - NDA requirement is satisfied when required by tags (e.g., NDA agreement ID present and valid)
  - SAP/compartment requirement is satisfied when required by tags (e.g., partner authorized for the specific compartment/program)
- If any required restriction is not satisfied, block the request and present a clear reason.

### 6) Enforce mandatory prompts/validation for NDA and SAP/compartment
- When tags indicate NDA-governed or SAP/compartment-governed sharing, require the user to complete mandatory validations before submission/approval:
  - NDA prompt: confirm the correct NDA agreement ID/coverage for the partner and purpose (or select from eligible NDA records)
  - SAP/compartment prompt: confirm the correct compartment/program authorization scope
- The workflow must not proceed until prompts are completed.

### 7) Support user discretion only in defined circumstances, with recorded rationale
- Implement the organization-defined discretion circumstances (**ac-21_odp.01**) as explicit workflow branches (e.g., “exception review required”).
- When discretion is invoked:
  - require the user to provide rationale and reference the specific restriction(s) considered
  - require an approval step by an authorized decision-maker (role-based) if your organization’s process requires it
  - record the rationale and decision outcome in the audit log.

### 8) Generate audit-ready evidence
- Log and retain (per enterprise logging/retention policy) at minimum:
  - request metadata (who, when, item, partner, requested access, purpose)
  - derived required restrictions from tags
  - automated access-match results (pass/fail and which checks failed)
  - NDA/SAP/compartment prompt completion status and selected agreement/compartment identifiers
  - any user discretion rationale and approver identity

## WHO
- **Application Owner / Product Owner**: owns workflow requirements and user experience.
- **Security Architect / Compliance Engineer**: defines the classification-to-restriction mapping and discretion circumstances.
- **IAM/Contracts Integration Owner**: ensures partner eligibility, NDA, and SAP/compartment authorization data are available and accurate.
- **Software Engineers**: implement workflow, policy-as-code checks, and audit logging.
- **Security Operations / Audit Liaison**: validates evidence completeness and retention.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For an item tagged as **contract-sensitive/NDA-governed**, a share request cannot be approved unless the NDA validation prompt is completed with an eligible/valid NDA agreement ID for the selected partner.
2. For an item tagged as **SAP/compartment-governed**, a share request cannot be approved unless the SAP/compartment prompt confirms partner authorization for the specific compartment/program required by the item tags.
3. The automated access-match check uses the **item’s required restrictions** (derived from tags) and fails when partner authorizations do not match those required restrictions.
4. All share requests produce audit records containing: request metadata, derived required restrictions, automated-check results, prompt completion status, and (if discretion is used) user rationale and approver identity.
5. Discretion is only available in the explicitly configured circumstances (**ac-21_odp.01**), and rationale is mandatory when discretion is invoked.


### ac-21.1 — Automated Decision Support (Enhancement)

#### Automated policy-gated sharing workflow using partner + data restrictions

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an automated, policy-driven workflow/approval gate that enforces information-sharing decisions by authorized users. A sharing request must be evaluated against:
1) the sharing partner’s current access authorizations, and
2) the specific access restrictions attached to the information being shared.
The workflow must prevent bypass (no direct activation of sharing without passing the automated checks) and must generate system-generated decision records for audit.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 AC-21(1) enhancement requires: “Employ {{ insert: param, ac-21.01_odp }} to enforce information-sharing decisions by authorized users based on access authorizations of sharing partners and access restrictions on information to be shared.” The guidance states automated mechanisms are used to enforce information sharing decisions.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the policy inputs (authoritative, system-resident)
- **Information access restrictions catalog**: Create a system-managed mapping from each shareable data/object type (and/or data classification label) to explicit restrictions (e.g., allowed recipient partner types, required approval level, allowed purposes, expiry, and any additional constraints).
- **Sharing partner authorization catalog**: Create a system-managed mapping of each sharing partner identity (external org, vendor tenant, service principal, etc.) to what they are authorized to receive (by data category/object type and/or restriction class).
- **Decision-maker authorization**: Define which authenticated users are allowed to initiate and/or approve sharing decisions (e.g., IdP groups/roles such as “Sharing Requester” and “Sharing Approver”).

### 2) Implement the automated decision support workflow
- Treat “share” as an **access grant request** that is **inactive** until policy evaluation succeeds.
- Add an application/service workflow endpoint (or integrate with an enterprise access request workflow engine) that performs, in order:
  1. **Requester/approver authorization check**: confirm the user is in the decision-maker role(s).
  2. **Partner authorization check**: verify the target partner is authorized for the requested information category/object type.
  3. **Information restriction check**: verify the requested sharing parameters satisfy the information’s access restrictions (e.g., classification-based rules, required approvals, time limits, purpose constraints).
  4. **Outcome determination**: allow/block and, if required by policy, route to the correct approver tier.
- Ensure the workflow is the **only** path that can activate sharing (disable/guard direct “grant access” actions for non-workflow paths; enforce server-side checks for all API/UI actions).

### 3) Enforce no-bypass controls
- Implement server-side enforcement so that even if a user attempts to call an internal API or UI action directly, the system refuses activation unless the request has a successful workflow decision record.
- Use least-privilege service accounts for the workflow engine; sharing activation should be performed only by the workflow component after approval.

### 4) Generate decision records (audit-ready)
For every sharing decision, record a system-generated decision object including at minimum:
- request ID, requester identity, approver identity (if applicable)
- partner identity
- information/object identifier and restriction class
- which policy rules were evaluated (rule IDs/version)
- evaluation results for partner authorization and information restrictions
- final decision (allow/deny) and timestamp
- any required approvals obtained

### 5) Operationalize policy changes
- Store policy/rules in a versioned, change-controlled repository (policy-as-code or equivalent) and ensure the workflow evaluates the **current** policy version.
- Document the enforcement logic and evidence generation so auditors can trace “decision → evaluated inputs → outcome.”

## WHO
- **Application Security Architect / IAM Architect**: designs the policy model, decision-maker roles, and enforcement points.
- **Application Owner / Backend Engineers**: implement workflow enforcement and decision record generation.
- **IAM/Access Governance Team**: maintains partner authorization catalog and decision-maker role assignments.
- **Compliance/Audit Liaison**: validates audit evidence sufficiency and documentation.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Authorized decision enforcement**: A user not in the decision-maker roles cannot initiate or approve sharing; attempts are denied server-side.
2. **Partner-based enforcement**: If the partner is not authorized for the requested information category/object type, the workflow denies sharing.
3. **Information restriction enforcement**: If the requested sharing parameters violate the information’s access restrictions, the workflow denies sharing.
4. **No bypass**: Direct activation of sharing (via UI/API/admin action) fails unless a successful workflow decision record exists.
5. **Decision records**: Every allow/deny decision produces a system-generated decision record containing evaluated inputs and policy rule/version identifiers.
6. **Audit traceability**: Given a decision record, an auditor can identify requester, partner, information restriction class, evaluated rules, and final outcome.


### ac-21.2 — Information Search and Retrieval (Enhancement)

#### ABAC policy-as-code to filter Secret/Confidential search results

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement information search and retrieval services that enforce **information-sharing restrictions** for Secret/Confidential data by filtering results at query-time based on:
- **User authorization** (who is allowed to receive results)
- **Approved data-sharing boundaries** (where/for which programme/customer/country/partner the data may be shared)
- **Export-control and CMMC constraints** (ITAR/EAR and CMMC-L2/L3 requirements)

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST **AC-21(2)** (Enhancement) requires: “Implement information search and retrieval services that enforce {{ param, ac-21.02_odp }}.” The parameter **ac-21.02_odp** specifies that **information-sharing restrictions** are defined and must be enforced by the search/retrieval services. This enhancement is intended to ensure relevant resources are returned only when the request is within approved sharing boundaries and the user is authorized.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the authoritative restriction model (data + sharing boundaries)
- For every searchable item (document/record), ensure metadata exists for at least:
  - Classification: Secret/Confidential (and any subcategories used internally)
  - ITAR/EAR tags (e.g., ECCN/USML mapping or equivalent internal tags)
  - Required CMMC level (L2 vs L3) for the item/recipient context
  - Sharing boundary attributes (e.g., programme/customer/partner, permitted country/region, approved recipient group)
- Store this metadata in a system that the search service can query at enforcement time (e.g., alongside the index documents or via a metadata lookup service).

### 2) Define the authoritative user/recipient authorization model
- For each user (employee/contractor/partner/service account), ensure the identity system provides attributes used for enforcement:
  - Authorization/clearance/role mapping to allowed data categories
  - Approved programmes/partner relationships
  - Permitted countries/regions for receiving the data
  - CMMC status/eligibility for external recipients (where applicable)
- Ensure identity assurance is strong enough for enforcement decisions (use enterprise IdP claims; avoid unauthenticated/weakly assured identities).

### 3) Implement ABAC policy-as-code for search enforcement
- Create policy-as-code rules (versioned, reviewed, and deployed via change management) that evaluate, for each candidate item, whether it may be returned for the current requester.
- Policy decision logic must enforce **ac-21.02_odp** by requiring both:
  - **User is authorized** to receive the item’s classification and compliance category
  - **Request is within approved sharing boundaries** matching the item’s boundary attributes
- Include explicit checks for:
  - ITAR/EAR constraints for Secret/Confidential results
  - CMMC-L2/L3 constraints for Secret/Confidential results

### 4) Enforce at query-time and result-time in the search service
- Integrate the policy decision point with the search service so that filtering occurs before results are returned.
- Practical implementation pattern:
  - During indexing, include enforcement-relevant metadata fields in the search index (or store item IDs + metadata for a fast lookup).
  - At query-time, translate the ABAC decision into search filters (or a two-stage approach: candidate retrieval → policy evaluation → final result set).
- Ensure that any downstream actions from search results (e.g., preview, download, API retrieval) re-check the same enforcement decision or inherit the same authorization context.

### 5) Maintain an auditable “restriction list” derived from policy + metadata
- Generate and store a system-held restriction/enforcement dataset (e.g., compiled policy rules and/or effective allowed/blocked mappings) used by the search service.
- This restriction list must be derived from the authoritative metadata and policy definitions so enforcement is consistent and reviewable.

### 6) Log enforcement outcomes for auditability
- For each search request involving Secret/Confidential content, log at minimum:
  - Requestor identity (user ID/service account), authentication context
  - Query parameters (or a safe representation)
  - Item identifiers returned vs withheld
  - Enforcement decision outcome and reason code (e.g., “withheld: boundary mismatch”, “withheld: ITAR/EAR not permitted”, “withheld: CMMC-L2/L3 not satisfied”)
- Forward logs to SIEM and retain per enterprise logging/retention requirements.

### 7) Test with negative cases and boundary probing
- Validate that unauthorized users cannot infer restricted content via search result counts, previews, or metadata leakage.
- Include tests for:
  - Boundary mismatch (wrong programme/customer/country/partner)
  - ITAR/EAR mismatch
  - CMMC-L2 vs L3 mismatch
  - Role/clearance mismatch

## WHO
- **Application Owner / Engineering Lead**: implement ABAC enforcement integration in the search service and ensure consistent enforcement across preview/download/API.
- **Information Security / Compliance (Export Control & CMMC owner)**: define and approve the authoritative sharing boundary rules and compliance mappings.
- **Identity & Access Management (IAM) team**: provision required user/recipient attributes and ensure reliable identity claims.
- **Security Operations / SIEM admin**: configure log pipelines, retention, and alerting for repeated boundary probing.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For Secret/Confidential items, the search service returns **only** items where ABAC policy evaluation confirms:
   - requester authorization AND
   - approved sharing boundary match AND
   - ITAR/EAR and CMMC-L2/L3 constraints are satisfied.
2. For any withheld item, the system records an audit event with a **reason code** indicating which restriction failed (boundary vs ITAR/EAR vs CMMC).
3. Negative tests confirm that users outside approved boundaries cannot obtain restricted items via:
   - search results
   - previews
   - downloads
   - API retrieval
4. Policies are versioned and deployed through change management; enforcement behavior is reproducible from the logged policy version.
5. Audit logs are ingested into SIEM and retained per organizational requirements, and can be used to demonstrate enforcement outcomes for a given search request.

### ac-22 — Publicly Accessible Content (Control)

#### RBAC publishing workflow with approval gates and daily review

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement a controlled workflow for any **publicly accessible content** so that:
1) Only **authorised and trained individuals** can publish to public-facing systems.
2) Every item is **reviewed before it becomes public** with recorded evidence.
3) Public-facing content is **reviewed daily** for non-public information with recorded evidence.
4) Any discovered non-public information is **removed promptly** with recorded remediation details.

## WHY (control requirement)
AC-22 requires managing publicly accessible content to ensure the public does not gain access to **non-public information** (including protected and proprietary information). The guidance specifies that publicly accessible content is typically accessible without identification/authentication and that the organization must manage **who can make content public** and ensure **pre- and post-publication checks** (including the organization-defined review frequency; default is **daily**).

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define scope and system boundaries
- Identify all application components that are **publicly accessible** (e.g., marketing site pages, public downloads, public knowledge base, public landing pages, public API documentation portals, app-store listing pages if hosted by the app).
- Exclude non-organizational public platforms (covered by policy) and focus on systems controlled by the organization.

### 2) Implement an authorised publisher list (source of truth)
- Maintain a current list of authorised publishers including: user identity, role, and **last training/attestation date**.
- Make this list the authoritative input to CMS/web platform permissions.

### 3) Enforce technical publishing gates (RBAC + workflow)
- Configure the CMS/web platform (or publishing portal) with RBAC:
  - **Publishers**: can create drafts and submit for review.
  - **Approvers/Reviewers**: can review and approve.
  - **No direct publish** permission for publishers to production/public endpoints.
- Require an **approval gate** before content can be published:
  - Publishing to production must be only possible via an approval action that references an approval record (e.g., ticket ID, checklist completion record, or sign-off).

### 4) Pre-publication review checklist (mandatory)
- Create a standard checklist that reviewers must complete before approving publication. Include checks for common non-public items such as:
  - personal data not intended for public release
  - internal documents or confidential contract terms
  - credentials/secrets
  - system/network details that should not be public
  - incident details not cleared for release
  - proprietary information / non-public IP references
- Make checklist completion a **required field** in the workflow so evidence is captured.

### 5) Daily post-publication review (frequency = daily)
- Assign a defined reviewer role to perform a **daily review** of public-facing content.
- Use a repeatable daily checklist and record evidence in a ticketing system or GRC log.
- Review at minimum: newly published items since last review and high-risk sections (e.g., “Downloads”, “News/Updates”, “Latest”, public FAQs).

### 6) Prompt removal and remediation evidence
- When non-public information is found:
  - immediately remove the content (or roll back to the last known-good version)
  - open a remediation record documenting: what was removed, where it was located, timestamp, and who performed the action
  - capture the root cause (e.g., checklist failure, misunderstanding of classification) and corrective action.

### 7) Validate authorised access and training currency
- Periodically (e.g., monthly) validate that the authorised publisher list matches actual CMS permissions and that training/attestation is current.
- Remove access promptly when individuals leave the role.

## WHO
- **Application Owner / Web Platform Owner**: owns scope definition and workflow configuration.
- **GRC/Compliance or Security Governance**: owns the AC-22 checklist template, evidence requirements, and review cadence.
- **CMS/Web Administrators**: implement RBAC, workflow gates, and required evidence fields.
- **Authorised Publishers**: submit drafts and complete required submission steps.
- **Approvers/Reviewers**: perform pre-publication review and daily post-publication review.
- **Incident/Content Remediation Lead (as defined by org)**: ensures prompt removal and remediation record completion.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1) **RBAC enforcement**: publishers cannot publish directly to production/public endpoints; only approvers can publish.
2) **Pre-publication evidence**: every published item has an associated approval record (ticket/checklist/sign-off) with timestamp and approver identity.
3) **Daily review evidence**: daily review logs exist for the defined review period and include reviewer identity, date, and checklist results.
4) **Removal evidence**: for any identified non-public content, the system shows prompt removal/rollback and a remediation record with what/where/when/who.
5) **Authorised list control**: only identities on the authorised publisher list have publisher permissions, and the list is kept current with training/attestation dates.


### ac-23 — Data Mining Protection (Control)

#### Protected-data query gateway with throttling, scope limits, and alerts

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Months
- **Confidence:** 82%

## WHAT
Implement a centralized “query control plane” (gateway/service layer) that mediates all queries and analytics requests against **protected database records and fields** (Confidential/Secret). The gateway must:
- Enforce **rate limiting and query throttling** per identity and per protected object
- Enforce **least-privilege query controls** (deny/rewrite queries that request unauthorized fields/rows or broaden scope)
- **Detect and alert** on atypical query patterns consistent with data mining
- Where feasible, route analytics to **differential-privacy (DP) enabled** query templates/endpoints
- Produce **audit evidence** (allowed/denied/throttled decisions and query telemetry)

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-23 Data Mining Protection** requires employing the organization-defined **techniques** for the organization-defined **data storage objects** to detect and protect against unauthorized data mining. The guidance explicitly calls out techniques such as **limiting number/frequency of database queries**, **limiting types of responses**, **least-privilege query controls**, and **notifying personnel when atypical database queries or accesses occur**. It also notes DP/homomorphic encryption as feasible data mining protection techniques.

This solution directly implements the required techniques for the specified protected objects: **database records and database fields containing Confidential and Secret data**.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Build the protected-data mapping (object-to-policy)
- Create a configuration-driven catalogue mapping:
  - Database **tables/collections** and **columns/fields** that contain Confidential/Secret data
  - The allowed query/analysis patterns for each protected object (e.g., permitted filters, required predicates, allowed aggregations)
- Store this mapping as policy-as-code (e.g., versioned config) so it can be audited.

### 2) Route all protected-data access through the gateway
- Modify application/reporting paths so that any request that could touch protected objects must call the gateway/service layer.
- Block direct database access paths for non-admin roles where feasible (enforce via network rules and/or database permissions).

### 3) Enforce least-privilege at query time
In the gateway, implement an allowlist model for query “shape” and scope:
- Deny or rewrite queries that:
  - Request unauthorized columns/fields
  - Omit required predicates (e.g., tenant/customer scoping)
  - Attempt to broaden row scope beyond what is authorized
  - Request high-cardinality outputs that enable extraction (e.g., unbounded distinct values)
- Enforce row/field-level constraints based on identity attributes/roles.

### 4) Apply rate limiting and query throttling
Implement throttles keyed on:
- Identity (user/service account)
- Protected object(s) targeted (table/column groups)
- Query shape category (e.g., aggregation vs raw record retrieval)

Use two tiers of limits:
- Interactive/user limits (lower thresholds for repeated access)
- Automated/service limits (separate thresholds and stricter controls for protected fields)

When limits are exceeded:
- Throttle (delay) or deny with a controlled error response
- Record the event for investigation

### 5) Detect atypical mining-like behavior and alert
- Emit structured telemetry for every protected-data query decision:
  - identity, timestamp, targeted protected objects, query shape hash, estimated result cardinality, allowed/denied/throttled outcome
- Establish baselines (per identity and per protected object) and alert on deviations such as:
  - Unusual query frequency
  - Repeated access to many protected fields
  - High-cardinality extraction attempts
  - Sudden changes in query shape
- Send alerts to the SOC/incident workflow (SIEM/SOAR) with enough context to investigate.

### 6) Differential privacy where feasible
For analytics/reporting use-cases that return aggregates over protected fields:
- Prefer DP-enabled query templates/endpoints (e.g., DP-wrapped stored procedures or DP analytics service)
- Ensure the gateway only returns DP-compliant outputs for protected fields when DP is enabled for that use-case.
- If DP is not feasible for a specific query type, document the technical rationale and ensure other mining protections (throttling/scope limits/response limiting) are enforced.

### 7) Generate audit-ready evidence
- Log every gateway decision (allowed/denied/throttled) and the policy version used.
- Retain logs according to enterprise logging/retention requirements.

## WHO
- **Application/Data Platform Owner**: ensures all protected-data access is routed through the gateway
- **Security Architect / IAM Engineer**: defines identity-to-policy mapping and least-privilege enforcement model
- **Database Administrator / Data Engineer**: maintains protected-data catalogue and DP-enabled query templates where feasible
- **SOC Analyst / Incident Response Lead**: triages alerts and tunes detection thresholds

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Protected object coverage**: For all configured Confidential/Secret database fields/records, requests are mediated by the gateway (no direct query path for non-admin roles).
2. **Least-privilege enforcement**: Queries attempting to access unauthorized fields/rows are denied or rewritten; evidence shows correct policy decisions.
3. **Throttling effectiveness**: Repeated queries against the same protected objects by the same identity trigger throttling/denial at configured thresholds; evidence includes telemetry and outcomes.
4. **Atypical detection**: At least one test scenario (e.g., scripted high-frequency query pattern) generates an alert in SIEM/SOAR with query context.
5. **Audit evidence**: For allowed/denied/throttled requests, logs include identity, targeted protected objects, query shape, decision outcome, and policy version.
6. **DP where feasible**: For at least one analytics use-case over protected fields, the gateway returns DP-compliant outputs (or documented technical rationale exists for any non-DP use-case).

### ac-24 — Access Control Decisions (Control)

#### Enforce decision-before-access via PDP/PEP and audit evidence

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement an authorization decision flow where **for every access request**, the system obtains an **access control decision** and applies it **before any access enforcement** (i.e., before content is returned, business logic executes, or privileged actions succeed). Ensure the decision outcome is **auditable per request**.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-24: Access Control Decisions** requires that **access control decisions are applied to each access request prior to access enforcement** (ac-24_odp.01 and ac-24_odp.02). This prevents enforcement from occurring without a validated authorization decision.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the decision contract (inputs/outputs)
- Create a documented **authorization decision contract** used by all enforcement points.
- Decision inputs must include at minimum: subject identity (user/service account), requested action, target resource, and relevant context (e.g., environment, tenant, device/workload claims as applicable).
- Decision output must be explicit: **Allow/Deny** plus (at least) a reason code and a decision identifier.

### 2) Implement a Policy Decision Point (PDP)
- Deploy a PDP (e.g., policy engine or policy service) that evaluates authorization policies for each request.
- Ensure the PDP is invoked **synchronously** (or via a request-time decision mechanism) so the enforcement point cannot proceed without a decision.
- Store policies as code with versioning and change control.

### 3) Implement enforcement points (PEPs) at every access path
- Identify all access enforcement paths in the application, including:
  - Web/API endpoints (including admin endpoints)
  - Background jobs that act on behalf of users (if they represent access requests)
  - Data access layers that serve data (e.g., repository/service methods)
  - Any privileged operations (e.g., configuration changes, exports, user management)
- For each path, implement a PEP that:
  - Calls the PDP for the specific request
  - **Blocks by default**
  - Proceeds only when PDP returns **Allow**
  - Returns a consistent denial response when PDP returns **Deny**

### 4) Guarantee “decision-before-enforcement” in code and middleware
- Add middleware/interceptors/guards so that the request pipeline performs:
  1) Build decision inputs
  2) Call PDP
  3) Enforce decision (allow/deny)
  4) Only then execute business logic / return data / perform the action
- Add a hard requirement in the enforcement layer that **no success path** (including partial responses) occurs before the PDP decision is received.

### 5) Record audit evidence per access request
- Extend logging/auditing so that each access request produces an auditable record containing:
  - Request identifier (correlation ID)
  - Subject
  - Resource and action
  - PDP decision outcome (Allow/Deny)
  - PDP decision identifier/version (policy version)
  - Enforcement outcome (e.g., request blocked/served)
- Send logs to the enterprise SIEM/central logging platform.

### 6) Add automated verification tests
- Implement integration tests that assert the sequence:
  - PDP is called for each request
  - Enforcement does not occur when PDP returns Deny
  - Audit record includes the decision outcome and correlates to the request
- Include tests for both standard and administrative functions.

## WHO
- **Application Security Engineer / IAM Engineer**: define decision contract, PDP/PEP design, policy model.
- **Backend/Platform Engineers**: implement PEP middleware/guards and PDP integration across all access paths.
- **DevOps/SRE**: configure logging, correlation IDs, and SIEM forwarding.
- **QA/Test Engineer**: implement and maintain automated sequence and audit evidence tests.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. For every identified access path (web/API/admin/data operations), the enforcement layer performs a PDP decision **before** executing the action or returning data.
2. When PDP returns **Deny**, the system does not enforce access (no data returned; no privileged action executed).
3. Each access request generates an audit record that includes the **PDP decision outcome** and correlates to the request identifier.
4. Automated tests exist and pass for both Allow and Deny scenarios, including at least one administrative/privileged endpoint.
5. Policies are versioned and the audit record includes the policy decision identifier/version (or an equivalent traceable reference).

### ac-24.1 — Transmit Access Authorization Information (Enhancement)

#### Secure signed authorization tokens over mTLS to API enforcement

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 78%

## WHAT
Implement a secure, verifiable transmission of **access authorization information** (token) from the authorization decision point to the **federated application/API enforcement points** that enforce access control decisions.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-24(1)** requires that **{{ac-24.01_odp.01}}** be transmitted using **{{ac-24.01_odp.02}}** to **{{ac-24.01_odp.03}}** such that the receiving enforcement systems can enforce access control decisions. The guidance emphasizes protecting authorization information from being **altered, spoofed, or compromised during transmission**, and that authorization decisions may occur in separate parts/systems.

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the authorization token contents (ac-24.01_odp.01)
- Create a canonical token schema for **signed authorisation tokens** that include at minimum:
  - **subject** (who is requesting)
  - **resource** (what is being accessed)
  - **action** (what is requested)
  - **security/privacy attributes** required to support access control decisions.
- Enforce at issuance time that required claims are present and correctly typed.

### 2) Sign the authorization token (message integrity/authenticity)
- Issue tokens as **signed authorization tokens** (e.g., **JWT/JWS** or equivalent signed token format).
- Use a signing key stored in an enterprise **KMS/HSM**.
- Include standard protections in the token:
  - **audience** restricted to the intended enforcement point(s)
  - **issuer** identifier for the authorization decision service
  - **short expiration** (and optionally not-before) to reduce replay risk
  - a unique **jti** (token identifier) if your enforcement layer supports replay detection.

### 3) Transmit using mutual TLS with certificate pinning (ac-24.01_odp.02)
- Configure the authorization decision service (issuer) and the federated API enforcement points (policy decision enforcement services) to use **mutual TLS**.
- Apply **certificate pinning** so the client/enforcement peer only accepts the expected certificate/public key(s).
- Ensure TLS configuration rejects:
  - unexpected peer identities
  - invalid/expired certificates
  - unpinned endpoints.

### 4) Enforce “verify before decision” at the enforcement point (ac-24.01_odp.03)
At each federated application/API enforcement point:
- Require successful **mTLS handshake**.
- Validate the **token signature** before using any claims.
- Validate token claims relevant to the access decision:
  - subject/resource/action/required security/privacy attributes
  - issuer/audience
  - expiration
- Only after all validations succeed, apply the allow/deny decision.
- If validation fails, deny by default and return an appropriate error (without leaking sensitive validation details).

### 5) Auditability / evidence
- Record enforcement-side evidence for each request that includes at least:
  - token verification outcome (success/failure)
  - issuer/audience match result
  - signature validation result
  - enforcement decision (allow/deny)
- Ensure logs are protected for integrity and retained per organizational logging requirements.

## WHO
- **Security Architect / IAM Architect**: define token schema, signing strategy, claim requirements, and trust boundaries.
- **Backend/API Engineering Lead**: implement token issuance, mTLS client/server configuration, certificate pinning, and enforcement-side verification.
- **Platform/DevOps Engineer**: manage KMS/HSM integration, certificate lifecycle, pin rotation process, and deployment automation.
- **Security Operations / Compliance**: validate audit evidence and review logs during control testing.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. The authorization decision service transmits authorization information to enforcement points **only** over **mutual TLS**.
2. **Certificate pinning** is implemented such that connections to non-pinned endpoints are rejected.
3. Authorization information is transmitted as **signed tokens** containing subject, resource, action, and security/privacy attributes.
4. Enforcement points **reject** requests when token signature validation fails, issuer/audience/expiration checks fail, or required claims are missing.
5. Enforcement points apply access decisions **only after** successful token verification.
6. Enforcement-side logs show token verification outcome and enforcement decision for test requests (success and failure cases).

### ac-24.2 — No User or Process Identity (Enhancement)

#### Identity-free ABAC decision rules enforced in policy engine

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Weeks
- **Confidence:** 82%

## WHAT
Implement authorization decisions so every allow/deny outcome is computed **only** from identity-free attributes defined by the organization (e.g., resource classification label, data handling category, access purpose code; and/or enclave/zone + required access mode; and/or privacy purpose + data minimisation category). Ensure the policy decision logic **does not reference, depend on, query, or embed** user or acting-process identity.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-24(2)** requires: “Enforce access control decisions based on {{ insert: param, ac-24.2_prm_1 }} that do not include the identity of the user or process acting on behalf of the user.” The organization-defined parameters for AC-24(2) specify identity-free security/privacy attributes such as:
- **ac-24.2_prm_1**: resource classification label, data handling category, access purpose code (no user/process identity)
- **ac-24.02_odp.01**: security attributes (resource classification label, system enclave/zone, required access mode)
- **ac-24.02_odp.02**: privacy attributes (privacy purpose and data minimisation category)

## HOW (specific steps/approach)
### 1) Define the identity-free decision attributes and mapping
- Create an “Identity-Free Access Attributes” catalog for the application/API resources that includes:
  - resource classification label
  - data handling category
  - access purpose code
  - (optional) system enclave/zone and required access mode
  - (optional) privacy purpose and data minimisation category
- Map each API endpoint / UI function / service operation to the required identity-free attributes (e.g., “read invoice PDF” requires classification=Confidential, purpose=Billing, access mode=read).

### 2) Enforce identity-free evaluation at the authorization enforcement point
- Choose a single enforcement point for allow/deny decisions (e.g., API gateway, service mesh authorization, or application authorization middleware) and ensure all requests pass through it.
- Configure the policy engine to evaluate only the approved identity-free attributes (from the catalog) and to **never** use subject/actor fields (e.g., userId, username, subject DN, service account identity, process id) in allow/deny conditions.
- If the system currently uses identity-aware policies, refactor them so identity is not part of the decision inputs.

### 3) Provide attributes via a trusted, integrity-protected context (without identity)
- Require callers (or an internal policy context service) to supply the identity-free attributes in a trusted context token/header (e.g., signed JWT or mTLS-authenticated service-to-service intent).
- Ensure the token/header contains only the identity-free attributes (and any non-decision metadata allowed by your organization), and that the policy engine validates integrity/signature.
- Identity may still be present for authentication and auditing, but it must not be used by the policy engine for allow/deny.

### 4) Add “no identity in decision logic” guardrails (verifiable)
- Implement a CI/CD policy-as-code check that fails builds if authorization rules reference identity fields (e.g., patterns for subject/user/process identifiers) in allow/deny logic.
- Add runtime assertions/tests in the policy engine integration tests that verify the decision result changes only when identity-free attributes change, not when identity changes.

### 5) Produce audit evidence that decisions were based on identity-free attributes
- Configure authorization decision logs to record the **exact identity-free attributes used** (classification label, data handling category, purpose code; and/or enclave/zone + access mode; and/or privacy purpose + minimisation category).
- Ensure logs clearly separate:
  - “decision basis attributes” (identity-free)
  - “authentication identity” (optional for audit) but not marked/used as decision basis.

## WHO
- **Application Security Engineer / IAM/Authorization Engineer**: implement policy engine rules, attribute catalog, and enforcement configuration.
- **Backend/API Gateway/Service Mesh Engineer**: integrate trusted attribute context and ensure all traffic routes through the enforcement point.
- **DevOps/Platform Engineer**: implement CI/CD guardrails and automated tests.
- **Security/Privacy Officer (or delegate)**: approve the identity-free attribute catalog and mapping to resources.

## Acceptance criteria (must be verifiable)
1. For all allow/deny decisions, the policy engine evaluates only the organization-defined identity-free attributes corresponding to **ac-24.2_prm_1** (and optionally **ac-24.02_odp.01** / **ac-24.02_odp.02**), and the allow/deny logic contains no references to user/process identity fields.
2. Automated CI/CD checks fail if policy code references identity fields in decision conditions.
3. Integration tests demonstrate that changing authentication identity (while keeping identity-free attributes constant) does **not** change authorization outcomes.
4. Authorization decision logs include the identity-free “decision basis attributes” values used for each decision.
5. A documented mapping exists from application resources/endpoints to required identity-free attributes, approved by security/privacy stakeholders.

### ac-25 — Reference Monitor (Control)

#### OS/kernel reference monitor for DoD Conf/Secret access mediation

- **Category:** Software
- **Priority:** Critical
- **Effort:** Months
- **Confidence:** 72%

## WHAT
Implement a dedicated, tamper-resistant reference monitor at the OS/kernel (or equivalent security boundary) that **always mediates** access to **DoD Confidential and Secret** objects and enforces the organization’s **RBAC/ABAC least-privilege access control policies** (param: `ac-25_odp`). The enforcement logic must be **small/bounded** and **verifiably correct** via automated tests and evidence.

## WHY (control requirement)
NIST SP 800-53 **AC-25 (Reference Monitor)** requires that the reference validation mechanism be:
- **Always invoked** (no bypass)
- **Tamper-proof** (adversaries cannot compromise the mechanism)
- **Small enough to be subject to analysis and testing** with **verifiable completeness**
- Enforce the access control policy over **all subjects and objects** based on the rule set.

## HOW (specific approach)
### 1) Define the mediation boundary and scope (Conf/Secret only)
- Identify all OS-mediated access paths that can reach Confidential/Secret data (e.g., labeled file paths, container volumes, database access via OS-mediated connectors, IPC endpoints, message queues, network service endpoints mapped to data labels).
- Define a **label/classification scheme** for objects (e.g., `CONF`, `SECRET`) and a **subject context** derived from enterprise identity (role/attributes/clearance).

### 2) Implement the reference monitor as the OS/kernel access mediation point
- Use an OS/kernel MAC/labeling mechanism that provides a single enforcement point for access decisions (e.g., SELinux/AppArmor-style MAC on Linux, or equivalent mandatory mediation on the chosen platform).
- Configure the system so that **all access to labeled Conf/Secret objects** is mediated by the MAC policy engine (deny-by-default for those labels).
- Ensure the policy engine evaluates **allow/deny** based on subject context (RBAC/ABAC attributes) and object label (Conf/Secret).

### 3) Make “always invoked” enforceable (no bypass)
- Remove/disable alternative access routes that would allow direct access without mediation (e.g., disable unconfined execution modes; restrict capabilities; ensure service accounts and workloads run under the mediated domain/context).
- For each application entry point (web/API/batch), ensure the workload identity and process context are set so that subsequent object access is still mediated by the reference monitor.

### 4) Make the reference monitor tamper-resistant
- Enforce privileged control over policy and enforcement configuration:
  - Restrict who can modify MAC policy artifacts and enforcement settings (least privilege; separate admin roles).
  - Protect policy artifacts with integrity controls (e.g., signed policy bundles; controlled deployment pipeline).
  - Enable runtime protections that prevent disabling enforcement (e.g., prevent switching to permissive/unconfined modes in production; enforce secure boot / integrity where available).

### 5) Keep enforcement logic small and verifiable
- Keep the **policy decision logic** narrowly scoped to mediation rules for Conf/Secret labels.
- Push complex business logic out of the reference monitor; the reference monitor should only decide access based on labels/attributes and requested operations.
- Create a **test harness** that exercises the mediation rules:
  - Unit tests for policy rules (expected allow/deny for representative subject/object/action tuples)
  - Integration tests that attempt real access operations against labeled objects
  - Negative tests that attempt bypass patterns (alternate paths, mislabeling attempts, unconfined execution attempts)

### 6) Produce audit evidence tied to the reference monitor decision
- Enable and retain audit logs that record mediation outcomes (allow/deny) including subject context, object label, and operation.
- Ensure logs are forwarded to the enterprise SIEM for auditability and correlation.

## WHO
- **System/Platform Security Engineer**: implements and hardens the OS/kernel MAC/reference monitor configuration.
- **Security Policy Engineer**: authors RBAC/ABAC-to-label mapping and the Conf/Secret mediation policy.
- **Application Owner / DevOps**: ensures workloads run in the correct mediated contexts and that all access paths to Conf/Secret data are labeled and mediated.
- **Security Assurance / Compliance**: validates test evidence and audit log completeness.

## Acceptance criteria (verifiable)
1. **Always invoked**: For Confidential/Secret labeled objects, every tested access attempt (read/write/execute/IPC/network operations as applicable) results in an allow/deny decision recorded by the reference monitor; no tested access path bypasses mediation.
2. **Tamper resistance**: In production configuration, attempts to disable enforcement, switch to permissive/unconfined modes, or modify policy artifacts without authorization fail; policy changes require controlled, privileged, integrity-protected deployment.
3. **Correctness**: For a defined test matrix of subject attributes/roles and object labels (Conf/Secret), the reference monitor produces the expected allow/deny outcomes per the organization’s RBAC/ABAC least-privilege policy.
4. **Small/bounded and testable**: The mediation policy/ruleset is bounded in scope to Conf/Secret labels and is covered by automated unit/integration tests with documented expected results.
5. **Auditability**: Audit records for mediation decisions (subject context, object label, operation, decision) are generated and forwarded to SIEM for retention per organizational requirements.
